[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU Reviews the Thrilling New Adventure from Anthony Horowitz: Oblivion\xa9 2016

Oblivion is the fifth and final instalment in the bestselling fantasy series The Power of Five and it certainly will not disappoint fans of the series. Oblivion is also a great standalone book that can be enjoyed without prior exposure to the other books in the series.Each chapter tells a different story, with each Gatekeeper facing his or her own challenges to get to Antarctica for the final battle with the Old Ones. Matt, Pedro, Scott, Jamie and Scarlett must overcome the horrors of a world turn apart by greed, destruction, terrorism and fear. The Old Ones have trapped London in a nuclear winter, levelled Hong Kong to the ground, turned Egypt into a warzone and left Brazil for dead. This grim imagining of 2022 and beyond seems all too real and with the complete collapse of the global system, of rule of law and governance, the journey to fulfil their destiny is a nightmare that often seems to have no end in sight.While the five are technically just teenagers, they each have a strength and resilience well beyond their years. Horowitz turns what should be depressing and frightening into a story that is fast-paced and action-packed. It's a dark novel but a thrilling one: highly recommended for teenage boys and girls.<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=J__3qEkWroM&amp;feature=share&amp;list=UU2Begme37cpqPTlv6dqMA6Q">Watch Anthony Horowitz talking about his writing experience for Oblivion                1/25/2013 6:04:20 AM\r                            1/25/2013 6:04:20 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Mary Sadler-Altena resenseer Brigadier en die Raaiselponie\xa9 2016

Terwyl dit lyk asof hierdie boek met die perd en sy nooi op die voorblad die bestanddele vir 'n wenresep het, gaan dit mank aan die essensi\xeble vereiste \u2013 dit kort 'n goeie storie. Vanaf die openingsbladsy blyk dit al dat <em>Brigadier en die raaiselponie</em> gaan oor die disfunksionele familie wat deesdae in baie jeugboeke die norm skyn te wees. Die veertienjarige Zahn vertrek met haar vervreemde pa en bekkige suster vir 'n week na 'n vakansie-oord, haar perd Brigadier  agterna in sy sleepstal. Sonder hom sal Zahn nie kan vakansie hou nie, hoewel dit al gou wil voorkom asof hy moet terugstaan vir 'n jong plaaslike Adonis met pragtige kuitspiere. Intriges wat op die horison skemer, val plat.  'n Swart ponie verskyn en verdwyn op onverklaarbare wyse, maar op die ou end is die enigste raaisel daarvan wat die dier hoegenaamd in die boek (en die titel) soek.  Daar is sinistere waarskuwings oor bose nagloper-wesens, wat nie verwesenlik word nie. En na 'n voorspelbare en onwaarskynlik-gehanteerde krisis sien mens aan die einde van die boek nogal hoopvol uit na 'n beloofde slim set van die suster se BF (boy friend? best friend?) om Zahn se seriously insane (sic) ma te laat afsien van haar ontydige dreigement om haar eks-man se toegangsregte tot die kinders op te skort. Ook dit stel egter teleur.Die karakters is s\xf3 stereotiep dat mens hulle amper wil afmerk soos hulle verskyn \u2013 geskeide ouers en hul onhebbelike nuwe liefdes, \u2018n rebelse suster wat hoofsaaklik dien as bladvulling, 'n verstrooide sibille wat bome liefdevolle drukkies gee en as deus ex machina verdring word deur hedendaagse tegnologie, en ander. Selfs die obligatoriese swart vriend is daar. Dit is jammer dat <strong>Marga Jonker</strong> nie die moeite gedoen het om een suiwer verhouding \u2013 die amper magiese band wat bestaan tussen ruiter en perd \u2013 uit te lig bo hierdie warboel van haat en nyd en kleinlike onverdraagsaamheid nie. Die kontras sou 'n waarde aan die boek gegee het wat nou ongelukkig ontbreek.                8/7/2014 6:39:37 AM\r                            8/7/2014 6:39:37 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Mary Sadler-Altena resenseer Eggo's in die Skimberge\xa9 2016

Na 'n asemrowende vaart op 'n vlot al met die Gansrivier af en bo-oor 'n waterval, beland Mattie en Henk in 'n digte woud waar die avontuur eers werklik begin. Hulle kom in die geheime elwe-stad Loherin, binne-in die Skimberge waar ook hekse en towenaars woon en hulle hul  menswees moet geheim hou. Dan raak hulle betrokke by die groot verdriet van koningin Ellerin en dit kan nie anders nie of hulle moet help. Mens verwonder jou aan die fyn detail wat die boek deurgaans bevat. Verbeeldingryke beskrywings van die elwe se lewenswyse, met pragtige name soos Ronan Alsund en sy suster Lyra; die unieke kleredrag; die kunstige geboue wat hulle besoek; die spel baljerne met sy snaakse re\xebls waaraan Mattie en Henk deelneem; die heks  Orelia Astral en haar dogters Iridessa en Soraja met hul vliegbesems, en veral die brousels  wat sy vir etes voorsit  soos gebraaide ruspes met knoffelsous en verbrande vetkoet, roereiers met gekerfde uie en 'n paar handevol slakke, spinnekoppe en sampioene gebraai totdat hulle deeglik verbrand is, asook  gestoofde paddavissies met suurpap en 'n modderige sous. Daar is ook die towenaar Miekelzak en sy twee aasvo\xebls Dizzero en Dwarrel en die drakyne Baf en Roef, en nog ander vreemde figure - te veel om op te noem \u2013 wat almal bydra tot die verrassende en geslaagde einde van die storie.<em>Eggo's in die Skimberge</em> is 'n fantasievlug soos min en met sy 269 bladsye 'n heerlike kluif (\u2018n beentjie om aan te knibbel) vir enige jong leser. In pragtige taal geskryf wat nie afgewater is na \u2018kinder\u2019taal nie, lees dit lekker maklik. Beslis 'n boek wat aanbeveel word.<img alt="Kobie Kr\xfcger " src="http://www.tafelberg.com/Authors/HomePage/kobie-kruger---06.jpg"/><strong>Kobie Kr\xfcger</strong> is in 1946 op \u2018n bosveldplaas in Limpopo gebore. Sy verwerf \u2018n BA en HOD aan Tukkies en werk daarna in Windhoek en Johannesburg. Hierna woon die gesin vir baie jare in die Krugerwildtuin, waar hulle drie dogters grootword. Die wildtuinlewe is ook die inspirasie vir haar boeke Boskonsert en The Wilderness Family, waarvan vertaalregte van lg. aan 13 lande verkoop word en veral in die VSA en Kanada gewild is. Sedert 2006 woon Kobie en haar man op die oewer van die Blyderivier in \u2018n wildreservaat naby die wildtuin.                 7/22/2014 8:39:05 PM\r                            7/22/2014 8:39:05 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nicky Townsend reviews Hooray for Hoppy!\xa9 2016

<img alt="rabbit with flowers" src="http://images.kalahari.net/img/2013/10/29/47905849_0_Img2.jpg"/>This is a story about Hoppy, a rabbit who is waiting for spring to come. Popping out to find it's still cold, Hoppy one day sticks his head out to find the grass is green, birds are singing, flowers have opened and the sun is shining.<em>Hooray for Hoppy!</em> is a great little story for young children as it shows how our senses help us discover the world. The illustrations are lovely, colourful and clear, assisting the story to unfold.For little children learning to speak, parents can read the story or just look at the pictures and name all there is within them.It is a simple little story but with the addition of the 5 Senses being a crucial part of this hard book, <em>Hooray for Hoppy!</em> has an extra learning and teaching angle.I did start to think this book may appeal more to girls than boys as my two year old refused it and wouldn't even let me read it, but was probably just asserting his will! Eventually we read Hoppy and then I had to read the story again!We are now smelling the flowers, listening to the birds tweeting and enjoying this beautiful little book!                7/25/2014 9:11:43 AM\r                            7/25/2014 9:11:43 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Madelein du Toit resenseer Iewers vlieg daar fairy dust\xa9 2016

Nadat Elmien en haar twee niggies hul ouers verloor het in \u2018n motorongeluk, moes  hul ouma hulle grootmaak. Die vier beland noodgedwonge in \u2018n upperclass Wendyhuis in \u2018n plakkerskamp. Elmien werk deeltyds by \u2018n videowinkel en spaar kliphard: sy wil, nee sy g\xe1\xe1n medies studeer.  Die inwoners van die kamp dink dis verwaand om so groot te droom. \u201cJy wil \u2018n dokter word? \u2018n Kind van hierdie plek wil \u2018n dokter word?\u201d Maar \u2018n gehawende mediese tas onder haar bed en gesteelde ure op YouTube op die videowinkel se rekenaar, hou haar droom lewendig.Oom Bok vat Elmien goedhartiglik werk toe, sy het sy  kar nodig om haar betyds by die videowinkel te kry, maar sy moet al hoe meer sy grillerige vatterigheid afweer. En dan is daar Mevrou, die welgestelde socialite  met \u201c...  so \u2018n hart vir die arme mense in hul nood.\u201d Tannie Madaleen is Hoewe 717 se maatskaplike werker wat maar vir \u2018mevrou\u2019 verduur want sy besef haar oop beursie en aansien het die mag om vir sommiges die kans te gun vir \u2018n beter lewe.Elmien se ouma is vuisvoos geveg, hoe sou sy weet dat op haar oudag sal die grootmaak van 3 kleinkinders in haar skoot val? Sy leef van dag tot dag en verlang na die ontvlugting van \u2018n TV en ander klein plesiertjies in die lewe.  Sy hou \u2018n blinde oog om die vrede in die Wendyhuis te bewaar en sien nie die grootword drome en frustrasies van drie tiener meisies raak nie.Dit is hard luck mense wat in plakkerskampe beland. Mense wat moet watertrap om aan die lewe te bly. <em>Iewers vlieg daar fairy dust</em> is \u2018n brutaal eerlike verhaal van so \u2018n familie wat eens \u2018n beter lewe geken het. Die uitdagings van elke dag het my soms laat kreun, hoeveel kan mens dan n\xf3g verduur? As leser wou ek met tye in die boek inklim en help. Die onverwagte draaie en kinkels ruk aan \u2018n mens. Moraliteit en oorlewing kruis knaend swaarde en straatslimheid verseker oorlewing. Dis \u2018n moderne verhaal wat na aan die been kloof. Die boek is per slot van sake opgedra aan die mense van Kleinfontein se woonwapark wat die inspirasie vir die verhaal was.Skrywer <strong>Marisa Haasbroek</strong> beweeg gemaklik rond tussen die verskillende karakters in haar verhaal.  \u201cHulle is mense soos ons\u201d, hulle deel \u2018n storie en is lewende bewyse van hoe vinnig \u2018n mens se lewe kan verander. Ek is seker lesers ken ook \u2018n \u201coom Bok\u201d, of \u2018n maatskaplike werker wat die potensiaal in mense raaksien,  of \u2018n \u201cElmien\u201d met \u2018n regte egte, gehawende dokterstas onder haar bed! Dis verreweg die beste boek wat ek hierdie jaar gelees het. (En dis 'n pragtige voorblad!) <em>Iewers vlieg daar fairy dust</em> behoort elke leser te motiveer om hul drome na te jaag en elke stukkie lewe voluit te leef,t.s.v. hulle omstandighede. <img alt="Marissa Haasbroek" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-AfQj7jfgif8/U2h-xiKQGxI/AAAAAAAAAKI/lMlJhz0sv0M/s1600/Lees-boek-2.jpg"/><strong>Marisa Haasbroek</strong> woon naby Rayton, Gauteng, saam met haar man en twee kinders. Voor die geboorte van haar kroos was sy redakteur van verskeie korporatiewe tydskrifte en het sy talle artikels en kortverhale vir bekende tydskrifte geskryf. Marisa geniet dit om haar man met \u2019n kwinkslag te laat lag, is dol op haar seun se ernstige bruin o\xeb as sy vir hom stories lees, haar dogter se hare as die son daarop val, Bosveldvure, om mense dop te hou, en oor skryf. Hierdie is haar eerste roman vir tienerlesers.                7/25/2014 8:00:40 AM\r                            7/25/2014 8:00:40 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Rebecca Jose reviews Supernova's History of Dogs.\xa9 2016

<img alt="Husky Dog" src="http://www.magazines.co.za/uploads/poster/491697001397213302.jpg"/>The volume reviewed related to the history of dogs, discussed futuristic buildings, named the heroes of South Africa and provided the reader with examples of the types of animals/insects you could find in your own back garden or nearby green area.I enjoyed reading and learning about the <em>Can Recycling Process</em>. This article was set out in a clear and concise way with pictures that were easily understood and not too busy on the eye.In <em>Andy\u2019s Atlas</em> I would have liked to have seen a bigger picture of the Canary Islands, showing the different capitals and maybe the article should have been structured to look more like a mind map with separate subheadings. In terms of the cartoon pictures, having an actual picture of the national dress would have been a lot easier to identify with. In terms of the blue font setting out information on the Islands, I found it difficult to read the blue font and for children who are just learning to read, it is really difficult to distinguish the letters as they are too close together.The idea of the <em>Calendar Almanac</em> is awesome, however, the background colours detracted from the information in the blocks. With the fact or fiction question it would have been nice to see the question on a straight line and not curved, as the two pages already had a lot of information on and the text was difficult for the eye to see the question.I enjoyed the <em>\u201cRed-list\u201d</em> environmental article and liked reading about how to make your own insecticide and will definitely be trying out the recipe shortly.The main article <em>The History of Dogs</em> was off-putting for me, the colours were dull and not something that made me want to read the article. I would have liked to have seen a timeline, with more original pictures of different types of breeds of dogs etc. It might have been nice to have a poster page with maybe the first dog/wolf which could be torn out of the magazine and used by the reader.The <em>\u201cSouth African Heroes\u201d</em> article should have had original photos of the celebrities, allowing children to associate with the hero and also enabling them to use both the information and the photos for school projects and orals etc. The information provided, however, was interesting.The heading on <em>\u201cVegetarianism\u201d</em> for me was misleading as I expected to find out about vegetarians and not 'meat free Mondays'. I think that it would have been better for children to read what the body gets from different vegetables.  It would also have been nice to see a recipe for a vegetarian dish that the reader could have made without too much difficulty, or a link to an easy vegetarian site that the reader could have viewed. Given the time of year a good example would have been a wholesome vegetarian soup.On the whole, I found the magazine too busy and difficult to concentrate on, even though it was easy reading.As a regular reader of the Kids National Geographic,the purpose of buying magazines is for the pictures and information that my children can use for school projects and/or orals, which this magazine didn't meet.                 7/28/2014 9:41:12 AM\r                            7/28/2014 9:41:12 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews Oliver Strange and the Ghosts of Madagascar\xa9 2016

<img alt="Animal eye with two children" src="http://www.nb.co.za/Books/Big//tafelberg_covers/childrens/2013/9780624056867.jpg"/><strong><em>Oliver Strange and the Ghosts of Madagascar</em></strong> is an utterly compelling and thrilling story and a fabulous follow on to <em>Oliver Strange and the Journey to the Swamps</em>.  With the first book as a delicious appetizer, the second in the series is a true feast for young readers.Woken by terrible sounds outside in the night, Oliver finds himself in a fantasy world of hammock beds, tree-houses, swinging walkways, mist and dense forest.  Zinzi, who readers have come to really love, is immediately prominent as she guides Oliver out into the wilderness of Madagascar.Together with their parents Oliver and Zinzi are helping the WWF to find animals on the CR Red List; the famous herpetologist father this time around searching for the highly venomous Golden Mantella frog, as Zinzi\u2019s Mum studies the lemurs.While beautiful, Madagascar is a wild place with dangerous people and a terrible history of slavery.  In other words, it is the perfect setting for the two young detectives.  From Ylang Ylang plantations to the centre of the forest with its ancient Rosewood trees, Oliver and Zinzi uncover illegal trading, pirates and deforestation happening on a grand level.Slightly sad that the setting had moved away from Africa, I was soon swept along in the mystery of Madagascar, <strong>Dianne Hofmeyr</strong> leading me into an adventure filled with intrigue and suspense.  In fact, so exciting is this tale that I gasped loudly more than a few times, much to my son\u2019s amusement.Again, the power of description in <strong>Hofmeyr\u2019s</strong> writing must be mentioned, where scenes are so vivid and so powerful that readers forget where they sit quietly to read, and instead exist completely within the new world woven around them.  The colours are scintillating and the visions mouthwateringly real, with words that will sweep youngsters beyond language and paper.<strong>Rob Foote\u2019s</strong> hand-drawn illustrations are gently understated and neutral, but make such an impression on young readers.  His childlike writing and drawings so real and believable, allowing children to connect on every level.This is a story that is wonderfully educational without <em>being</em> educational and I believe this is a tale that will appeal to children all around the world.Having never experienced Madagascar myself, I cannot imagine any greater adventure for children to go on - the maps, exotic names and exotic animals make this book a seriously exciting read.                 8/16/2014 1:08:25 PM\r                            8/18/2014 5:50:52 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Hannelie Dreyer resenseer Speurder Kwaaikofski - Die stinkstorie\xa9 2016

Dit kos Olga tien pakkies Carpenters om speurder Kwaaikofski  sover te kry om haar saak te ondersoek. \u2018n Dief steel soggens voor oopmaaktyd koerante voor haar kiosk, een van elk. Almal weet Kwaaikofski werk alleen, maar sonder sy vriendin Olga sou hy nooit so suksesvol gewees het nie. En sonder sy geliefkoosde Carpenters kougom kan hy nie dink nie.Dis \u2018n saak vir beginners, dink hy, en skaam hom dood.  Tot hy die walglike mengsel van stink reuke ruik \u2013 hondebolle, suur melk en vrot appels.  Skielik  word dit  een van die gevaarlikste sake wat hy nog ooit ondersoek het, \u2018n regte stinkstorie. Gewapen met \u2018n bottel melk, \u2018n pakkie Carpenters en \u2018n flitslig spring hy aan die werk.Skrywer <strong>J\xfcrgen Bancherus</strong> van di\xe9 opwindende speurreeks  hou die beginnerleser  van meet af aan ge\xefnteresseerd soos die raaisel verdiep. Kwaaikofski  klouter deur \u2018n mangat na die onderw\xeareld van die stad en beland in die doolhof van donker tonnels,  al agter die walglike reuk aan. Verdwaal natuurlik. En sy flits se batterye gee die gees. Dis  nat en daar hardloop rotte rond. \u201cJy wonder seker of ek gehuil het? Ja, ek het, al is dit nie vir \u2018n privaatspeurder lekker om dit te erken nie.\u201d Die avontuur raak al hoe gevaarliker.  \u2018n Maer, donker figuur kry hom aan die skouers beet en lei hom deur die donker gange tot by sy karige blyplek.Die intrige ontvou in eenvoudige taal wat maklik lees. <strong>Ralf Butschkow</strong>  se lewendige illustrasies en <strong>Kobus Geldenhuys</strong> se gemaklike gladde vertaling sorg vir \u2018n lekkerleesavontuur .  Seuns en dogters sal die boek enduit  geniet.<strong>J\xfcrgen Banscherus</strong>  woon saam met sy gesin in Duitsland.  Hy het sy eerste kinderboek in 1985 gepubliseer. <em>Kwaaikofski</em>-boeke is vertaal in Engels, Spaans, Deens, Thai, Chinees en elf ander tale.                 9/8/2014 8:00:09 AM\r                            9/8/2014 8:00:09 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Madelein du Toit resenseer Lotta se lewe: Konyne by dosyne\xa9 2016

Dit is Lotta se eerste dag in graad 5 en vandag mag sy na die senior deel van die skool skuif. Dit is die cooler deel van die skool en sy is erg opgewonde.Gelukkig is sy en haar beste maatjie, Chantelle in dieselfde klas ingedeel. Hulle is al maatjies van kindertuin af. Lotta het \u2018n lysie gemaak van al die redes waarom hulle so baie van mekaar hou: hulle hou van dieselfde speletjies, lag vir dieselfde goed en is altwee mal oor diere. Die Liebenbergs is \u2018n doodgewone familie: Lotta se pa is \u2018n onderwyser en haar ma is \u2018n  eksentrieke gadget mens wat knaend eienaardige goed koop. Haar Shiatsu masseerkussing en gloeiende fontein van edelstene is groot gesprekspunte by vriende en familie. Maar die hout blokfluit wat sy vir Lotta koop is nie \u2018n goeie idee nie, want sy haat die blokfluit en sou baie eerder \u2018n troeteldiertjie verkies het. Lotta probeer heeltyd van die fluit ontslae raak, maar dit het \u2018n nare manier om elke keer die pad terug te vind.Sy voel bietjie jaloers op haar beste vriendin wat 200 konyne in hul baie klein woonstel aanhou. Die lewe is onregverdig, dink Lotta, want Chantelle het so baie troeteldiere, maar sy wil nie eers vir Lotta een baba konyntjie gee nie. En as haar ma net minder gadgets wil koop sal hulle ook meer plek h\xea vir \u2018n troeteldier in hulle groot huis. Hulle het nou wel plek vir Metusalem, die skilpad, maar haar sewe-jarige tweeling boeties sit knaend die skilpad neer waar Lotta oor hom val. Haar boeties is \u201c\u2026 die ergste soort broers wat daar is\u201d en bak allerhande poetse op haar soos om haar blokfluit vol mosterd te stop. Lotta dink aan allerhande maniere om haar ouers te oorreed om \u2018n troeteldier vir haar aan te skaf en in die proses bevind sy haar in talle humoristiese sitiuasies.  Die verhaal lees soos \u2018n strokiesprent en die sketse van Daniela Kohl is nommerpas vir skrywer, <strong>Alice Panterm\xfcller</strong> se storie.  Die detail is fyn en skreeusnaaks en behoort groot genot te verskaf aan die beginner leser. Benewens allerhande kleiner lewenslessies, dra <em>Lotta se lewe: Konyne by dosyne</em> \u2018n belangrike boodskap: die aanhou van \u2018n troeteldier verg verantwoordelikheid. Die skrywer leer ook dat aanhouer wen wanneer Lotta so erg sukkel om die blokfluit te leer speel, of slim idees uitdink sodat sy 'n troeteldier kan koop.Daar is egter een aspek in die verhaal waarvan ek nie gehou het nie. Op bladsy 124 neem Lotta se maatjie, Chantelle, R50 uit haar ma se oop beursie sonder toestemming. Alhoewel Lotta noem dat so iets glad nie in hul familie toegelaat sal word nie, geniet sy tog die vrugte van hierdie ekstra geld by die kermis saam met haar beste maatjie. Die skrywer neem geen verantwoordelikheid om die diefstal, of Lotta se medepligtigheid, aan te spreek nie. Dit is nie ok om iets te neem wat nie aan jou behoort nie. Ek stel voor dat ouers en/of onderwysers hier leiding neem om Chantelle en Lotta se optrede met die leser te bespreek.<strong>Kobus Geldenhuys</strong> se Afrikaanse vertaling is puik en dra die humor in die verhaal goed oor. Die dagboek-styl van die skrywer is baie goed vir beginner lesers en alhoewel die boek 180 bladsye  het, lees dit vinnig en maklik aangesien die strokiesprentagtige illustrasies heelwat plek opneem.                9/22/2014 7:22:42 AM\r                            9/22/2014 7:25:14 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Hannelie Dreyer resenseer Gemaklik in Jou Eie Lyf - Wees die beste jy\xa9 2016

Almal wil anders wees, maar die ironie is, jy is anders gebore! Jy hoef net jouself te wees, dan is jy outomaties anders.  Wees altyd jouself, maar die beste weergawe van jouself.<strong>Leandie du Randt</strong>, bekende aktrise en professionele psigometris, skryf in gemaklike  tienertaal, dog baie volledig, oor die talle uitdagings waarmee die jong meisie te doen kry. Sy was self daar en praat uit persoonlike ervaring. In selfhelpstyl word verskeie kwessies aangespreek in drie dele wat onderskeidelik handel oor jou liggaam, jou gedagtes en jou siel. Sy skryf nie vir \u2018n onbekende leser nie, sy praat regstreeks en openhartig soos \u2018n vertroueling met die tienermeisie. Oor \u2018n tydperk van 21 dae is daar  \u2018n hoofstuk vir elke dag, gevolg deur \u2018n oefening. Die hoofstukke is nie lank nie en die oefeninge is eenvoudig en pret. Daar is by sommige oefeninge QR-kodes wat die tiener met haar foon kan skandeer om te kyk hoe die skrywer die oefeninge benader.  Dis \u2018n vars nuwe benadering  wat die skrywer se vertrouensverhouding met die leser versterk. Die boek neem mettertyd vir die leser die vorm van \u2018n dagboek aan met  die persoonlike aantekeninge wat daarin gemaak word.Die leser word gemotiveer tot \u2018n positiewe ingesteldheid. <strong>Leandie du Randt</strong> gee die tienermeisie leiding en vermaan haar, sonder om in prekerigheid en beterweterigheid te verval. Netelige kwessies word voor die voet afgestof. Sy praat reguit en openhartig  oor eetsteurnisse en puisies en seks, drank en dwelms,  oor drome, selfvertroue, verantwoordelikheid, dankbaarheid, vriendskap, om deur God se o\xeb na jouself te kyk.Die boek is \u2018n reis vir die tienermeisie na selfontdekking en selfaanvaarding, na volwassenheid.<em>\u201cWees lief vir jouself, leer jouself ken en moenie te veel van jouself vra nie.  Jy is net mens, jy gaan soms foute maak, maar staan op en probeer weer.  Moenie dink jy is beter as ander nie; wees dankbaar vir wie jy is en wat jy het; moenie iemand anders as kompetisie sien nie, want jy is self jou enigste kompetisie.  As jy eendag \u2018n prins wil h\xea, gedra jou dan soos \u2018n prinses. Geniet elke oomblik en hou op stres oor m\xf4re, God sal vir  jou sorg en glo my, jy sal daardeur kom. Alles sal op die ou einde oukei wees. As dit nie is nie, is dit nie die einde nie.\u201d</em>Aan die einde van die boek verskyn \u2018n nuttige verwysing na \u2018n hulplyn waar tieners kan aanklop. <em>Gemaklik in Jou Eie Lyf - Wees die beste jy</em> is 'n ideale geskenk, elke tienermeisie behoort hierdie boek te lees. <strong><em>Meer oor die skryfster</em></strong>:<img alt="Leandi du Randt" src="http://www.randomstruik.co.za/us3rd0cs/Author1395732832.jpg"/><strong>Leandie du Randt</strong> is \u2019n gewilde jong Afrikaanse aktrise en ook \u2019n geregistreerde psigometris. <em>Gemaklik in Jou Eie Lyf</em> het ontstaan uit haar passie om mense te help en uit haar eie ondervinding en dus het sy hierdie boek geskryf gemik daarop om jonger meisies te help om selfvertroue te ontwikkel en die beste weergawe van hulself te wees.Die boek is geskryf in gemaklike taal wat tieners sal verstaan, maar die boek bevat wysheid en lesse wat bre\xebr van toepassing kan wees. Die boek word as \u2019n drie-week-kursus aangebied met praktiese oefening aan die einde van elke dag. Die onderwerpe dek alle kwessies wat tieners sal raak, soos dwelm en alkoholmisbruik, groepsdruk, eetsteurnisse, liggaamsbeeld en dieper kwessies rondom gedagtes, innerlike selfvertroue en geestelike welstand. Die praktiese raad sal tienermeisies help om anders oor hulself te dink, om meer selfvertroue te kry en om mishandeling te hanteer en te rapporteer. Alhoewel daar \u2019n sterk geestelike boodskap is, \u2018preek\u2019 die outeur nie en maak sy dit duidelik dat die boek vir enige iemand is, wat ook al hul geloofsoortuiging.                   9/22/2014 8:12:37 AM\r                            9/22/2014 8:12:37 AM\r

Drawn by the author herself, each creature is represented as she sees them, giving children free license to explore their own talents.<em>The Field Guide to Lesser Known Spooks and Magical Beings</em> reminded me of the reason I read books. Within a space of whimsical fancy, the very real fears of strange sounds and occurrences can be uncovered in young children. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Tessa O'Connell reviews Activity Book for 3-6 years\xa9 2016

<img alt="animals on the farm" src="http://www.nb.co.za/Books/Big//hr_covers/childrens/2014/9780798166928.jpg"/><h2>Brenda Apsley's <em>6 Friends Have Fun on the Farm</em></h2>Billy the bull has a big secret that he wants to share with his six farm friends. He can\u2019t however share his secret until his friends have completed various obstacle courses. The secret is revealed at the end of the book where his farm friends compete in a tug of war competition.The farmyard friends are unnamed through the book and one animal is chosen for each event, with the young reader of the book deciding who is best suited.<em>6 Friends Have Fun on the Farm</em> is a story that encourages patience.As my children and I worked towards the end goal, we worked as a team and I enjoyed seeing my children\u2019s reactions.The story has a good moral grounding and the images are done in a child friendly manner with cute images of animals that made my daughter come back over and over again.  I could definitely relate to this book and felt the story was informative in many ways to a younger audience.I have kept secrets and have been told secrets by others. By gaining a friend\u2019s trust before sharing a secret means that you can appreciate it more when they finally tell you.My favourite part of the story was getting to choose the animals for each task and helping the children to place the magnetic pieces in their relevant positions.  However, my least favourite part was when the magnets weren't placed correctly and constantly fell out of the book and onto the floor.The font was a little small for a children's book, and I would suggest that, as there are removable parts that can either be damaged or lost, children should be over two years at least.The idea behind this hard cover activity book is novel and interactive, and I\u2019d recommend <em>6 Friends Have Fun on the Farm</em> to parents as a great tool for teaching young children.                11/9/2014 8:44:27 PM\r                            11/10/2014 4:51:38 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Parents review activity books for ages 3-5 years.\xa9 2016

<img alt="baby animals in the bush" src="http://www.nb.co.za/Books/Big//hr_covers/childrens/2014/9780798166935.jpg"/><h2>Bumper Magnet Activity Book - 6 Friends have Fun in the Wild</h2>Puku reviewer <strong>Shelley Grobler</strong> shares her experience with the latest <strong>Bumper Magnet activity books</strong> from South African Publishers <em>Human and Rousseau</em>.  Along with her five year old daughter and reviewer <strong>Nicky Townsend's</strong> two year old, the <em>6 Friends have Fun in the Wild!</em> book was explored thoroughly.The main character is Giraffe, who is wanting to start up a circus. He gets all his friends, Lion, Hippo, Zebra, Monkey, Elephant &amp; Tiger, to "audition" for him and show off their skills. They demonstrate these feats by balancing, climbing, tumbling and swimming, all the while not knowing what Giraffe is really up to. "I felt that this children's book was very innovative and Kendra (my 5 year old daughter) loved the idea that she could decide who was the best animal at climbing, tight-rope walking and diving into water as she placed the magnets onto the pages," says <strong>Grobler</strong>. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Reviews of 'Notes From a Headmaster's Desk'\xa9 2016

<img alt="Images of students and classrooms" src="http://panmacmillan.co.za/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/Notes.jpg"/><h2><em>'Notes From a Headmaster's Desk'</em> reviewed by Puku's Karen Brooks</h2>When I was first offered this book to read, I was quite excited.I have a pre-teen son who is already acting like a sixteen-year-old.  I hoped this book, written by the headmaster of a school in the group which my son attends, might offer some strategies for dealing with him.  Being a work of non-fiction, I didn\u2019t expect a page turner, but a self-help book that is entertaining at the same time.<strong>Marc Falconer</strong> is the principal of <em>King David Linksfield High School</em>, a parochial Jewish school in Johannesburg, and the flagship of six schools in the group.  He has the distinction of being one of the few non-Jewish leaders of these schools, so it follows that he has a unique view of dealing with teenage problems and from what I have heard, is a very popular leader.He mentions in the forward that he was encouraged by an eminent Johannesburg psychologist and parent at the school, <strong>Dr Dee</strong>, to write this book.So I sat down one afternoon and began.  The cover notes say \u201c<em>an entertaining and thought-provoking exploration of education, parenting, teenagers and the sometimes bizarre world of school life</em>\u201d.Reading chapter one, I was interested. By chapter five I was trying hard, and at around chapter ten I gave up.  Each chapter is between three and five pages, which is a good thing and each starts with a relevant quote, so that was encouraging.However, each anecdote was simply not backed up by a practical piece of advice at the end, which would have made such a difference.  A short summary of what <strong>Marc Falconer</strong> was trying to communicate to the reader was what I was expecting but never quite found.  I felt that the anecdotes on which each chapter is based are not written personally enough and they don\u2019t give enough detail about the people involved and the events that happened to be engaging.Given what we are used to in publications like <em>Time Magazine</em>, <em>Huffington Post</em> and <em>the Daily Maverick</em>, and the multitude of psychological \u201cfix your life\u201d shows on TV, these then became boring and repetitive.  I felt that <strong>Marc\u2019s</strong> comments, rather than feeling like advice backed up by experience, quite early on become preachy and \u201cheadmaster-like\u201d.The book is, at the end of the day, boring.  I think the editor should have been firmer and kept the book shorter.Instead of 242 pages, 150 would have sufficed... and perhaps <strong>Falconer</strong> should have told these stories to a professional writer to make them sparkle.<hr/><img alt="Bookshelf with words, ISASA Logo" src="http://www.ieducation.co.za/wp-content/uploads/isasa.gif"/><h2>Fiona de Villiers from ISASA Reviews <em>'Notes from a Headmaster's Desk'</em></h2>Upon retirement, it\u2019s become fashionable for principals (like politicians) to pen a memoir or summation of their vast and valuable experiences \u2018in the field\u2019.<strong>Marc Falconer</strong>, headmaster of <em>King David High School in Linksfield, Johannesburg, Gauteng</em>, has \u2018seized the day\u2019 and done it in his spare time. I use the phrase \u2018spare time\u2019 rather cheekily because I know that <strong>Falconer</strong>, whom I first met many years ago at <em>St Stithians College</em> at an interhouse play competition he asked me to adjudicate, will smile, exhibiting his own unique sense of humour: a healthy dollop of wicked, blended with detachment and seasoned with a mellow empathy.Perhaps these qualities are strict requirements for the first non-Jewish head of one of South Africa\u2019s largest, busiest, most successful Jewish schools. Certainly, <strong>Falconer</strong> makes it clear in his book (he calls it \u201c[a] compilation of reflections\u2026 essentially a set of short essays on various themes\u201d) that he has found them useful in leading an institution in a faith-based community that is energetically invested in almost every aspect of the school and its pupils\u2019 development.<strong>Nurturing menschen</strong>In the book\u2019s foreword, respected clinical psychologist <strong>Dorianne Cara Weill</strong> observes that <strong>Falconer</strong> is able to use his inimitable attitude in his writing. As a non-Jewish principal, he can stand back to observe just how best to \u201c<em>nurture menschen</em>\u201d and inculcate nachas (pride and joy) in his staff, pupils and parents. At the same time, he is, as <strong>Weill</strong> points out, wrestling with the following questions:\u201c<em>How do we allow our children to burn their fingers but ensure they are not third-degree burns?</em><em>How do we insist on conformity but promote individuality?</em><em>How do we assist and support but not disempower?</em><em>How do we love but not over-rescue?</em><em>To what extent are we present and available without engendering a sense of entitlement?</em><em>How do we maintain valued traditions and ensure progress by moving with the times?</em><em>When do we stand back as parents and trust the school and its teachers to know what\u2019s best?</em><em>When should the school and teachers trust as parents?</em><em>How do we as parents and teachers cope with our anxiety in order to be adult and available for our children?\u201d</em><strong>Private sustenance and public guidance</strong>These are, of course, questions that take up the time of any principal in any school, and in this respect I am grateful to <strong>Falconer</strong> for having put his thoughts down so frankly on paper. I anticipate that this book will join many a pile of trusted, dogeared volumes on principals\u2019 desks, to be dipped into for private sustenance in a quiet office after the last bell has rung, and public guidance at the assembly podium, or in the staffroom during professional teacher development time. There should, in fact, be a copy readily available for all staff at all schools to dip into and derive pleasure, comfort or edification, on a wide range of topics \u2013 for <strong>Falconer</strong> demonstrates that he is both receptive to the wisdom of others (not as common a trait as one may think in school principals) and determined to stay on top of current affairs both in his own community, across the country and around the world.<strong>Well versed</strong><strong>Falconer</strong> has collected so many insights and wonderful stories as both a parent, a teacher and a school leader that this book is divided into no less than eight subsections, each one packed with well-edited short essays. Each one of those is food for thought.For example, <strong>Falconer</strong> on technology: \u201c<em>Teachers now have the opportunity for a level of engagement, analysis\u2026 and critical thinking\u2026 it has never been easier to be part of the education process.</em>\u201d<strong>Falconer</strong> on providing a moral compass: \u201c<em>Our school is not modelled on the \u2018real world\u2019. On the contrary, it is designed to be an artificial and protective hothouse\u2026 it is our intention to give pupils the space to confront safely many of the challenges they are going to have to face outside.</em>\u201dAnd <strong>Falconer</strong> on educating for independence: \u201c<em>Every time new parents come into my office\u2026 one issue in particular keeps being raised: will our children be adequately prepared to take on the challenges of the world they will encounter when they leave school?</em>\u201d<strong>Such chutzpah!</strong>One of <strong>Falconer\u2019s</strong> most priceless anecdotes comes right at the start of this wonderful resource, and it seems right to end this review with it:\u201c<em>At my very first staff meeting [at King David] I was proud of my efforts at demonstrating linguistic and cultural adaptability. Somewhat smugly, I loudly and publicly requested a young and rather buxom member of staff, who had chosen this moment to spring-clean her handbag, to put away her tzitchas (breasts) instead of her tzatchas (trinkets). It\u2019s not a mistake that will be easily forgotten.</em>\u201d                11/10/2014 1:45:24 PM\r                            11/10/2014 1:45:24 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku's Nonkululeko Zondo Reviews Jealous in Jozi\xa9 2016

<em>Jealous in Jozi</em> picks up where <em>Broken Promises</em> left off. Ntombi is in Johannesburg for the \u2018South African Teen Voice\u2019 finals. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku Reviews the Haunting New YA Drama, Capture the Light\xa9 2016

Lavender Thyme is difficult to like. Her fundamentalist views make her an obvious target at school and, while you can see her point, it is often baffling why she has to so vocally and frequently judge her peers, knowing the harsh backlash that will follow. Part of her dogmatic attitude has been learned from her stern, artist mother and part of it is a rebellion in its own way against modern society and the way her classmates lead their lives. When the notes start arriving on her desk at school, anyone who has ever been at high school can understand why. Like Lavender, readers start to form their own suspicions about who is playing this childish but hurtful game with her. Meanwhile, back at home, Lavender and her mother face sharp criticism from their Christian neighbours over the massive \u2018heathen\u2019 Shrine they have built to honour nature and the natural world.The night attack changes everything. Up to then Lavender is just naive and somewhat irritating; living her mother\u2019s beliefs and not really forming her own. After the events of that evening, Lavender is forced to grow, to trust herself against all others and to deal with far harsher consequences of her fundamentalism than anyone expected. Her small Western Cape town is shocked, her core group of friends and family left in disbelief and Lavender herself forgets the condemnation and slurs of the past and focusses on just trying to put her life back together again.<em>Capture the Light</em> is a book about life\u2019s darkest moments, the fragile, imperfect and ugly nature of even those we thought we knew best, and how, sometimes, even the truth can\u2019t set you free. It\u2019s slow in the start and does not have the same pace and action of many YA books in the market right now. It doesn't have the same 'like-ability' as some of this publisher's other YA releases of 2012 either. But it does delicately paint a rich portrait of a few weeks in a confused and frightened girl\u2019s life beautifully. Give it time to work its way into your heart: its twists and turns will keep you guessing but, more than that, leave you with haunting moral questions and some dissatisfaction when the truth is finally revealed. Contains some mature content but is suitable for teens 15 years and up.                3/5/2013 9:20:35 AM\r                            3/5/2013 9:20:35 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews 'The Mark' by Edyth Bulbring\xa9 2016

<img alt="Girl in barren city with tattoo number on her back" src="http://www.nb.co.za/Books/Big//hr_covers/childrens/2014/9780624068815.jpg"/><em>Reviewed by Puku's Nikki McDiarmid</em><h2>Dystopian fiction that South African readers have been desperate for</h2>Instantly gripping, <strong>The Mark\u2019s</strong> first chapter has readers scrambling for some semblance of recognition in a city where nothing is the same.It is the year 264 PC.Thrust immediately into a scene of chaos, readers are confronted by invisible monsters, Market Nags, Locusts and sun worshippers, watching as thieves from the Slums filch the treasures left behind. Ettie is nearly caught, on purpose, so that Kitty can get away safely; Kitty, her attractive roommate, whose survival is more important than her own.Handled by a cruel man, Ettie and Kitty must survive in Slum City until they reach their coming of age, where they will then be assigned to a trade, bound to duties that will make them slaves to the system, controlled always by the Machine.The mark on Ettie\u2019s back burns after numerous attempts to remove it.  But this pain will keep her alive.Other than Kitty, Ettie loves only books, their paper pages ancient remnants of a world long past.  So when Nicolas shows his interest, even though forbidden to her, Ettie has no choice, but to follow her heart and change the future of Mangeria.Hiding where there were no distractions, I dived eagerly into <strong>The Mark</strong>, waiting for it to come alive.  I was not disappointed.  The mysteries of this new world lead the reader on a fast-paced adventure that is most compelling.It is a dystopian story so hauntingly South African that I wrapped it around me like a shroud.  Reminded of the isolated prawns in \u2018<em>District 9</em>\u2019 and the children in \u2018<em>The Thief Lord</em>\u2019 by <strong>Cornelia Funke</strong>, <strong>Edyth Bulbring\u2019s</strong> orphans are as memorable.Existing in a world bereft of innocence, where beauty is a fragile commodity and stands out noticeably against its surroundings, the treasures of humanity must be suppressed and carefully secreted away to places where none can find them.As I read, I find myself wanting more, desperate for further pages of this richly-described horrendous place, filled with evil and filth and soft over-ripe bananas.In the middle of the story <strong>The Mark</strong> is split in two halves, demarcating one life from another and jarring the process of reading. My thoughts were displaced and I was left to begin over.  This stopped the flow of the story and in coming up for air, I found myself feeling curiously abandoned.And yet, despite this disjointedness, <strong>Bulbring</strong> manages to pull the reader back again and whip them through the pages so fast that <strong>The Mark</strong> pretty much guarantees an exciting second read.<strong>The Mark</strong>, perhaps not completely resolved, is a first that will pave the way for future tales in this genre, leaving readers in no doubt that when a South African story is richer than most of its competitors, then local storytellers have finally come home to roost.This is the South African fiction we have all been waiting for.                11/28/2014 7:22:34 AM\r                            11/28/2014 10:31:50 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku Reviews Youth Chick-Lit Novel The Spy Who Loved Him\xa9 2016

South African women of a certain age all seem to have in common a secret and embarrassing love for Mills &amp; Boon books. As teenagers, they all seemed to love the stories of the young, shy girl and the slightly older, richer and taller gentleman who steals her heart. Woman of this generation don\u2019t seem to have something similar \u2013 unless you count Twilight \u2013 but Nollybooks is trying to change that. Their series of \u2018bookazines\u2019 are easy-to-read, chic-lit for teens and young women.This week Puku tackled <em>The Spy Who Loved Him</em>, a fun little book about a undercover journalist who stumbles into a situation that her journalism degree definitely did not prepare her for. Like all books of this genre, it\u2019s fairly predictable but it is fun and young women in the city can relate to already facing choices of love versus career or integrity versus loyalty. Thuli is just the right mix of ambitious and uncertain, and it was refreshing to read a main female character who wasn\u2019t weepy and weak to the point of disbelief.The twist in this tale and that we also get a glimpse of what the hero of the story, millionaire businessman Luasi Nkhosi, is thinking and feeling about his new domestic worker. The heroine also has a great supporting cast of strong, funny women who sound like they could be your mom, baby sister or best friends. Everything down to the saving for the next Woolworths sales rings true in Thuli\u2019s life and while teens will probably enjoy the book, it\u2019s also probable only those 16 and up will actually be able to relate.<em>The Spy Who Loved Him</em> was more young Hollywood than Mills &amp; Boon, and ultra-lite. That said, it was more enjoyable than anything on TV or most chick-lit for young women. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Sindiwe Magona's 'Greedy Man, Kind Rock'\xa9 2016

[<h2>South African Folk Tales in English</h2><img alt="Man against the wind" src="http://www.waterstones.com/wat/images/nbd/m/978148/560/9781485600725.jpg"/>Written by South African storyteller, <strong>Sindiwe Magona</strong>, \u201c<em>Greedy Man, Kind Rock</em>\u201d is a folk tale taking place in a severe drought, that leaves Hlohlesakhe, his wife Nobuhle and their young family, desperate and starving.Here the land is \u201c<em>dry and hard as steel</em>\u201d, and the soil is \u201c<em>cracked into clods.  Then the clods broke into tiny, tiny pieces</em>\u201d. The family\u2019s despair is painfully evident and <strong>Sindiwe Magona\u2019s</strong> words sweep young readers up into the dusty winds that envelope the story.Eventually Hlohlesakhe embarks on a long journey in search of food, finding a place with a rock that is filled with wisdom and magic. But the man is greedy and Hlohlesakhe shares none of it.Intrigued by this unusual story, my son loved that local folklore is so different to the stories he is used to reading and hearing.\u201c<em>This is a really cool story, but that man was so greedy!</em>\u201d He told me and was suitably shocked by the gluttonous Hlohlesakhe. Together we laughed at the punishment the man got in return for not sharing.Discussion flowed easily after finishing the book, opening the subjects of hunger and need, and continuing on to conversations about sharing food and thinking of others.This tale has a delightful story line, but the pages drag a little for today\u2019s generation, leaving readers bored and giving up too easily.  The wording is not easy and will either force young readers to learn, or turn them away.\u201cGreedy Man, Kind Rock\u201d is a good quality publication with great illustrations that I could well imagine children also colouring in as an interactive exercise.<em>Nikki McDiarmid</em>                12/3/2014 9:41:30 AM\r                            12/4/2014 7:12:03 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews The strange and beautiful sorrows of Ava Lavender\xa9 2016

<img alt="Golden feather on blue" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/books/1397110326l/18166936.jpg"/><h2>The Strange and Beautiful Sorrows of Ava Lavender</h2><em>The Strange and Beautiful Sorrows of Ava Lavender</em> is an artistic and musical tale told by a true storyteller.In the opening prologue, Ava is introduced from birth as the \u2018<em>myth incarnate</em>\u2019, a girl born with wings.  Birds behave strangely in surrounding areas as she arrives and the twin who follows behind her seems overwhelmed by the power Ava brings.In an attempt to understand why she is the way she is, Ava returns first to her childhood and then delves further back into her family lineage.  Immediately, the reader begins a journey that is both strange and wildly different to any other.Amusing, lighthearted and sweet, <strong>Leslye Walton</strong> explores the innocence of youth and the boundless possibilities that accompany it, using metaphors and similes to build a wonderfully rich story. However, in order to grow, the young Ava must reach a point where she abandons innocence via the path of pain and heartbreak.  The pages of this book get darker and darker as the story goes on.<strong>Walton\u2019s</strong> artistic vision sweeps through the legend of Ava Lavender, painting the characters and the scenery until the tale resembles a theatrical performance of carnival creatures.  Vibrant musical tones accompany the intricate weaving of characters, changing tempo often as the pace slows down, then rushes forward with Ava, like a moth driven towards the flames.  The momentum beats erratically against the inner workings of the psyche, leaving readers no choice, but to dance.The power of <strong>Walton's</strong> narrative, lies in the diversity of her characters, each a study in human nature blending the impossible with real life personalities. Completely different to each other, all are bizarre and whimsical. As their many quirks and tweaks fill the pages in a maelstrom of energy, I am reminded of the surrealist painters, <strong>Joan Miro's</strong> <em>Harlequin's Carnival</em> and <strong>Dali's</strong> dream scapes.I am left in no doubt that <strong>Leslye Walton</strong> is convincing readers that they only <em>think</em>  they are normal. <strong>Be warned</strong> though, as this is not a tale for sensitive readers and should be assessed for younger teens.  The dark parts are really dark and the strange, very strange.This is a finely written novel for adults and teenagers who like contemporary fiction.  A superb holiday read.<em>Nikki McDiarmid10/12/2014</em>                 12/10/2014 9:32:25 AM\r                            12/10/2014 10:19:54 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Sindiwe Magona's 'Stronger than Lion'\xa9 2016

<img alt="Lion with mouse on his head" src="http://d1w7fb2mkkr3kw.cloudfront.net/assets/images/book/large/9781/4856/9781485600701.jpg"/><h2>Who can be stronger than Lion?</h2>All young boys say they are 'strong like a lion' and this African folktale is one that boys will certainly connect with.Lion may be strong, but in this story he is also greedy, selfish and filled with arrogant pride.  The African bush animals have called a meeting to discuss Lions rampant feeding.  The carnivore is wiping out their species and must be stopped.  Lion, however, believes he has the right to do as he wishes, for he is the most important animal in the kingdom. When it is the lowly mouse who reports back to him, Lion is surprised. The mouse has news that will question his strength as a Lion, but soon enough, the king of the jungle learns that \u2018pride comes before a fall\u2019.Personally, I find folktales about animals immensely enjoyable, their timelessness ensuring that even as adults, the basic morals are relevant to human nature.  Folktales cross boundaries, cultural differences and restrictions, allowing children to explore various interpretations and gain diverse understanding.This story is great fun.  Thoroughly involved from the beginning, my young reader giggled and laughed loudly, finding Lion most amusing!Some interesting words were discovered, such as \u2018<em>massacre</em>\u2019 and \u2018<em>pride</em>\u2019 which needed explaining, as well as the phrasing of \u2018<em>suggestions and rejections</em>\u2019 which encouraged slower reading and the challenge of building up sounds.Worrying that the \u2018<em>slain</em>\u2019 Lion was a little sad for an ending, I was quickly assured that Lion didn\u2019t die and that the animals let him out of the cave to eat once he had learnt his lesson.Further discussion could also center around the mocking of others, especially in grades where verbal bullying is rife:\u201c<em>There were screeches and giggles; hiccups and snorts; guffaws, heckles and sneering, and a lot of other noises \u2013 all of them cruel ways of laughing at someone</em>.\u201dSouth African children are fully aware that lions feast upon large animals and go for days before they hunt again. <strong>Sindiwe Magona\u2019s</strong> story broadens the imagination and possibilities that these eating habits are due to the influence of one very small mouse...<em>Stronger than Lion</em> is the perfect gift for boys, for children who love discussions as well as for tourists and African children who live overseas.                12/12/2014 8:47:45 AM\r                            12/12/2014 10:27:23 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku Reviews 'Fangirl' by Rainbow Rowell\xa9 2016

<img alt="Girl with laptop, boy looking on" src="http://images.kalahari.net/img/2013/09/05/47741931_0_Img2.jpg"/><h2>13yr old Shinead Promitz discovers a story that will appeal to most teenagers.</h2><em>Fangirl</em> is a book about twin girls who go to college for the first time.Cath and Wren have to learn to be apart and face going through many hard situations such as popularity hierarchy and betrayal, but they are always there for each other in the end.The main characters are Cath, Levi, Wren, Art, Nick and Reagan, students trying to get through college with good grades and without any problems.The bond the characters had in the book reminds readers of the importance of good relationships, the ones you have always wanted to have, and the story is relaxing and happy at the same time. I enjoyed the different personalities of every character and the way they resolved their issues. When they were not able to handle the silence anymore and they came out into the open, good friendships were made.Cath is the main character.  She is sweet and kind, but nobody knows this because she is so quiet.  I could relate to Cath a lot because I am also a very shy person and just want to be alone sometimes.<strong>I enjoyed this book a lot.</strong>The story affected me in a positive way because it taught me some of the problems a person may have as a student at college so now I should know what to do if I was ever at a party that I didn\u2019t want to be at\u2026. (But I don\u2019t want to reveal too much.)I am still in High School but I could relate to some problems from this point of view, especially the popularity hierarchy.  Who knew that occurred everywhere in the world?Finding out who Cath falls for was my favourite part and trust me, it was a nice surprise to see who was waiting for her.There was not much I did not like, except for when I finished reading an intense chapter, wanted to know what happens next, so I wanted to get to the next chapter as soon as possible, but still had to read a Simon Snow chapter. (This is a book Cath likes to read.) I think the pages with Simon Snow weren\u2019t that bad in themselves, they were just really irritating, and I felt like I had to read them before carrying on.<strong>I would definitely recommend this book.</strong>For any person who likes a good book to curl up with and never let go of, <em>Fangirl</em> is perfect. Young adults in high school who love stories about real life problems will also connect with this book.<em>Fangirl</em> is entertaining to read and covers some important issues.<em>By Shinead Promitz</em><hr/><img alt="Boy, girl and lovers in a bubble" src="http://novelsounds.net/wp-content/uploads/2013/08/fangirl-by-rainbow-rowell.jpg"/><h2>'<em>Fangirl disappoints</em>' Review 2</h2>Twins, Cath and Wren, have arrived at college, but Wren has dumped her twin as she's keen to try living an independent life away from her sibling.  The gregarious and outgoing Wren appears initially to be able to cope with the challenges of college, but later the wheels fall off as she gets caught up in a world of partying and drinking.The second sister and main character, Cath, is far more insular and a hermit writer of fan-fiction who never leaves her room. She writes a \u2018fic\u2019 (or fanfiction) about the popular magician <em>Simon Snow</em>, using characters already created by another author, reminding young writers most subtly about plagiarism and theft.Cath's <em>Simon Snow</em> excerpts complete every chapter and are quite disruptive to the reading flow.  These are rather   irrelevant to the novel and serve as a confirmation of Cath's fan-fiction, which isn't really necessary. I felt they also undermined the value of gay relationships, appearing more as an afterthought to the plot line in an attempt to add some depth to a very one dimensional story.This heroine is neither strong nor bold.  She is afraid of strange places and finds it difficult to navigate the college campus, never leaving her room and surviving off snack bars.This is indeed a very real affliction, but I had to wonder what the average South African child would think, as they fight every step of the way to be accepted into local Universities and Colleges.  Would they appreciate a leading character who shies away from the greatest opportunity education has to offer?Sadly, I found <em>Fangirl</em> rather clich\xe9d and presumptuous.While the story is sweet and pleasant, with occasions where I did laugh out loud, there is nothing really surprising and the real issues are rather blandly portrayed.Selling alongside truly powerful South African stories, I think most African Young Adult readers will get a hundred pages in and still be looking for something to sink their teeth into. <em>Nikki McDiarmid</em>                12/15/2014 1:58:29 PM\r                            12/17/2014 9:30:59 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Reader Review of children's picture book, 'Please, Mr Panda'\xa9 2016

[<h2>Puku's Cheryl Robertson reviews 'Please Mr Panda' by Steve Anthony</h2><img alt="Book Cover: Panda Bear with doughnuts" src="http://halifax.momstown.ca/sites/halifax.momstown.ca/files/styles/crop_feature/public/mrpanda.jpg?itok=tSyVVl_S"/><strong>Please, Mr Panda</strong> is a delightful story about a panda bear who offers doughnuts to other animals, but when they say that they will have one or more, he refuses. It is only at the end of the story that we realise why Panda Bear denies them doughnuts, ignoring all of the animals, except one.This cleverly written story teaches children the fundamental manners of 'please' and 'thank you' in a few short sentences.Young readers will find it easy to identify with the characters in the way that they answer the question \u2018<em>Would you like a doughnut</em>?\u2019  Some of the animals are rude and others are greedy.The pictures are colourful and the expressions of the animals are well drawn.This story was read to my two and a half year old grandson who, when asked why he thought that the panda only gave doughnuts to one of the animals, he replied "Because he was the only one who said 'please' and 'thank you'."I would definitely recommend this book for 2 \u2013 3 year old toddlers.<hr/><img alt="Illustration: Panda on the boat looks at Whale" src="https://encrypted-tbn2.gstatic.com/images?q=tbn:ANd9GcS1nMpIoRL5JF-XqndbYhO3l8f_Qx8fHwLLcL7QODOjwlLpEGRfAQ"/><img alt="Logo: Publisher's Weekly" src="http://www.publishersweekly.com/images/logo-consumer.jpg"/><h2>Steve Antony, Author with Publisher's Weekly, reviews "Please Mr Panda"</h2>Mr. Panda, though he\u2019s a picture of tubby fuzziness, defies the friendly panda stereotype (for one, he has a permanent glower). He offers a box of iced doughnuts to a small penguin, who says, \u201cGive me the pink one.\u201d \u201cNo, you cannot have a doughnut,\u201d growls the panda, turning his back on the shocked penguin and lumbering away. \u201cI have changed my mind.\u201d He offends a series of animals in similar fashion until a lemur pokes its head in. \u201cMay I have a doughnut... PLEASE, Mr. Panda?\u201d While Mr. Panda doesn\u2019t warm up, the \u201cplease\u201d nets the lemur the entire box of doughnuts. Smart design decisions by Antony (Betty Goes Bananas) distinguish his visual storytelling. The warm gray backdrop and parade of black and white animals (a skunk, an ostrich, an orca) make the candy-colored doughnuts look all the more tantalizing. Novel perspectives, including an upside-down scene when the lemur makes its appearance, provide freshness, too.Children who remember to say \u201cPlease\u201d will know right away what\u2019s up, and those who don\u2019t will not mind the reminder. Ages 3\u20135.                4/20/2015 9:34:08 AM\r                            4/23/2015 6:50:01 AM\r

The alphabet is marked along the edge of the pages and is also highlighted in blue, making them instantly noticeable to visual learners.We liked that each word is immediately followed by it's part of speech, as this made looking up words for homework far quicker.  Children turn more frequently to the internet for fast results, but the <strong>Pharos dictionary</strong> allowed my eleven year old to access words easily and with speed.The sentences provided with each word are local in content and fitting with what children already see and hear.  For example with the word '<strong>America</strong>', the sentence reads "<em>Charlize dreams of going to <strong>America</strong> to become a Hollywood star</em>."At the back of the book there is a grammar supplement dedicated to the parts of speech, focusing on punctuation, irregular verbs and further words that are easily confused. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">City Girl en die swart hings\xa9 2016

<em>City Girl en die swart hings</em> deur <strong>Marga Jonker</strong> het my veral be\xefndruk. Die karakters is modern tieners wat gemaklik tussen stadslewe en die ongerepte natuur beweeg. Toegerus met die jongste tegnologie, geniet hulle ten volle wat die lewe hulle aanbied. Die liefde vir perde en die passie vir perdry is ook \u2018n sterk element in die verhaal, sonder dat dit die verhaal oorheers. Die goed gebalanseerde verhaal oor die doen en late van \u2018n groepie ruiters tydens hul skoolvakansie, sal aanklank vind by \u2018n wye tiener leserskring.  Die boek is in \u2018n groter lettertipe gedruk, wat die leeservaring vir die jonger leser vergemaklik.<img alt="Marga Jonker" src="http://www.nb.co.za/Authors/HomePage/marga-jonker.jpg"/><strong>Marga Jonker</strong> het grootgeword op \u2018n plaas tussen Paternoster en Stompneusbaai.  Na skool verwerf sy \u2018n onderwysdiploma aan die Wellington Onderwyserskollege, \u2018n BA graad met Xhosa en Geskiedenis aan die Universiteit van Stellenbosch, en \u2018n Verdere Diploma in Vroe\xeb Kinderontwikkeling aan die Randse Afrikaanse Universiteit verwerf.<strong>Marga</strong> is tans die Xhosa derdetaal-onderwyseres aan die Voorbereidingskool Durbanville waar sy graad 2- en 3-kinders bekendstel aan Xhosa as derde taal.  Sy skryf en ontwikkel die kurrikulum hiervoor en maak rympies en stories om by haar materiaal te pas. Sy glo veeltaligheid lei tot multi-kulturele ontwikkeling. Sy wou van kleins af graag skryf en het gedigte in haar dagboeke geskryf.  Sy het egter eers in haar veertigerjare dapper genoeg gevoel om van haar werk in Afrikaans aan uitgewers voor te l\xea.\u2019n Prenteboek, <em>Wat is jy Kartoffel?</em>, (Lapa Uitgewers, 2010) deur die skrywer en die illustreerder <strong>Alzette Prins</strong> is deur die Namibiese Kinderboekforum bekroon.                 4/13/2015 12:16:35 PM\r                            4/13/2015 12:16:35 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Young Adult reader review\xa9 2016

[<h2>11 year old, Zo\xeb Da Silva, reviews 'Hearing Helen' by Carolyn Morton</h2><img alt="Cover: Girl looking out over the ocean " src="http://www.nb.co.za/Books/Big//hr_covers/childrens/2013/9780798164368.jpg"/>I have read many books, ranging from fiction to fact, but this book, <strong>Hearing Helen</strong>, has got to be in my top ten books ever!Helen is a normal teenager, who also has Monday mornings where everything goes wrong.  Helen has an undiscovered talent for the piano, but even she doesn't know it's there, because her brother is constantly the centre of attention. Her school life isn't much better than her home life, because the boy she has a crush on, sees her only as his punching bag. He is also in love with someone else - June, the most sickly, gorgeous girl in school.However, once all three of them are assigned to be partners for a school project, Helen finally realizes that June is the best friend she could ever ask for and her crush, Kean, is not who she thinks he is. When something terrible happens to June, it really tests Helen's loyalty and her friendship.For me the definition of a good book is to make the reader <em>believe</em> the story, as well as transport them into it.<strong>Hearing Helen</strong> is an extraordinary book that didn\u2019t just transport me into the pages, but it took over my soul, so that when Helen felt weak at the knees, I had to sit down, and, when I read what happens to June, I couldn\u2019t help myself sobbing like a baby! I felt like June was <em>my</em> best friend and the way in which Helen helped hermade me cry with happiness and joy, because this is what friends are supposed to do.There were no parts of this story that were better than others, just that I loved the whole book. Even the cover spoke to me about Helen\u2019s personality.  The picture is simple and filled with longing, and Helen is like the ocean, filled with mystery.I honestly couldn\u2019t relate to Helen, but I didn\u2019t really need to because the author <em>Carolyn Morton</em> just makes you feel like you are part of the story and not just a reader. I found it most interesting that even though Helen is only fifteen, she has as many problems as her parents.I would most definitely recommend this book to other readers.  To all my friends, family and really, to anyone who loves a good heartfelt story.  This one was written in my country \u2013 South Africa!                4/20/2015 8:01:05 AM\r                            4/20/2015 8:46:48 AM\r

<img alt="Book Cover: Maisy and her friend in swimming pool" src="http://media3.takealot.com/covers_tsins/39264755/edc7131c94a1611f8b935c3357329dbd-zoom.jpg?1427928533"/>**<blockquote><strong>Review by Nicky Townsend</strong></blockquote>**<strong><em>Maisy Learns to Swim</em></strong> is about Maisy the mouse and her friends, Tallulah and Eddie, going to a swimming class.Together, the parent and young reader follow <strong>Maisy</strong> as she gets her swimming things together, changes for the pool and then goes through her lesson.  The story takes <strong>Maisy</strong> to the end of this experience, where she showers and eats a snack. The animal friends learn to float on their backs and blow bubbles until <strong>Maisy</strong> thinks swimming is more fun than bathing!My son, who is almost 3, enjoyed this book as he has been to swimming lessons from a young age, and therefore identified with this adventure. On the first page of any new book that catches his attention, he always points to the items on the page, in this case what Maisy is taking with her to swimming - towel, goggles, costume etc.I think <strong><em>Maisy Learns to Swim</em></strong> will also help those new to swimming, as the story sets up each of the processes involved and helps youngsters to see swimming as fun. The <strong>Maisy</strong> characters are straightforward and honest, as well as being well known, making them easy for children to recognise. The illustrations are clean and bold. <strong>The writing is simple and a good starting point for children learning to read.</strong> We have read this story many times and each time my son asks why we don\u2019t have the other books in the set that are displayed on the back cover!As he got to know the characters, he took more of an interactive role, making comments about Eddie splashing and <strong>Maisy</strong> enjoying the swimming. (Unfortunately, I do not know some of the characters, so I am unable to tell him <em>all</em> of the animal's names.)<strong>I would recommend this book for all young children, from a year and up.</strong><strong>To find out more about Maisy and her friends, visit the official website:</strong> http://www.maisyfun.com/forchildren/<strong>To buy the book:</strong> http://www.takealot.com/maisy-learns-to-swim/PLID36536694<img alt="Illustration: Maisy and friends in the swimming pool" src="http://www.wendybook.com/image/item/img76/76003_4.jpg"/><img alt="Logo: Walker Books" src="http://www.maisyfun.com/images/Maisy_Walker_Books_logo.gif"/><hr/><strong>Review by Nikki McDiarmid:</strong>I remember the <strong>Maisy</strong> books from my own youth and it was a melancholy experience holding one in my hands again.I was delighted to find their appeal timeless, watching as my eleven-year-old couldn't resist choosing it from the pile and paging through the story.<em>Who said picture books were only for littlies?</em>"                  5/18/2015 12:13:52 PM\r                            5/18/2015 1:29:50 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews Young Adult Fiction, "Frozen".\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book cover: Dragon and ice, Frozen" src="http://www.burnbright.com.au/wp-content/uploads/de-la-cruz-frozen.jpg"/>Natasha Kestal is a blackjack dealer and card shark in the casinos of Phoenix, Arizona, a city much changed by a world catastrophe.Now in an ice age, the environment is filled with giant junk yards, high tech military operations, zombies, polar bears and mythical creatures. It is here that organic items fetch millions and where gangs rule.Survival is based on killing those who are different, so Nat must hide who she really is, keeping it secret that she is controlled by a monster.Her journey is to find the \u2018Blue\u2019, a mythical paradise that no-one has seen. However, this mission means leaving the city and Nat needs a guide to do that. The handsome Wes is the only person prepared to help and yet he has a group of boys who are dangerous and violent, and Nat is unsure of how much faith she should put in them.Lead by the voice inside her head, Nat knows that this voyage will be her only way \u201chome\u201d.<strong><em>Frozen</em> is a dystopian love story perfect for young teens, focusing on the message that it\u2019s cool to be different.</strong>The chapter quotes are both fashionable and current, and the anticipation built up from the card games makes for a wonderful tension builder.<strong><em>Frozen</em></strong> is however, a slow starter. Vague suggestions imply that the character has extra powers, the dragon hinted at, but the build-up towards discovering them is painstakingly slow and rather disappointing.  There is a great deal of activity, and yet the story itself is hard to follow. Ten chapters in, the reader still has no clarity on what is really happening.The plot is a little one-dimensional for older readers, but for the scenery alone, <strong><em>Frozen</em></strong> is worth the read.<br/>Eventually the puzzle pieces fall into place and the excitement heats up, taking readers into a new world of imagery where anything can happen.The characters, specifically unique, play off against a backdrop of such diversity that the moral <strong><em>Frozen</em></strong> focuses on, is enhanced -  the more unusual a person is, the more power they have.  A story line most apt for this time in South Africa\u2019s history.<strong><em>Frozen</em></strong> is an enjoyable tale, suitable for those looking for an introduction to dystopian novels, and readers who have enjoyed books like Veronica Roth\u2019s <em>Divergent</em>.<img alt="Image: Frozen quote" src="http://38.media.tumblr.com/10ea21d6dc8dea65200a7afa4679de3c/tumblr_mor795SdJi1r0yglfo1_1280.gif"/>                5/22/2015 9:11:27 AM\r                            5/23/2015 7:38:41 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews Pig is a Blue Baboon\u2019s Bottom.\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book cover: Mum with Pig with a mask on his face" src="http://ecx.images-amazon.com/images/I/51ttgUxowhL._SY344_BO1,204,203,200_.jpg"/><strong>A delightful book that all young boys will enjoy.</strong>As a reviewer I see so many books, but few have had me reacting quite like <em>Pig is a Blue Baboon\u2019s Bottom</em> did.Set Two of the <strong>Pig series</strong> is published by <a href="http://www.ransom.co.uk/Product%20Pages/PIG/PIGReaders.html#">Ransome Publishing, a specialist publisher for reluctant and struggling readers. The <strong>Pig reading books</strong> all feature Peter Ian Green - although everybody calls him Pig, even his teachers. As the publisher states, "<strong>The 'Pig' reading series</strong> offers friendly, fast-paced and extremely funny stories in first-person diary format, for readers who want a great story in a quick read."<strong>There is only one word to describe this book - Wonderful!</strong><em>Pig is a Blue Baboon\u2019s Bottom</em> is the amusing tale of a boy who lives with his Mum, his much older sister Suki and his 'vampire' baby brother.  He lives in a house that sounds like a whirlwind of chaos, to which Pig seems to respond calmly, take it all in his stride, but with some hilarious comments and attitudes.  Pig is a character kids will instantly recognise and respond to, loving him because he embodies normality.  However, when Pig's school project goes wrong he nearly looses his friendship with Raj and young readers will question their own responses.Like a good comic, the Pig series are set out in the same style as <em>The Diary Of a Wimpy Kid</em> books, complete with underlined headings and simple but delightful illustrations.  The story itself is clean and honest and pure, making it such a great read for youngsters.My eleven year old thoroughly enjoyed this book, completed it in half an hour. (A good sign for boys who feel reading takes up too much of their time.)  He was still laughing when he handed it back to me, his only words being "It's so cool!" Intrigued, I too read <em>Pig is a Blue Baboon\u2019s Bottom</em> and found myself chortling out loud, smiling and reading avidly right to the very end.  This book is perfect for getting kids back into the habit of reading and having seen the responses from all ages, I can safely say that it is a guaranteed great read.Like a good comic <em>Pig is a Blue Baboon\u2019s Bottom</em> is ideal for reluctant readers aged 7 to 12 with a reading age of 8 - 9 years.<img alt="Logo: Juta" src="http://www.skycastle.co.za/wp-content/uploads/logo-juta.jpg"/><hr/><strong>About the Author</strong><em>Barbara Catchpole taught for over forty years before becoming a full time writer. Her interest in special needs education and disability issues was first sparked by her middle son, who was born profoundly deaf. Barbara has taught as a Special Needs Coordinator and has held leadership positions in several schools, including Academies. She has also worked as SENCo in a secure training centre. Barbara writes primarily for reluctant and struggling readers, with the aim of entertaining the reader and developing empathy for the characters. Pig is her finest example to date.</em>                6/22/2015 11:24:43 AM\r                            6/22/2015 11:24:43 AM\r
