[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku resenseer Emma en die Creepy Komplot\xa9 2016

Kosterkloof is in rep en roer. \u2018n Nuwe skoolhoof is aan beheer van sake by die skool en koshuis; \u2018n nuwe afrigter het leiding geneem van die skool rugbyspan; \u2018n nuwe drama- en musiekonderwyseres maak haar verskyning en die hotel op die dorp kry \u2018n nuwe eienaar wat groot planne vir die hotel sowel as die dorp het. \u2018n Blink nuwe toekoms wink vir die skool en die gemeenskap.Finansies vloei onophoudelik in die skool in. \u2018n Musiekkamer word vir die leerlinge by die hotel ingerig en al die instrumente wat hulle benodig word voorsien. Die rugbyspan se lede kry nuwe selfone en hul ondersteuners pette en t-hemde. \u2018n Nuwe tennisbaan word aan die leerlinge belowe. Die skoolhoof, Gyt Plottenboer, tesame met die eienaar van die hotel, Sarel Samuels, beplan \u2018n kultuurfees vir die dorp en skool. Almal is opgewonde oor die ontwikkelinge by die skool en op die dorp, behalwe Emma. Sy word geteister deur die vraag, \u201cWaar kom al die geld vandaan?\u201dNa die debakel met die Snopkes (wat ongelukkig nie aan die lesers verduidelik word nie ) is Emma lugtig om sommer net al die verwikkelinge op sigwaarde te aanvaar. Haar agterdog word verder geprikkel deur die blou koelsakke wat die sportafrigter elke aand om twee uur by die koshuis aflewer. Sy begin rondsnuffel vir antwoorde en binnekort kry sy bevestiging vir haar vermoedens. Met die hulp van haar vriend, Zoltan, kry hulle genoegsame bewyse om die saak na die polisie te neem en so die raaisel te ontrafel.Die verhaal behou die spanningslyn dwarsdeur die verhaal. Ek het egter gesukkel om in die vloei van die verhaal te kom as gevolg van gebrekkige omskrywing van die karakters, die agtergrond waarteen en die omgewing waarin die verhaal afspeel , sowel as van die vooraf gebeure waarna telkens verwys word. Die onus was op my as leser om self die inligting stukkie vir stukkie bymekaar te sit soos ek brokkies in die storielyn gevind het. Ek weet nog egter steeds nie wie die Snopkes is nie en wat hulle betrokkenheid by en invloed op die skool en gemeenskap was nie. Ek is ook onseker oor die ouderdomme van die betrokke karakters, hul fisiese voorkoms en wie hulle as persone is. Die verhaal word sterk deur die storielyn gedryf, maar ongelukkig ten koste van die onderskeie karakters. Aangesien die hoofkarakters nie vanaf die begin duidelik omskryf word nie, is daar verwarring wanneer \u2018n nuwe karakter die storielyn binnekom. Ek was onseker oor die belang van die karakter tot die verhaal en oor die hoveelheid aandag wat die karakter regverdig. Hierdie faktor het die boek vir my tot slegs \u2018n gemiddelde leeservaring verlaag.Micelle Coetsee                6/22/2015 11:39:05 AM\r                            6/22/2015 11:39:05 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Gabriella en die Hertog van Harte\xa9 2016

Gabriella is kwaad: kwaad omdat haar ma oorlede is, woedend omdat haar pa sowaar staan en trou het met daardie aaklike stadsjapie Patricia wat met haar spykerhakke op hulle plaas rond pronk, en sommer warm onder die kraag omdat die kastige Bolandse perdefluisteraar, Robert, haar behandel asof sy niks van perde af weet nie.<br>Gabi is vasbeslote om haar ma se gunstelingmerrie, Donnabelle, se vullens op te spoor en terug te koop om haar ma se droom om met Oldenburgers te teel, te bewaarheid. Sy hoop dit sal die herinneringe aan haar ma vars in haar en haar pa se gedagtes  hou, veral noudat Patricia se teenwoordigheid dreig om alle tekens van haar ma van die plaas af te laat verdwyn.<br>Een van Donnabelle se afstammelinge is die spoghings Duke, die Hertog van Harte. Die probleem is hy is so humeurig dat hy die bynaam Duke of Death gekry het by die leerders van die landbouskool aan wie hy behoort.<br> Gabi kan dit nie glo wanneer Patricia inmeng in haar soektog na Duke en aanbied om haar en haar maats na die landbouskool in die Boland toe te vat nie. Sy het  so uitgesien om haar pa \u2018n bietjie vir haarself  h\xea op die lang pad Kaap toe. Wat skuil agter  Patricia se optrede? Wil sy Gabi se planne in die wiele ry?<br> Wanneer Gabi die landbouskool se perdefluisteraar ontmoet, kan sy hom dadelik nie verdra nie. Sy is so krapperig teenoor Robert dat hy op sy tande moet kners om nie die bitsige meisiekind in te vlieg nie. Tog het hierdie twee baie meer met mekaar gemeen as wat hulle besef: albei het hulle troos by perde gevind nadat hulle hulle ma\u2019s verloor het en albei het dieselfde benadering tot en liefde vir hierdie edel diere. Albei droom ook daarvan om met perde te boer.<br>In <em>Gabriella en die Hertog van Harte</em>, verweef <strong>Marga Jonker</strong> \u2018n lekker verteltrant, \u2018n interessante verskeidenheid uiteenlopende karakters en  heerlike humor in \u2018n storie wat jy nie kan neersit voor jy die laaste bladsy gelees het nie. Die spanning laai ook op: gaan Gabi te laat by die skool kom om  Duke te koop? Gaan haar probleme met haar stiefma ook haar verhouding met haar pa bederf? En sal sy en Robert ooit die strydbyl begrawe soos wat die lesers graag wil h\xea?<br> Die skrywer se insig in jongmense se lief en leed sal haar beslis laat aanklank vind by lesers wat hulle kan regmaak vir \u2018n lekker kuier met hierdie karakters.<br/></br></br></br></br></br></br>Resensie: Liby Nel<em>emphasized text</em>                11/25/2015 7:41:15 AM\r                            11/25/2015 7:41:15 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku resenseer Prettige Plaas\xa9 2016

Kleurvolle prentjieboeke is \u2018n wonderlike wyse waarop die klein kind aan die w\xeareld van lees voorgestel kan word. Voordat die kind taalvaardighede aangeleer het, kan hulle reeds deel aan die genot van lees deur die illustrasie te ondersoek en te geniet.Goed geillustreerde boekies dui die verband aan tussen woorde, emosies, aksies, gebeurtenisse en die w\xeareld in die algemeen. Deur die kind se eksplorasie van die illustrasies word hierdie verband vasgel\xea nog voor die verwerwing van taal as sulks.Die Vrolike Vriende reeks se kleurvolle prentjieboeke is sodanige handige hulpmiddel vir die ouer in die verwerwing en aanleer van taal by die klein kind. Die boekies se kleurvolle illustrasies is \u2018n uitnodiging aan die kind om die boekie en die karakters te ondersoek en te ontdek.Die stewige kartonbladsye en ronde hoekies maak die boekies maklik hanteerbaar vir klein handjies. Die eenvoudige sinskonstruksie maak die boekie \u2018n goeie keuse vir voorlees aan die klein kind om sodoende die kind se luistertaal te ontwikkel, sowel as om die verband tussen die woorde en die illustrasies vas te l\xea.Die hantering van die omruilbare kartonkarakters help verder met die ontwikkeling van oog-hand ko\xf6rdinasie sowel as probleemoplossing.Micelle Coetsee                7/27/2015 9:11:44 AM\r                            7/27/2015 9:11:44 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku resenseer Bambaduze deur Derick van der Walt\xa9 2016

Derick van der Walt, skrywer van o.a. Lien se lankstaanskoene (Sanlam-prys vir jeuglektuur 2007) en Willem Poprok (M.E.R.-prys vir beste jeugroman 2011) het bekendheid verwerf vir sy menslike verhale wat hy met groot deernis omskryf. Met \u2018n ongekunstelde hand skets hy die besondere leefw\xeareld van die moderne jong volwassene en hul soeke na antwoorde vir eiesoortige uitdagings. Met Bambaduza stel hy weereens nie teleur nie.Jurie Viljoen, matrikulant  aan \u2018n vooraanstaande skool in Pretoria, het o\xebnskynlik opgegee op sy toekoms voordat dit nog begin het. Hy staan apaties teenoor sy skoolwerk en bank gereeld klasse. Hy voel ook oorweldig deur die diep voetspore wat deur voorgangers getrap is en probeer nie eens om in hierdie voetspore te volg nie. Sosiale aktiwiteite saam met sy vriende hou nie meer vir hom vreugde in nie. Wanneer hy per toeval \u2018n goue medalje by \u2018n swemgala verower, weier hy om verder deel van die swemspan te wees. Dinge gaan geensens beter by sy huis nie. Kommunikasie tussen hom en sy pa verbrokkel tot op die punt waar hulle niks meer vir mekaar te s\xea het nie en bymekaar verby leef, elkeen besig met sy eie lewe.Die enigste tyd wanneer Jurie lewendig voel is wanneer hy \u2018n kar steel en vir \u2018n plesierrit daarmee gaan. Keer op keer neem hy die Gautrein na Rosebank waar hy homself in \u2018n w\xeareld ver verwyderd van sy eie vind. Hier beweeg hy onopsigtelik en identiteitsloos deur die strate totdat hy \u2018n motor vind wat hom geval, om te steel. Die opwinding van die oomblik help hom vergeet van sy lewe wat uitsigloos voor hom l\xea.Sy uitkyk op die lewe en sy omstandighede verander wanneer hy deur onvoorsiene omstandighede met Nandi Ngobeni bevriend raak. Hy deel sy geheim met haar en sy dring by hom aan dat hy sal ophou om karre te steel. Hy is vasbeslote om nie weer aan die begeerte toe te gee nie, tot die aand wat hy die Volksie in \u2018n systraat in Brooklyn gewaar. Hy neem hom voor dat dit sy laaste keer sou wees. Min het hy geweet watter kettingreaksie dit tot gevolg sou h\xea.Met \u2018n vernuftige hand skilder Derick van der Walt die grou landskap van Jurie se gebroke w\xeareld en sy innerlike stryd met vrae waarvoor hy nie antwoorde vind nie. Sy simpatieke maar tog ook objektiewe karakterbeelding van Jurie maak dat die leser empatie met Jurie kan ervaar. Die leser ervaar saam met Jurie die onbekende las waaronder hy gebuk gaan en sy selfkastyding deur die wrang e-posse aan sy ma. Maar dit is nie \u2018n verhaal sonder hoop nie. Soos die lente terug keer na hul voorstedelike tuin, breek daar ook \u2018n nuwe seisoen vir Jurie aan. Hy vind sy stem en begin uitdrukking gee aan die pyn wat hy vir lank alleen gedra het. Hy vind in die proses ook die plekkie wat sy voete kan vol staan. Hy maak die keuse om weer te lewe.Lesers wat Pleisters vir die Dooies deur Fanie Viljoen geniet het, sal aanklank vind by hierdie verhaal. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Maisy's Plane - Book Review by Jonathan (3yrs) and his Mum, Rujeko\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: Maisy Mouse in a plane with presents" src="http://ecx.images-amazon.com/images/I/51jGA+n2ZyL.jpg"/><strong>Jonathan is three years old and he doesn't understand all of the questions I ask him, but I can say that, over all, he enjoyed going through the story of '<em>Maisy's plane</em>'</strong>.He was attentive and engaged throughout the book and was also well able to follow the progression of the story.<em>Maisy's Plane</em> by <strong>Lucy Cousins</strong>, is the story of <strong>Maisy Mouse</strong> flying to Eddie's party in her plane.  The propellers go '<em>round and round</em>', and Maisy is '<em>up, up and away</em>'.  Once airborne Maisy greets her friend the duck - '<em>Hello Tallulah</em>.'  '<em>Hello Sun! Hello cloud!</em>'She says.Jonathan understood that the story was about a helicopter flying to a birthday party.  He satisfactorily recognised that the characters in this story were Eddie, <strong>Maisy</strong>, Tallulah, Elephant and Squirrel.He particularly took note of the different modes of transport used, namely <strong>Maisy's</strong> helicopter, Tallulah's balloon, Squirrel's bike and Eddie's truck, but what he was most fascinated with, however, was Tallulah's hot air balloon.<strong>He was most intrigued by the plane's flying upside down!</strong>The name Tallulah seems to have made a lasting impression on my son and his favourite part of the book was the birthday party.Fascinated by the cakes, Jonathan counted them all (including the birthday candles which he said were 'hot') and he 'tasted' them, announcing that they were delicious! Additionally, he noted and counted the crowns worn by Eddie, Elephant and Tallulah.Funnily enough though, the presents didn't make much of an impression on him.The various animals and the components of nature (such as the blue sky, yellow sun, white clouds, green trees(with fruit and flowers); modes of transport; houses; and the birthday party itself)  were all illustrations that my son recognised and I noticed that that helped to make the read both enjoyable and interactive for him.<strong><em>Maisy's Plane</em></strong> is a winner.The use of colour and detail on the cover and throughout the book fully engages with its young readers and the semi-circular turning edge of each page brings a fun and playful feel to the book, naturally enhancing its appeal.This boardbook is certainly tailored for babies and toddlers and I would recommend it for all children up to four years.<strong>Check out Maisy's official website:</strong> http://www.maisyfun.com/forchildren/                6/29/2015 6:59:10 PM\r                            6/29/2015 6:59:10 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Elton Amper-Famous April en Juffrou Brom\xa9 2016

Sommer met die intrapslag kom jy agter dis \u2018n opwindende boek hierdie, een met \u2018n vars aanslag, hope humor en \u2018n hele paar situasies wat jou \u2018n knop in die keel sal laat kry.<br> </br>Elton April is Laerskool Jakaranda se Nommer Een loser. Maar hy\u2019s ook \u2018n aartsoptimis en reken daar is niks wat hom keer om eendag famous te word nie. Hy het sy visier gestel op \u2018n skrywer or \u2018n rapper of  dalk \u2018n krieketspeler wat kan skryf \xe9n rap!<br/>Daarom skryf hy alles in sy lewe neer  \u2013 kompleet met reggemaakte spelling (want hy kan nie spel om sy lewe te red!), kantaantekeninge en sketse. Dis nou ekstra inligting vir die boek wat eendag oor hom geskryf gaan word wanneer hy famous is.<br/>Maar intussen moet hy eers graad sewe deurkom en dit gaan nie \u2018n grap wees nie. Dis ook nie al probleem wat hy het nie. Sy krieket-kit word gesteel en daar\u2019s nie geld om dit te vervang nie (en hoe kan hy \u2018n famous krieketspeler word as hy nie meer vir die eerstes kan uitdraf nie?); sy groot projek vir Entrepreneursdag dreig om een yslike gemors te wees en die hoofmeisie maak gedurig sy naam toffie.<br/>\u2018n Mens kom gou agter Elton se probleme hou nie by die skool op nie. Sy ma het die gewoonte om saam met slymbol-boyfriends te verdwyn en hom dae lank te los om alleen en sonder geld op te snork. Sy dad is in Oudtshoorn . Hy dink die son skyn  uit hom uit en dis nie voor die einde van die boek dat Elton agterkom hy kan eintlik net so min op sy pa kan as op sy ma staatmaak nie.<br/>As dit vir Mr Reddy by die Spar was wat vir hom los werkies laat doen het vir geld nie, sou hy menige dag nie nat of droog oor sy lippe gehad en nie. Selfs Mr Reddy se buitetoilet moes al \u2018n keer of wat instaan as slaapplek.<br/>Nogtans is daar nie \u2018n greintjie selfbejammering by Elton te bespeur nie. Hy\u2019s selfstandig, dink op sy voete en kan in \u2018n japtrap met \u2018n vindingryke plan of twee vorendag kom. Daarom bly die aanslag van die boek altyd opgeruimd en verval dit nooit in sentimentaliteit of swartgalligheid nie.<br/>Die nuwe Afrikaans-onderwyseres, Juffrou Broom (of Brom soos sy gou gedoop word), is die skerpste vrou wat Elton nooit ooit te\xebgekom het. Niemand in die klas kan haar \u2018n rat voor die o\xeb draai nie en sy trap jou sommer soos \u2018n Gunston-stompie as jy vir haar probeer lieg. Wat Elton veral laat lekkerkry is dat sy selfs deur die neus-in-die-lug hoofmeisie, Letitzia,se skynheiligheid sien en vinnig haar tjank vir haar aftrap.<br/>Juffrou Brom het ook vreemde idees oor die leer van Afrikaans. Sy gooi onmiddellik al die ou klasre\xebls, woordeboeke en plakkate van dooie digters uit en nuwe begrippe soos \u201ckannie is dood van kruiwa stoot\u201d en \u201cprobeer is die beste geweer\u201d word opgeplak.Elton is oortuig hy en sy beste p\xeal, Dawid, kan hulle drome maar koebaai soen, want met hierdie juffrou sien hy swarigheid om graad sewe deur te kom. Sy\u2019s oral waar jy haar die minste verwag, sy kom met begrippe uit wat niemand ken nie, sy sien dwarsdeur jou en het die vuil manier om jou heeltemal onkant in die klas te betrap.<br/>En wat is haar, die Bakkieboef en meneer Wolles se storie? Is al die gissings oor hulle waar? Hoekom plant sy \u2018n groentetuin by die skool? En hoekom is haar o\xeb soms dikgehuil wanneer sy by die klas aankom?<br/>Al hierdie geheime en nog \u2018n hele paar aangename verrassings wag op Elton en sy klasmaats met hierdie nuwe juffrou want daar steek baie meer in haar as wat hulle ooit sou kon dink.&gt;br&gt;Met <em>Elton Amper-Famous April en Juffrou Brom</em> slaag <strong>Carin Krahtz</strong> nie net daarin om \u2018n spannende storie vol humor, verrassings in kwinkslae te skryf nie, sy gee ook sommer Afrikaans-les sonder dat jy dit agterkom omdat dit so subtiel en vermaaklik gedoen word!<br/>En juffrou Brom se byderwetse ingesteldheid, wat haar so in voeling bring met haar leerlers, wys ook vir elkeen van ons dat daar meer as een manier is om na \u2018n saak of \u2018n vak te kyk en dat kreatiwiteit aangemoedig en beloon moet word.<br/>Die omslagillustrasie en kantsketse deur Silvia Rebel is in die kol en hierdie boek met sy lekker loslitafrikaans word beslis hoog aanbeveel.Resensie: Liby Nel                2/14/2016 12:23:29 PM\r                            2/14/2016 12:23:29 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku resenseer Swemlesse vir \u2018n Meermin deur Marita van der Vyver\xa9 2016

Hanna Minnaar bevind haar alleen op die vaarwaters van adolessensie en daar is niemand om haar rigting aan te wys in hierdie vreemde landskap nie. Uit haar soeke na antwoorde vir die uitdagings wat haar te beurt val sowel as die slentergang van haar Desember skoolvakansie wat sy tuis deurbring, word \u2018n gids vir hierdie wisselvallige lewensfase gebore. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku resenseer Clint Eastwood van Wyk en die Moordenaarsklok deur Pieter Verwey\xa9 2016

Die steampunk voorblad van die boek het my dadelik opgeval en ek kon nie wag om verby die titelblad te kom en myself tussen die bladsye te verloor nie. Dit was die eerste smakie wat ek van steampunk in afrikaans sou kry en ek wou met genoegdoening die oomblik ervaar. Clint Eastwood van Wyk en sy Amerikaanse neef, Budde spandeer hulle Julie skoolvakansie saam met Clint se ouers in die middel van die Moordenaarskaroo waar Clint se pa besig is met argeologiese opgrawings. Min het Clint geweet wat die nadraai van sy planne sou wees. Clint en Budde raak ook bevriend met Kiewiet, een van die inwoners van die plaas wat hulle besoek. Kort voor lank raak die drie betrokke in \u2018n avontuur wat min mense hulle sal glo.Slegs drie steampunk elemente kom in die verhaal voor naamlik die tegnologie element, die hout en koper element en die stoomkrag element, wat eers tydens die tweede helfte van die verhaal ter sprake kom. Die verhaal speel dit ook nie in \u2018n retro era af soos van \u2018n steampunk verhaal verwag nie. Geharde steampunk aanhangers sal die verhaal dalk nie in die genre klassifiseer nie. Nieteenstaande, is dit \u2018n heerlike avontuurverhaal wat deurspek is met Clint se spitsvondighede en komiese insidente. Die onwaarskynlikhede van hulle avontuur maak die leeservaring iets besonder. Vir \u2018n man met sy wortels in die advertensiew\xeareld, het Pieter homself uitstekend van sy taak gekwyt. <img alt="Book Cover: Nokulunga, Mother of Goodness, runs from the cooking pot" src="http://d4rri9bdfuube.cloudfront.net/assets/images/book/large/9781/4856/9781485600763.jpg"/><strong>Eight year old, Yamile Moyo, reviews 'Nokulunga, Mother of Goodness'</strong>This story is about a magic pot.The main characters are the family members that use the pot - Nokulunga, the first wife; Zintle, Noncedo,Nobulumko, the new brides; Zinto the husband and Zimkhitha, the child. As each new bride comes home, the magic cooking pot is produced to test her. <strong>Says Yamile</strong>, "I like the part in the very beginning where the mother of the bride tells her daughter all there is to know about her duties as a wife and mother. I also liked the part of baby Zimkhitha being born.I liked that the magic pot could cook yummy food and also that it could talk, jump and scream like a human. I don't think the pot was evil, I just think that maybe it wasn't meant for cooking. Maybe it was supposed to be used for something else and it could have been a good friend?The book made me feel sad, especially because of the child that died and also the wives that died. I felt angry with the man and his last wife, Nobulumko, for killing the first wife, Nokulunga. I think they should have just sent her away or to jail for killing the other wives, but they shouldn't have killed her.I wouldn't really recommend this book to other children because it has a sad ending, but I think the story shows that you can't trust people because not everyone is honest (like Nokulunga wasn't honest with Zinto).I also learnt that children shouldn't just blindly obey their parents, especially when the parents are telling them to do something wrong.<strong>Puku reviewer, Rujeko Moyo, Yamile's mother says:</strong>This folktale engaged Yamile throughout, but it wasn't an enjoyable read because of the repeated deaths. She did, however, learn vital lessons from the tale, which was probably the primary aim of the story.I would recommend it for a slightly older age group (maybe 10-12 years) that can appreciate the lesson relayed without being too affected by the deaths.I love the minimalist look to '<em>Nokulunga, Mother of Goodness</em>'. It is simple but beautiful. The glitterwork on the outside cover is a perfect finish (and probably the magic-pull-factor for any child) and my daughter loved it!<img alt="Author photo: Sindiwe Magona" src="http://www.kwela.com/Authors/HomePage/sindiwe-magona-scholtz.jpg"/>I also loved the illustrations in the book. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU resenseer  Kan 'n pikkewyn fietsry?... en ander vrae\xa9 2016

Dink jy \u2018n koningspikkewyn sal vir jou kom kuier? En as hy sou, wat sal jy doen? Wat gaan jy vir hom gee om te eet, dink jy hy sal saam met jou na die supermark kan gaan?<em>Kan \u2018n pikkewyn fietsry?</em> is een  van vier nuwe boeke in \u2018n reeks van skrywer <strong>Aleksei Bitskoff</strong> wat lesers van vier jaar oud en ouer op prettige wyse sal leer van koningspikkewyne.Die manier waarop feite oorgedra word sal byklank vind by die jonger kind en maklik vasgel\xea word in die geheue. 'n Koningspikkewyn sal nie saam kan kegelbal speel nie, want hy het nie vingers om die bal mee vas te hou nie, en hy sal nie saam met jou in die kerkkoor kan sing nie, hy jil en gil heeltemal te veel. Die w\xeareldkaart aan die einde van die boek wys die woonplekke van die koningspikkewyn mooi uit en daar is addisionele feite wat vir beide kind en volwassene baie leersaam sal wees. Die helderkleurige  illustrasies van pikkewyne op ryplanke, fietse en op die kegelbaan is baie komies en kan tot lekker interaksie lei. <strong>Kobus Geldenhuys</strong> het hom goed van sy taak gekwyt met die vertaling.As jou kind \u2018n besondere aanklank het vir seelewe, behoort <em>Feite en geite: seediere. Kan \u2018n pikkewyn fietsry? \u2026 en ander vrae</em> \u2018n gunsteling te wees.                8/3/2015 11:00:37 AM\r                            8/3/2015 11:00:37 AM\r

"<em>I could, and would, most definitely, use this book in the classroom, however, I would focus more on the underlying messages</em>." There is also the hint that those living there are unable to see beyond their technology and the bright lights, and unable to think for themselves. The fact that the \u2018Kool Kats\u2019 cell phone is missing, stumps them all. The characters are unable to think of alternate solutions themselves, proving and emphasising our inability to become problem solvers in the modern day world.<strong>The illustrations are fitting and appealing to children, effectively blending modern day life with that of the African plains</strong> The images are relevant to today's children and draw in their attention by making the characters look \u2018cool\u2019, as well as including technological devices in an environment where one would not expect to see such things. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Geheime Koninkryk: Borrelvulkaan\xa9 2016

Boesemvriendinne Tamsin, Janie en Bianka het lanklaas geheime boodskappe van die Towerkissie gekry. Koning Kieliebaard en Trixibelle, die feetjie, vra soms die drie meisies se hulp wanneer dinge nie klopdisselboom gaan in die Geheime Koninkryk nie. Koning Kieliebaard se nare suster, koningin Gorina is knaend aan die probeer om heerskappy van die land by haar broer te gaps.In <em>Geheime Koninkryk \u2013 Borrelvulkaan</em> word die drie uitgenooi na \u2018n lentebal by die paleis. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU resenseer Fanie Viljoen se PLONS\xa9 2016

Hein dink hy droom wanneer die pragtige Mila aanbied om hulle swembad skoon te maak. Maar die droom verander vinnig in \u2018n nagmerrie wanneer sy en haar hele familie in hulle swembad kom plak. Wanneer hy hulle uiteindelik uit die swembad kry, trek hulle in die badkamer in met morsige gevolge. Die prettige taalgebruik en alliterasie (soos Milla, Mollie, Montie en mars-moeras) tintel op die tong en, saam met rymwoorde, help dit om die storie seepglad te laat ontvou.<br/>Die lekker humor en tipiese situasies tussen ouboet, kleinsus, hulle ouers en die meermense laat lesers met hulle identifiseer en dra verder by tot die leesgenot. Die spesiale gebruik van tipografie help belangrike woorde uitstaan en die lesertjie om dit beter te onthou.<br/>Sommer so ongemerk word dit by die lesers tuisgebring hoe belangrik dit is om nie te mors in ons oseane nie want dit maak dit onleefbaar vir visse en ander waterbewoners. Ons hou nie daarvan dat daar in ons huise gemors word nie, so hoekom dink ons ons kan maar diere, visse en vo\xebls se habitat bemors? Dis 'n baie belangrike punt om by ons kinders tuis te bring in hierdie era van omgewingsagteruitgang. <br/>In die ATKV-Woordveertjies se  kategorie vir Kinderboektoekennings stem lesers self vir hulle gunstelingboeke en -illustrasies en <em>Plons</em> het verlede jaar as die wenner weggestap. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU resenseer AS EK VAL\xa9 2016

Hierdie ontroerende verhaal van liefde en verlies sal lank nadat jy die laaste bladsy gelees het nog by jou spook.<br/>Hoewel dit handel oor die laaste kosbare weke in die lewe van \u2018n tiener wat terminaal siek is, verval dit nooit in swartgalligheid of soetsappigheid nie. Trouens, die nugter verteltrant wortel jou dadelik in die werklikheid waarmee Kara daagliks te make het. <br/>Sy besef sy verloor vinnig  haar 4-jaar-lange stryd teen leukemie en skielik word haar hele lewe gekonsentreer in die volgende paar...wat? Maande? Weke? Dae? Hoe pas jy \u2018n leeftyd se leef in so \u2019n kort tydjie in?<br/>Maar sy is vasbeslote om, soos TS Elliot dit gestel het, uit te gaan met \u2018n \u201cbang\u201d en nie \u2018n \u201cwimper\u201d nie. Daarom stel sy \u2018n lys van 10 dinge op wat sy wil doen voor sy doodgaan.<br/>Haar beste vriendin, Nicky, se hulp word ingeroep en binne \u2018n japtrap is die eerste item op Kara se lys - seks - afgetik. Maar dis eers wanneer sy liefde leer ken dat Kara besef waaroor seks eintlik gaan.<br/>Soos sy deur haar lys werk, kom sy agter dat vrede en geluk jou dikwels verras in die eenvoudige dinge: die luukse om jou diepste geheime te deel met iemand wat jou verstaan; die teenwoordigheid van jou gesin wat die pyn verdryf en  jou in warmte koester; \u2018n motorfietsrit wat die bloed deur jou are laat bruis; of \u2018n lieflike uitsig wat die gewoel van die stad soos \u2018n mantel van jou laat afval.<br/>Die kollig val op ook die verhoudings in Kara se lewe. Daar\u2019s haar vervreemde ma wat amper \u2018n jaar nadat sy gediagnoseer is uit die vreemde voor hulle deur opdaag; haar jonger boetie wat haar om die beurt irriteer, dood wens en uitgelate in haar avonture deel; Nicky wie se situasie \u2018n skrille kontras met haar eie vorm; haar k\xearel wat haar soms weer gesond en opgewonde oor die lewe laat voel.<br/>Een dan is daar haar pa - die eintlike tragiese figuur wat heeltyd op die agtergrond huiwer: beskermend, soekend na nuwe mediese ontwikkelings, verskeur deur die feit dat sy stukkie vir stukkie van hom af weggevat word terwyl hy hulpeloos toekyk, wat die stryd aanhou stry ten spyte van die moegheid en hopeloosheid wat dreig om hom te oorweldig.<br/>Uiteindelik moet Kara ook met haarself vrede maak. Haar liggaamlike agteruitgang. Die emosionele verwerking van mense se vrees vir haar siekte wat hulle ongemaklik maak en haar laat vermy. En die innerlike eensaamheid omdat jy op \u2018n plek is waar ander jou nie regtig kan bereik nie. <br/>Sy beleef oomblikke van woede en rebelsheid, \u2018n lus om ander so seer te maak soos sy het; die drang om goed te vernietig: foto\u2019s van haar toe daar nog hoop was, die word-gesond-kaartjies en partytjierokke.<br/>Kara openbaar die tipiese selfbeheptheid van die terminaal sieke: hoe kan jy vir jou eindeksamen swot as ek jou nodig het? Hoe kan jy slaap terwyl ek doodgaan? <br/>Hierdie boek is ook deurspek van humor \u2013 al is Kara s\u2019n dikwels galgehumor \u2013 en haar wilde verbeeldingsvlugte neem jou  op \u2018n sprokiesavontuur wat jou met nuwe o\xeb na die lewe laat kyk. Dis uiteindelik \u2018n verhaal vol hoop en 'n liefde vir die lewe.<br/><em>As Ek Val</em> is oorspronklik in Engels uitgegee as <strong>Jenny Downham</strong> se <em>Before I  Die</em> en het w\xeareldwyd toekennings ingepalm, waaronder:<br> * Publishers Weekly se beste kinderboek van die jaar<br>* Booklist Editors\u2019 Choice<br>* Book Sense Children\u2019s Pick<br>* Kirkus Reviews se redakteurskeuse<br>* Publishers Weekly se Flying Start Author<br>* ALA-YALSA se toptien beste boeke vir jong volwassenes<br/></br></br></br></br></br></br>Dis ook deur die BBC verfilm as Now is Good, met Dakota Fanning in die hoofrol.<br/><em>As ek val</em> is uitstekend vertaal deur Lydia du Plessis en is \u2019n onvergeetlike boek wat deur ho\xebrskoollesers \xe9n volwassenes geniet sal word.<br/>Resensie: Liby Nel                4/14/2016 9:51:44 AM\r                            4/14/2016 9:51:44 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews the Supernova Magazine, Vol 4.6 2015\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: Supernova Mag, History of video games" src="http://www.magazines.co.za/uploads/medium/568875001439480497.jpg"/><strong>Did you know that Mangroves are considered to be amongst the rarest and most threatened of forest types in South Africa?</strong><strong>The Kosi Bay Mangrove Forests are unique plants that extract freshwater from saltwater!</strong> Yes, it's possible, and having never been to Kosi Bay, I was enthralled by this information and rather appreciated being able to learn something new too.  As parents, all we want for our children is a chance for them to learn and to be exposed to the world they live in.On opening the <strong>Supernova Magazine</strong>, the inside cover has an illustrated map of our continent, with a list of African countries and tiny drawings that had both me and the kids pouring over it, searching for sights we recognized. Instantly drawn in, I have no doubt, that had the kids had crayons, it would have been some time before they moved on to the rest of the book.Alongside the <em>Nova Note</em> in the introduction, is a great little cartoon that often catches my eye, but this time the dialogue was in SWAHILI.  I loved this and thought this was a fabulous addition for the kids who read Supernova in English, but speak many other languages in their daily lives. Way to go, Supernova team!That cartoon sets the tone for the rest of the magazine as Tanzania is the country featured on <em>Andy\u2019s Africa</em>, covering not only the geographical points, but also the tribes of Tanzania and the languages they speak.  From there, the storyline continues up Africa to the <em>Maasai</em>, giving kids the chance to learn about the languages spoken, the Maasai homes, where they came from and what foods are traditionally eaten by these nomadic people.<img alt="Cover: The Maasai" src="http://www.magazines.co.za/uploads/small70/419284001439363335.jpg"/> <strong>This article provides a fascinating look into a culture that is fast disappearing.</strong>In Africa, people are different too in the way they look and behave. In the <em>Supernova Chatroom</em> this week is the subject of <em>Xenophobia</em>. This is a gently written, child-appropriate article that still drives the message home.  In fact, so inspired was <strong>Jenna \u2013 Lane Fuller</strong> (14 years) by reading this, that she abruptly said: \u201c<em>Oh Man! I\u2019m going to use this book for school speeches!</em>\u201dAs children learn about other people, they must also learn about the places they come from, and the page on small towns was a topic I\u2019d not noticed before.  In this issue <em>Parys</em> is the featured town.  I was pleasantly surprised and felt it a wonderful topic for educational purposes, as well as an important introduction for kids new to South Africa.<strong>As usual Supernova has great recycling and green ideas.</strong><img alt="Cover image: Litre of light" src="http://www.magazines.co.za/uploads/small70/813927001439363721.jpg"/>Kids can create their own hanging herb gardens \u2013 a wonderful way to grow produce without needing great amounts of space or water.  And, the environmental story: \u2018<em>Litre of Light</em>\u2019, is an interesting read about recycling old coke bottles.The main feature <em>the History of Video Games</em>, immediately drew interest, even from the kids near us who were playing on their tablets.  The four-page spread is filled with interesting facts that even non-gamers, (like me) can enjoy.<img alt="Cover: History of Video Games" src="http://www.magazines.co.za/uploads/small70/085857001439363227.jpg"/><strong>This magazine is a really great read, especially in a group and the kids (even the big ones) enjoyed me reading it out loud with them.</strong>Having not read a Supernova for a while I was impressed with the simpler layout and easy-to-read pages.  This magazine has all the relevant South African information that kids should know about, and is, seriously, a first class production.<strong>Forget those bulky encyclopedias and learn all about your world here.</strong><strong><em>Nikki McDiarmid.</em></strong><hr/><img alt="Logo: Supernova Magazine" src="http://www.gondwanaalive.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/Supernova-magaizne-logo-small-1-300x136.jpg"/><strong>To subscribe:</strong> http://www.magazines.co.za/magazine/supernova.html                9/15/2015 8:53:28 AM\r                            9/18/2015 5:59:12 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews 'Rhinocephants on the Roof'\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: &lt;em&gt;Rhinocephants on the Roof&lt;/em&gt;" src="http://www.iol.co.za/polopoly_fs/bk-rhinocephants-1.1861063!/image/2843808779.jpg_gen/derivatives/box_300/2843808779.jpg"/><strong>With muted evening colours, the drawings and simple writing echo the night, as young readers are introduced to Daniel, who is sleeping over at his grandparent\u2019s house. It is here that the noises are unfamiliar and the shadows strange and scary.  He begins to see monsters in the dark shapes, that are not normally there\u2026</strong>Not dissimilar to a movie screen, there is an incredible play on the light and dark aspects of this tale, on courage and fear, shadow and depth.But, the story is also filled with hope. Hope that fills the somber places inside children\u2019s minds and highlights the power of trust and understanding that comes from adults as they soothe all fears and calm the night.The illustrations are classical and rather European in detail; Daniel in his 'onesie' with his old suitcase and teddy bear, alongside the striped wallpaper of a rather English setting. Designed to emphasise the length of the book, the figures are stiff and elongated and there are tall ladders that stretch to up to strange places\u2026 making the walls seem longer and the bed so much smaller...<img alt="Illustration: In Daniel's room, &lt;em&gt;Rhinocephants on the Roof&lt;/em&gt;" src="https://s-media-cache-ak0.pinimg.com/236x/b8/0e/8d/b80e8de514623a8328364406cec55172.jpg"/><strong>This is, however, an uncomfortable book to read</strong><em>Rhinocephants on the Roof</em> highlights the fear of the unknown, taking the reader on a journey through this horror to a place where the mind can process the emotions and find tools to overcome them.As an adult I was transported back in time to when I had a creature beneath my bed and my sister slept above a hungry animal, the memories instantly recalled.  And I have no doubt that those who have never experienced this emotional trauma, will gain an understanding of it through these pages.Personally, I have visions of children all over Southern Africa creating their own beastly combinations and turning them into protectors instead of tokoloshes.These pages might be scary at first, but they are amusing later and they capture readers again and again as children search for the missing bear and the elusive cat, finding details they had missed before. The scenery is sublime and wonderfully detailed.<strong>This is a super book with a very powerful message.</strong><em>Nikki McDiarmid</em><hr/><h2>Olinosters op die dak</h2>Second language readers may find the Afrikaans version, <strong>Olinosters op die dak</strong>, a bit advanced in terms of language, but they will certainly react to the picture story.\u201c<em>It\u2019s the story of what is happening in Daniel's imagination,</em>\u201d says eleven year old, Chris,\u201c<em>but it\u2019s freaky!</em>\u201d and is reluctant to turn the pages as he picks up on Daniel's discomfort. At the same time though, he is wondering what will happen...<img alt="Book Cover: The scary house in &lt;em&gt;Olinosters op die dak&lt;/em&gt;" src="https://www.cna.co.za/media/catalog/productimages//7/9/79611931.jpg"/> \u201c<em>What is something bad happens to him? What if the clock falls on his head?</em>\u201dThe entire look of the book worries Chris, but his Afrikaans teacher on the other hand, is impressed with the illustrations and at how well he reads the story, helping out here and there when he cannot understand."<em>It's a story that is both 'curious and cautious'...</em>" she says."<em>Huh!  These monsters! It's funny you know,</em>" says Chris, "<em>because Daniel says he's not scared, but he really is</em>."I think Chris was rather scared too.The jumbled names of the shadow creatures are fun. They add a lighthearted feel to a scary subject, but I think it's more fun for the teachers and parents to see how well children can read them...Says the Afrikaans teacher, "<em>This is a wonderful book of the imagination, in the dark, where pyjamas are bobarillas!</em>"<strong>To buy the book:</strong> http://www.loot.co.za/product/marita-van-der-vyver-rhinocephants-on-the-roof/hlvg-3097-g190?referrer=iosa<hr/><img alt="Illustration: The Rhinocephant from &lt;em&gt;Rhinocephants on the Roof&lt;/em&gt;" src="https://s-media-cache-ak0.pinimg.com/736x/10/ac/c8/10acc8d30f9d922f8bc155795822a0a7.jpg"/><h2>Further comments from reviewers:</h2><strong>Jenna-Lane Fuller, 14 years</strong>: "<em>The pictures are very scary and at first the story is wierd - it comes across as very creepy and dark.  But that's only the first time.  Then it's fun</em>."<strong>Manana du Toit, 11 years</strong>: "<em>It's cute!  And they all have mixed names!  I thought the drawings were really good and I read it before I went to bed and I wasn't scared</em>."<strong>Zoe da Silva, 12 years</strong>: "<em>Every time you look, you see something else.</em>"<strong>Louise da Silva</strong>: "<em>I Love the illustrations and they do seem more English in representation which is fun as the monsters are African animals...it's the boogey man under the bed and coming through the window and treading on the roof...</em>"<strong>Michelle Stanley Fuller</strong>: "<em>Going off the images alone, the book is odd, creepy and bizarre at first, but Oh! [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Young Sarah Yamile Moyo (8yrs) reviews 'Anna Angrysaurus'\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: Anna Angrysaurus" src="http://ep.yimg.com/ay/barronseduc/anna-angrysaurus-2.gif"/><strong>This story is about a dinosaur called Anna Angrysaurus. She is selfish and she gets angry a lot; so angry in fact that she can even erupt like a volcano!</strong> <strong>But by the end of the story, with her parents help, Anna has learnt to control herself when she gets angry.</strong>The main characters in this story are Anna and her Mum and Dad. Anna gets angry when her brother and sister receive gifts and she doesn\u2019t; she gets angry when her brother wins the games they play; she gets angry when she cannot watch her favourite TV program; and she even gets angry for no reason at all!When Anna's temper rises she stomps her feet, she roars so loudly that the windows rattle and the vases fall from the shelves, and she charges at the door!You see, Anna\u2019s problem is that she's selfish and she can't control herself when she gets angry, but I liked it when Anna discovered that she <em>could</em> control herself and she learnt how to control her moods better.<strong>I thought it was funny when Anna got angry and didn\u2019t even know why she was angry.</strong>Her brother and sister are also funny - they call each other silly names like \u2018Swamp Breath\u2019, \u2018Dino Dummy\u2019 and \u2018Baby Horns\u2019. I liked that the author, <strong>Brian Moses</strong>, could think of such funny things.I related to the part when Anna was angry about not being able to watch her favourite TV programme, because I also feel irritated when my dad changes my TV programs to something he wants to watch.<strong>I liked this book.  I was happy that Anna learnt to control herself and I found the story to be quite funny</strong>My favourite part is where the author tells us that Anna sometimes got so angry that she felt like she would erupt like a volcano! And of course where Anna and her brother and sister played the game of sticking their heads into a T.Rex\u2019s mouth!Yes, I would recommend this book to other children, and I think my friend Mmoutle would like it because I think she needs to learn how to get mad! She\u2019s too nice sometimes and I think she needs to show it when she's angry.<h2>BOOK REVIEW by Rujeko Moyo</h2><img alt="Book Cover: Little purple Anna Angrysaurus" src="http://ecx.images-amazon.com/images/I/51EVBtc8tZL._SL500_AA130_.jpg"/><em>Anna Angrysaurus</em> is a comically illustrated, pastel-coloured dinosaur story on paperback. Though funny in the way the message is relayed, the story truthfully demonstrates what anger looks like, feels like and acts like \u2013 and then provides some useful ideas on how to control it. <strong>I like that the book ventures to look at the causes for anger, the signs of anger and finally, how to control anger.</strong> I would recommend this book for children between the ages of 4-8 years. Ages 4-6 years would understand it as a story that\u2019s read to them whilst ages 7-8 years should be able to read the story on their own.Anger is a natural emotion that parents often try to curb in children because it is not a pretty thing to behold or endure. This book, however, demonstrates that though there is a need for anger to be controlled, it is healthy and necessary for this emotion to be expressed. It is an emotion that requires an outlet.The humour riddled throughout this book makes the story an enjoyable read, even as one gleans vital lessons on anger management during the process.<strong>Find out more about the author, Brian Moses:</strong> https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Moses<strong>Find out more about the illustrator, Mike Gordon:</strong> http://gordonillustration.com/                9/21/2015 9:35:03 AM\r                            9/22/2015 8:02:58 AM\r

<img alt="Illustration: Sam and Dave dig a hole" src="http://70f186a60af817fe0731-09dac41207c435675bfd529a14211b5c.r92.cf1.rackcdn.com/assets/attachments_p/000/048/839/size500_Prints_JonKlassen_SAM&amp;DAVE-6_main.jpg"/><strong><em>Sam and Dave Dig a Hole</em> takes readers into the private spaces that children inhabit, exploring the complete joy, the unlimited freedom and the journey of children's minds as they play.</strong>Sam and Dave leave their house dressed for adventure, wearing boots and carrying shovels. And zoo biscuits.Told primarily through earthy illustrations, <strong>Mac Barnett\u2019s</strong> story touches upon the emotions of readers, both young and old. I can\u2019t help, but wonder at the need for South African children to dream... or for us all to open our minds.<strong>Louise</strong>, another parent, snorts with laughter on finishing this book.\u201c<em>Oh my goodness!</em>\u201d she says. \u201c<em>But this story's about LIFE! [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews 'The Flying Bath' by Julia Donaldson\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: The Flying Bath" src="http://ecx.images-amazon.com/images/I/51XDMcxSOOL._SY446_BO1,204,203,200_.jpg"/><strong>At first, Julia Donaldson\u2019s story is, I must admit, rather strange.</strong> <strong>And yet, as we read it over and over, (my three year old does this with new books), I found myself enjoying <em>The Flying Bath</em> more and more.</strong><strong>This is a superhero story with a difference.</strong> The bath is under the control of three bath toys; a frog, a duck and a turtle. Together, the toys fill the bath up as soon as the family leave the house and then take calls from those in need through the bath\u2019s shower spray. As soon as they have someone, the bath flies around the world during the day to help out anyone in need of water.The ending is great too and my son loves the fact that the piglet, after being washed by the toys, is dirty again by the time the bath flies off to help someone else. As in all of Julia Donaldson's books, the pictures are great, the text is simple and the rhymes make it easy to read.And, luckily for me, the story is easy to remember so while we are driving in the car I can repeat the story without seeing the book!<strong>The illustrations are wonderful as there are enough little details in the pictures that allow for new things to be spotted, even as far in as the tenth read.</strong> My only critique is that the baboon looks more like a mandrill, but then being from Africa I find we notice these mistakes in books more often than the rest of the world would. I wouldn\u2019t hesitate to recommend this book to parents and teachers.<em>Nicky Townsend</em>                10/1/2015 1:01:18 PM\r                            10/1/2015 1:11:54 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku Book Review - 'Julius Zebra'\xa9 2016

<img alt="Cover: Julius Zebra by Gary Northfield" src="http://panmacmillan.co.za/wp-content/uploads/2015/06/9781406354928.jpg"/><strong>Julius Zebra is a hilarious story, filled with quirky characters, and is one of those tales that readers can get quite caught up in.</strong><strong><em>You don\u2019t want to stop reading!</em></strong>"<em>This is a book that makes it easy to imagine that you\u2019re there, watching every minute and not just reading - I absolutely adore this book,</em>" says reviewer <strong>Aimee Webster.</strong>The main characters in the story include a quirky zebra named Julius, a know-it-all warthog named Cornelius, and a lion\u2026just an ordinary lion.Julius Zebra is at the watering hole with his family where his brother is irritating him so badly that he wishes a crocodile would just come and eat him!  He leaves the herd behind to go exploring on his own, only to get lost and fall into a deep hole. He\u2019s trapped, and soon he's put with animals of all types - antelopes, zebra, buck, lions\u2026 you name it. <strong>Julius Zebra is going to Rome!</strong> He\u2019s going to see the circus\u2026 well, the whole duration of the drive he <em>thinks</em> he\u2019s going to <strong>WATCH</strong> the circus (and he\u2019s thrilled because he\u2019s never been a part of the audience before... all the animals are.) They have absolutely no idea that they are the ones the audience will be watching, and that they will be trained twenty-four seven as gladiators! I'd like to recommend this book to younger readers and schoolsKids are able to feel like they are inside the story, acting it out with Julius and Cornelius. Schools can also do so much with this subject - setting speeches, tests, spelling and even reading when school\u2019s almost finished and there's a few minutes left to go. <strong>Bring out the books!</strong>This story, written by <strong>Gary Northfield</strong>, has inspired me - not to go to the circus and be trained, not to become friends with a warthog, but to remove my blinkers and allow variety into my life. So, I truly encourage you to buy this book, even if it is for your niece or someone else you may know.  Kids will really like it.<strong>This review was written by:</strong><strong>Aimee Webster, Grade 6</strong> <hr/><img alt="Illustration: Gary Northfield, Julius Zebra" src="http://www.storymuseum.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2015/08/web-banner3.jpg"/><strong>Filled with wonderful illustrations and delightful puns and jokes, Julius Zebra is incredibly amusing.  This is a story guaranteed to encourage reluctant readers and get them chortling out loud.</strong><em>Nikki McDiarmid</em><strong><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jmMJra1wndo">Watch the trailer</strong><strong>Buy the Book:</strong> http://panmacmillan.co.za/catalogue/julius-zebra/<img alt="Logo: Pan Macmillan" src="https://fbcdn-profile-a.akamaihd.net/hprofile-ak-xfa1/v/t1.0-1/20068_284852760887_1559671_n.jpg?oh=51765f1b7634e3d00c8bea6ec55277e0&amp;oe=568633FC&amp;__gda__=1452031496_97b010830c48a7b03cbd5566ba7bbe66"/><hr/>                10/27/2015 9:15:41 AM\r                            10/27/2015 9:43:10 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews 'Frost Fire', The Kanin Chronicles, by Amanda Hocking\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: Frost Fire by Amanda Hocking" src="http://d39ttiideeq0ys.cloudfront.net/assets/images/book/large/9781/4472/9781447256649.jpg"/><strong>Amanda Hocking has sold millions of books globally and will always be referred to as the writer who made <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2012/jan/12/amanda-hocking-self-publishing">bestseller status by self-publishing online.</strong>The first chapter is a little confusing and rather slow, with a great deal of backstory and excess detail, but at the same time, there are subtle innuendos that are really quite intriguing, ensnaring the reader into a fascinating story.Alongside some exaggerated internal dialogue, there are also some very worrying English phrases such as \u201cI\u2019m sure you did wonderful,...\u201d, that may well see South African readers closing the book right then and there. But there is a reason that this author is so widely acclaimed, for this novel is so much more than a few bad phrases and the brief explanation that is written on it's cover.<strong><em>Frost Fire</em> has all the elements of a great fantasy story</strong>Bryn is nineteen years old and has graduated as a tracker in the defense corps, responsible for protecting the changelings that are borrowed to the human world. A half-breed, and different to the rest of the clan, Bryn has constantly been singled out and targeted, bullied by the aristocracy, and had to fight for every step of her survival, making her a tough and heroic character that young readers can connect with.As children go missing in Trylle, it seems that Bryn is the only key to solving the mystery\u2026 and a mystery it is, indeed, for even Bryn doesn\u2019t know why she is at the centre of it all.A dark underworld of greed, kidnapping and murder provides the plot with suspense, alongside an intense and romantic story line, providing the reader with a gripping blend of genres that has kept Puku reviewers hooked to the very end.<strong>South African children who have enjoyed series like <em>Percy Jackson</em> and <em>Inkheart</em> should enjoy Amanda Hocking\u2019s <em>Kanin Chronicles</em> and may connect too with the cross-cultural love interests and hierarchical relationships that play throughout.</strong>With characters that are strange enough to be different and yet, strangely familiar at the same time, an exciting new world and a gripping plot, there is no doubt as to why these books have sold so well.  <em>Frost Fire</em> may not win any literary prizes, but it is written with an unmistakable teenage voice and provides a wonderful introduction to the fantasy genre that is sure to turn many a non-reader into a book lover.The story is easy to read and fascinating, the subject matter is new and fresh and the hooks are powerful enough to make this a read in one sitting. Young readers may well forgive the language hiccups as they are drawn into the story\u2026 I certainly did.<em>Nikki McDiarmid</em><strong>See The world of Amanda Hocking:</strong> http://www.worldofamandahocking.com/<hr/><img alt="Book Cover: Frost Fire" src="http://d39ttiideeq0ys.cloudfront.net/assets/images/book/large/9781/4472/9781447256649.jpg"/><h2>Review by Zo\xeb da Silva, aged 12</h2>The first book of this page-turning trilogy introduces readers to Bryn Aven whose life is filled with problems, both emotional and her bloodline and cultural differences. Frost fire begins with Bryn having to confront the fact the her fallen hero, Konstantin Black is an attempted murderer.  Together with her boss, Ridley (who she is secretly in love with) Bryn must bring Konstantin Black and his partner Viktor Dalig to justice, and yet\u2026something just doesn\u2019t seem right about it.  What is Bryn missing?<strong>This is a real \u2018CPD\u2019 book!  (A \u2018can\u2019t-put-it-down\u2019 book!)</strong>The cover of this book shows Bryn as a girl with beauty and elegance, but also with an air of power and strength as she stands against the background of a cold and forested North America, the land in which they live.I absolutely loved this book!  It is an exciting story with everything in it - moments of anger, sadness, humour and down-right sarcasm. In fact, this is one of my favorite areas of <strong>Amanda Hocking\u2019s</strong> writing \u2013 that her characters are so sarcastic and funny.The entire trilogy is to be praised for the storyline, characters and, in a way that I think mostly is ignored, the way the sentences are strung together that they read as easily as water flows. Any reader who has enjoyed Harry Potter or the Divergent series will fall in love with this trilogy. I know this will be a book I will read over and over again...Girls of 12-16 would enjoy this book just as much as I have, I\u2019m sure.                 12/11/2015 10:35:49 AM\r                            2/8/2016 11:52:00 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews SOUTH AFRICAN ANIMALS  by Lindiwe Mabuza\xa9 2016

<strong><em>South African Animals</em> is a paper-back alphabet book about animals found in South Africa.</strong> <img alt="Book Cover: South African Animals, by Lindiwe Mabuza" src="http://www.randomstruik.co.za/bookTitles/9781870516853.jpg"/>From A \u2013 Z children meet the Aardvark, Dolphin, Flycatcher, Millipede, Night Adder, Tree Dassie and Zebra, in this beautifully and elaborately illustrated book. So our approach in reading this book was for Yamile to first read a page on an animal and then I would read on the same animal in the index - this was a more engaging approach for her.</em>)<strong><em>South African Animals</em> tells us more about animals in South Africa.</strong>Whilst I liked the pictures, I particularly enjoyed the interesting facts about the animals provided at the end of the book. Each page, beautifully illustrated with an animal or two, provides for a satisfying visual experience. One or two animals written in the vernacular such as the Umsumpe (Zulu name for Red Duiker) and Xhama (Xhosa name for Red Hartebeest), as well as the beautiful illustration of an African girl on the cover page, will appeal to a South African child. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews "How Carbon Footprints Work"\xa9 2016

<strong>The concept of carbon footprints is a rather abstract subject, especially for younger children.</strong><img alt="Book Cover: How Carbon Footprints Work" src="https://www.hachettechildrens.co.uk/assets/HachetteChildrensBooks/img/book/074/isbn9781445139074-detail.jpg"/>As the CAPS curriculum introduces oxygen and carbon dioxide within the photosynthesis cycle from Grade 4, we were interested in how Grade 5\u2019s would deal with this information.<strong>Eco Works</strong> likens carbon pathways to footprints in the sand and then continues in some detail, discussing carbon emissions, the increase in Green House Gases, rising temperatures and their effects on nature.Children are taught the process of calculating their carbon use; preserving trees as carbon cushions and living in ways that can reduce their footprint, both in shopping habits and in their own homes. In conclusion there is a chapter dedicated to carbon trading and offsetting, future trends and decisions in which children themselves can have an impact on change.Photographic images are offset by rainbow-coloured bubbles filled with text, brightly designed for younger children.  The layout does, however, seem a rather strange combination of elements and there were doubts at how well it would be received.<strong>The Grade 5 students took great interest in this book.</strong>The information was relevant to what they were learning at school and they grasped far more than parents had expected. In all cases, it was the children who did the reading and the parents who listened and explained the difficult concepts.The text is a good introduction to words and phrases of the future, where language is constantly evolving as science changes the world we live in, and a glossary page at the back will have children and parents learning together.One youngster who reads only fiction commented on how much he enjoyed the non-fictional aspect of this book, while another mentioned his joy at being able to discuss what he was reading with his parents.  Four weeks later, we continued to point carbon footprints out to our son and refer back to the book, picking up on extra details and reading further on.<img alt="Page insert: example of the layout" src="https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/-ZreoGBhF1I4/Vk13XcI5dSI/AAAAAAAAAro/NM6ws1MSZo4/w346-h195/20150927_084922.jpg"/><strong>Mich\xe8 (11yrs), an avid reader of the <em>Guinness Book of Records</em>, said</strong>\u201c<em>This is a good book to read about Carbon Footprints. It is an easy read for Grade 5 and it was interesting to learn about carbon emissions. The book did not explain Green House Gases well (GHGs) and I had to find this out by using the Glossary. The book had good pictures and interesting topics and I think children from the ages of 8 to 15 years would like it.</em>"<strong>Miche\u2019s Mum felt otherwise, saying</strong>"<em>He actually got bored about half way through, from trying to get through all of the information. And you know how he loves facts. I read a bit of it and thought it was not so clear and concise. In fact, I found it was rather tedious.</em>"<strong>Chris (11yrs) said</strong>,"<em>I like this book.  I didn\u2019t know anything about carbon footprints, but the book tells you about how this happens.  There is a lot of information though, so I stopped after some pages and will have to read through it again to really understand. It helped me to look at my own carbon footprint and it has got my family talking about what we can each do to make things better. I read this book with my dad because he likes scientific things and we talked about this together.</em>"<em>The cover is strange as it doesn\u2019t really show you about carbon footprints and children will probably think this is a car book. The cover is not so attractive, but the title is very noticeable and that\u2019s what caught my attention.</em><em>The most interesting thing I learnt so far was that the extra carbon dioxide in the air affects water and it even kills the corals, because then there is no oxygen in the water.</em>"<strong>Chris's Dad was impressed with the way his son had interacted with the book.</strong>"<em>It's an educational book that is very accurate.  I think it's a good book, but we're not done with it yet</em>."This is not a quick read, nor a book that young readers will flit through. Children will take what they understand from the pages within and will return to read it again and again as they grow up with the information.We were most impressed at the excitement that <em>How Carbon Footprints Work</em> caused.<em>Nikki McDiarmid</em>                11/19/2015 7:38:08 AM\r                            11/19/2015 7:49:33 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku's young reader reviews  'The Journey that's Ours'. \xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: The Journey that's Ours " src="http://www.calminstorm.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/03/journey-that-ours.jpg"/><strong>Puku reviewer, Zo\xeb da Silva's first response to <em>The Journey that's Ours</em> was,</strong> <strong>"Wow!"</strong><strong><em>The Journey that's Ours</em> is about a brother and a sister whose lives couldn't be MORE different. Jina's life is great, she is determined to succeed and she has a crush on someone special, but her brother's life just isn't the same after he took a tumble in the sea...</strong><strong>Until 'Magic', the 'genie', visits them both with some wise words.</strong> This book looks like a typical self-esteem booster, but it actually has a proper story to it. Sometimes you can be doing well in your own life and everything just seems to go your way, but there are other times when nothing goes your way, and life seems as if it will never be okay again.The exercises at the back of the book are really awesome and make a lot of sense. They help with calming and the visualization of goals. (I loved the way the author sneakily added in how to make a mind map.)Some of these help you to realize what you really should be grateful for, and how to believe in yourself more. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">More about Puku's World AIDS Day book, 'Brenda has a Dragon in her Blood".\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book cover: Brenda has a dragon in her blood." src="http://d.gr-assets.com/books/1212493392l/3380530.jpg"/><strong>All over the world, people have misconceptions about how someone contracts HIV or AIDS from someone who has been infected \u2013 like thinking that it is not safe to drink something from the same glass as someone else. Most healthy people would rather stay away from someone with HIV or AIDS and don\u2019t realize how very hurtful this attitude is for that person.</strong> <strong>It is definitely not necessary to avoid contact.</strong>You cannot get AIDS by swimming in the same pool as someone else or by drinking out of the same glass or by taking a pinch of sugar from the same sugar-bowl. This book is intended firstly to support those children (and adults) with HIV and AIDS, in the hope that the prejudices about this disease will disappear. Both the information in this little book and Brenda\u2019s story make this possible. Although Brenda lives in the Netherlands, there are many children in many countries, also in our country, who suffer from the same sickness.<strong>A story from \u201creal life\u201d</strong>What is it like for a child to have AIDS?What problems does he or she face? And what can people in the child\u2019s circle do to help him or her?<em>Brenda Has a Dragon in her Blood</em> tries to explain to children what it means to be HIV positive at a level they can understand. <strong>But, "Who is Brenda?" you may ask.</strong>Brenda Mugabona was three-and-a-half years old when this book was written and she is now thirteen. She wrote this letter:<strong>Dear all,</strong><strong>My name is Brenda Mugabona. I am Brenda from the book <em>Brenda has a Dragon in her Blood</em>. I am a regular girl and I am doing fine, except for the fact that I have AIDS. You can read about that in the book.</strong><img alt="Photo: Brenda Mugabona" src="https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/-jn_rIQmig4Q/Vl_7L6-M05I/AAAAAAAAAtk/ZX6aoXRaiTI/w240-h320-no/Brenda.jpg"/><strong>I would like to say how happy I am now <em>Brenda has a Dragon in her Blood</em> has been translated in so many South African languages. Now many children and grown-ups as well can read it.</strong> <strong>I am very happy my (foster)mother Hijltje wrote this book as it has helped children in the Netherlands - where I live now - and in so many other countries around the world to talk about HIV/AIDS.</strong><strong>The book explains what AIDS is and that you don\u2019t need to be scared to get AIDS when you drink from the same cup. Or lick the same lollypop. It explains you can hug us and love us and play with us.</strong> <strong>Especially that.</strong> <strong>Everybody should know that. Even the South African President should know about that, so give him a copy of the book, too. And give one to Nelson Mandela. I think he is very brave and his son died because of AIDS, right? Just like my mother, you can read about that in the book.</strong><strong>I also hope many medicines will become available for the South African people.</strong><strong>I don\u2019t know what else to write.</strong><strong>God bless you all.</strong> <strong>Love, Brenda</strong><strong>P.S. My mother Hijltje also sends her best wishes!</strong><img alt="Logo: Biblionef" src="http://www.dgmt-community.co.za/sites/dgmt/files/styles/organisation_logo/public/organisation_logos/biblionef.jpg?itok=q0iyTyPf"/>Says Hijltje Vink,<em>I dream of a world where people are no longer discriminated against because they are brown, yellow or red. Or because they have AIDS, or are poor or they are disabled.</em>If you'd like a copy of this book please contact <a href="http://biblionefsa.org.za/">Biblionef directly. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews South African YA book, 'Granite'.\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: 'Granite' by Jenny Robson" src="http://static.raru.co.za/cover/2015/03/06/2526374-l.jpg?v=1425634098"/><strong><em>"Mokomba\u2019s words held beauty and dignity, such as I have never heard.</em></strong><strong><em>Not even in the tales of the Storykeepers. And it was as if, in the dim shadows of our room, the spirits of his family were present and listening too.</em></strong><strong><em>And what they heard quieted them and gave them peace."</em></strong><hr/><em>Granite</em> is an engaging, page-turning and emotion-stirring historical tale of the tragic downfall of a great ancient city, Zimba Remabwe, and is Jenny Robson\u2019s twelfth novel for young readers.<strong>Zimba Remabwe \u2013 uniquely and solidly built with mortarless granite stones \u2013 lies silent and forsaken.</strong>It is around the year 1440 AD and few people have survived Zimba Remabwe\u2019s destruction. Among the survivors are two men \u2013 Mokomba, the son of the late Redombo, head of the Stonemason Clan and Shafiq the Arab, a dear friend of Redombo\u2019s family. They have left the ruins of Zimba Remabwe and are waiting in Sofala, to set sail for Egypt.As they await the ship, Shafiq encourages a severely traumatised Mokomba to share his account of what took place in Zimba Remabwe. Shafiq wants the story recorded and remembered, and though storytelling does not come naturally to Mokomba, he is determined to tell the full story despite the pain, because he is the only person left who can.The King of the great city wants to build \u2018a cathedral that reaches the clouds\u2019 - like the one he's heard about from Shafiq\u2019s stories of the 'Milk people'. The people from the land of the Crusaders. The King's decree,  though unsettling and undesirable to the those who serve him, results in a team being sent to the far-off land of the Crusaders. The trip, many moons long and filled with woe, is successful and they all return to the great city. <strong>It is here that disaster strikes Zimba Remabwe.</strong> Will Mokomba's retelling of his painful story be too much for him, or will he find peace through his memories? Will he be able to leave his homeland, or find the strength to stay?<em>Granite</em> is a beautiful, sad and well-researched, ancient story, with several themes weaved together.  Each is relevant, moving and enlightening for today's readers. The intrinsic human need to belong and have a place to call home is clearly revealed, as is the appreciation of cultural similarities and differences between the races that come together in this central African city. Evident too is the value of storytelling and the recording of these stories, alongside the gift of friendship. Granite is narrated in a way that makes the story come alive for readers, the language representative of the era in which the story is set, but expressed in simple English for teenagers to comfortably read. <strong>Filled with suspense, Jenny Robson keeps the reader turning the pages to find out what is coming next.</strong><em>Granite</em> is well-researched and has close links to the historical and ancient city of Great Zimbabwe, from which the nation of Zimbabwe derives its name.The only slight dip to this well-written tale was that it felt like the story climaxed too soon. I wanted to read more about the journey to the land of the Crusaders, but other than that the conflict progresses naturally and is smoothly resolved. The story, though tragic, left me feeling quietly satisfied and introspective.I highly recommend this book for anyone who is a teenager and older... adults included! Although many an African and non-African will connect with <em>Granite\u2019s</em> story, I suspect a person of Zimbabwean descent will find it a notch more special.<em>Review by Rujeko Moyo</em>                12/3/2015 4:38:09 PM\r                            12/3/2015 4:38:09 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Hierdie boekie is 'n moet-lees vir die tyd waarin ons leef\xa9 2016

Hoe om jong kinders in te lig oor die MIV-virus en VIGS kan ouers behoorlik laat kopkrap. \u2018n Mens se kinders kom daagliks met ander kinders, wat MIV-positief is, in aanraking. Hoe kan ons hulle hiervan bewus  maak sonder om hulle bang te maak of vooroordele te skep?<br> Met <em>Brenda het \u2018n drakie in haar bloed</em>, los <strong>H\xffltje Vink</strong> hierdie probleem netjies op. Sy vertel die ware verhaal van Brenda \u2013 net drie jaartjies oud \u2013 wat reeds haar ma aan die gevreesde siekte afgestaan het en nou by haar en haar gesin in Nederland woon.<br> Brenda is \u2018n vrolike bruin dogtertjie, maar sy het \u2018n MIV-virusdrakie wat in haar bloed bly. Solank Brenda medisyne drink wat die drakie laat slaap, bly sy perdfris en gesond. Maar MIV-drakies is stoute goed en as hulle wakker is, begin hulle veg teen die soldaatjies in Brenda se bloed wat haar beskerm. Dan voel sy moeg en koorsig en speel is nie meer lekker nie. Dan soek sy net drukkies en stories van mamma.<br> Wanneer die geveg te lank aanhou, begin die soldaatjies moeg word. Dan begin die drakie wen en as dit gebeur, kan jy doodgaan \u2013 soos wat met Brenda se eie mamma, Mary, gebeur het.<br> Daarom is ander kinders soms bang vir Brenda se drakie en dan wil hulle nie met haar speel nie. Hulle is bang die drakie kom uit en kruip in hulle bloed in. Dit maak Brenda baie hartseer, selfs hartseerder as toe mamma Mary dood is.Dwarsdeur die boekie beklemtoon die skrywer die feit dat Brenda \u2018n doodgewone dogtertjie is. Soos alle kinders hou sy van speel, hardloop, teken, en drukkies en soentjies. Sy hou van maats saam met wie sy \u2018n lekseltjie suiker uit die pot kan steel en wat saam met  haar in haar bedjie kan slaap.Sonder om \u2018n bangmaakding daarvan te maak, wys <strong>H\xffltje Vink</strong> op wat gedoen en nie gedoen mag word nie. Drukkies is in die haak, uit dieselfde glas koeldrank drink is fyn. Maar wanneer Brenda seerkry en daar is bloed, moet \u2018n mens versigtig wees. Dan plak jy \u2018n pleister op die seerplek en als is weer reg. Die skrywer beklemtoon ook die belangrikheid van medikasie en gereelde hospitaalbesoeke om seker te maak die drakie bly vas aan die slaap.<br>Linda Rode se Afrikaanse vertaling uit die Nederlands is in die kol. Diny van de Lustgraaf se illustrasies is te dierbaar en plaas \u2018n mens onmiddellik midde-in \u2018n vrolike, warm, deurmekaar huis vol kinders en diere wat lustig speel. En ma en pa speel net so lekker saam. Die nare klein draak is oral te bespeur: opgekrul langs Brenda; tussen die skoene op die vloer, of vas aan die slaap op Brenda se rug. Wanneer sy siek is, sit hy ewe kordaat op haar bed.<em>Brenda het \u2018n drakie in haar bloed</em> word sterk aanbeveel vir enige ouer wat hierdie kwessie aan hulle kinders wil verduidelik, en hoewel dit gerig is op klein kinders sal ook ouer kinders baat by hierdie boekie. Agter in is daar bykomende inligting en die nommers van organisasies wat mense kan help wat met MIV en VIGS leef. Dis \u2018n absolute moet-lees vir die tyd waarin ons leef.<br>Resensie: Liby Nel</br></br></br></br></br></br>                12/8/2015 8:40:28 AM\r                            12/8/2015 8:40:28 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku Reviews Christa Laird's The dangerous dream of Ben Maludzi\xa9 2016

Fifteen year-old Ben Maludzi has an ambition that sets him apart from the rest of Khayelitsha, the poor South African township where he lives: When his favourite teacher encourages him to apply for a scholarship at a private school, offered to underprivileged, intelligent students, he hopes more than anything that he is chosen to attend. Maybe then he\u2019ll improve his chances of helping to find a cure for the disease that caused his mother\u2019s death. And maybe then he\u2019ll have the opportunity to honour his deceased relatives by continuing their struggle for a better life for the people of South Africa.But Ben\u2019s community has other ideas in mind for him. His uncle is convinced that Ben\u2019s schooling is unimportant because his future lies in his uncle\u2019s tyre and motor parts business. And a gang of boys, whose members used to be his friends, are threatening him to join their illegal cell phone dealings. Suddenly Ben\u2019s safety, as well as the safety of his younger sister, is at risk, and he is forced to make an impossible decision.This well-written drama is alive with the joys and uncertainties of a modern township teenager. It tells of South African township life in realistic detail, evoking the warmth of Xhosa traditions as well as the harsh realities of living with poverty, crime and the threat of fatal disease.At times Laird is meticulous in less significant bits of the story, while she skimps on more important details. However, she effectively takes the reader on a moving journey, from moments of celebration to moments that are unbearably tense. The result is a captivating narrative, demonstrating the benefits of optimism, for young adult South African readers of all classes and cultures.                5/14/2013 7:17:48 AM\r                            5/14/2013 7:17:48 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews the sensual "A Song for Ella Grey" by David Almond\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: A Song for Ella Grey " src="http://ecx.images-amazon.com/images/I/61FRAlUBMlL._SY344_BO1,204,203,200_.jpg"/><strong>The striking cover of David Almond's, <em>A Song for Ella Grey</em> draws readers into an artistic and creative story of magic, illusion, love and mythology.</strong>It is late spring, the temperatures are ambling into summer with beach parties, carefree days and youthful romance.  A sketched illustration instantly places the reader on the sand dunes, as two girls Ella and Claire are introduced, a whisper in the inflections that there is more to their relationship than just close friendship.Ella is beautiful and obedient, the perfect child, from a home where she is trapped and her life is confined and ordered.  Claire is the opposite, her home a unit of stability and love, her ideals simple and her love honest - an anchor to Ella\u2019s intensity.  It is Claire who tells Ella\u2019s story: \u201c<em>At 17 what does Ella know of life?</em>\u201dUntil the arrival of Orpheus.  Once Ella hears his song, she is lost to him forever, leaving Claire to watch as Ella is taken further and further away from her. Split into five parts, this is the modern day story of Orpheus, the musician whom Apollo, the Greek God of music, blessed with a golden lyre.  <strong>David Almond</strong>, the master of storytelling, weaves his words into a rhythmic and sensual tale of \u201c<em>those who walk the earth with the glow of the gods already upon them, drawing people and magic towards them, but often getting hurt in the process</em>\u2026\u201dLead to question the layers of their own lives, modern teens will enjoy the different layers of belief structures that shift throughout the story, watching the harmonies and discord of legend and religion, love within pain, music versing silence and life as always, partnering with death.<strong>For it is teenagers who search for the song of life...</strong>And yet, this is a strange tale, steeped in the atmosphere of North-East England and one that lies far from the lives of South African children.  Intriguing and thought-provoking, there is always a sense of the sinister and the story is never exactly what it seems.  It is bizarre, yet fascinating, but will it hold the interest of South African children to the very last page?<em>A Song for Ella Grey</em> is a great read - an ode to the sweetest love, reminding us all that even in the darkness, it is love that brings us home.<em>Nikki McDiarmid</em>                12/18/2015 10:52:55 AM\r                            12/18/2015 10:58:57 AM\r
