[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku Reviews The Mighty Elephant in the Land of Kachoo\xa9 2016

<em>Puku's Nikki McDiarmid reviews The Mighty Elephant in the Land of Kachoo</em>Written by <strong>Tina Scotford</strong>, the rhyming verse of <em>The Mighty Elephant in the Land of Kachoo</em> holds children enthralled as the lumbering elephant breaks down trees on the savanna, in the forests and the woodlands.  Every time the Elephant does this, he ruins the homes and dwellings of smaller creatures that live there and he becomes increasingly unpopular.  Soon, as fire breaks out in the bush, the smaller animals realise that there is no-one better equipped than the Elephant to help in such a situation.The mighty elephant of Kachoo is, at first, overshadowed by the importance of trees and the homes they provide.  He waits patiently for recognition as other creatures are brought to the fore - rock dassies, monkeys, banana bats, Marabou Storks and Black Sparrow Hawks, just to name a few. And yet, Elephant is the main character, holding the story together.Big animals versus small ones is a predominant theme, and so too, is the importance of different individuals living in harmony with each other: the lesson is that each creature is important in the Land of Kachoo.Illustrated by Frans Groenewald, the glossy pages are set out on ever-changing canvases, decorated with delightfully amusing cartoons.  The contrasting backgrounds are hues that remain true to Africa, vibrant, but still realistic, reminding readers of startling blue, winter skies; vivid, orange terracotta\u2019s of African soil and murky khaki-green waters. The characters have the most delicious expressions - chuckling crocodiles and surly baboons roaming alongside the dopey Elephant who is innocently out to enjoy the sun as the pages turn.These guys bring in the South Africanisms, using words like \u201ckaboosh!\u201d and \u201cvoetsek\u201d, along with colloquial bush signs, creating an adventure that children cannot get enough of.Added to the back (and the first thing my son noticed) is a page of stickers, making the book a truly interactive experience, as well as a story that becomes uniquely personal.  And, isn\u2019t that the point, now that there is a uniquely South African children\u2019s book to call our own.With an insatiable desire for stories about their own environment, South African children will find the Kachoo series a wonderful way to begin exploring this gap. Wonderfully catchy \u2013 and informative -  families all over the world will find <em>The Mighty Elephant in the Land of Kachoo</em> a joy to read, just as we did.                8/12/2013 7:35:05 AM\r                            8/12/2013 7:35:05 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews YA short story collection, Big Ups!\xa9 2016

<em>Puku's Bontle Senne reviews FunDza Literary Trust\u2019s Big Ups! story anthology.</em>Big Ups! is an anthology of short stories sourced from FunDza\u2019s mobile platform. Every week, thousands of teens around the country read the seriliased novels and short stories that FunDza publishes on its site and with the publication of Big Ups! some of these stories can now be enjoyed in print format. The title Big Ups! comes from the FunDza Fanz, who regularly post the comment \u2018Big Ups to the Author!\u2019 after reading a short stories on their mobile phones.<img alt="enter image description here" src="http://www.fundza.co.za/wp-content/uploads/2013/05/Bigups-instagram-300x300.jpg"/>The book is definitely not what local YA readers are used to. For a start, it\u2019s a look at the real South Africa. The characters are representative of real teens and the real, uncomfortable challenges they face. These stories do not always make it into the mainstream local or international YA market so Big Ups! is a breath of fresh air. What I enjoyed most about the stories was that while they were all about ordinary South African teenagers living in townships, suburbs or villages, each had its own twists and turns to keep you guessing. From \u2018Courage Like a Lion\u2019 about a boy trying to overcome much more than just his fear of train-surfing to \u2018Secret Enemy\u2019, a story about the dark side of technology, each story had a unique perspective. The only thing they have in common is that none of them get caught up in trying to teach a moral or educate on a social ill. Instead, the story itself and the joy of reading it is the focus.Big Ups! features an impressive array of authors including Jenny Robson, Tracey Farren, Cynthia Jele, Lauri Kubuitsile and newcomer Sonwabiso Ngcowa. Being able to draw such a talented ensemble of authors is part of what has driven the success of FunDza\u2019s mobile site and hopefully part of what will draw readers into this book. It\u2019s a fun and quick read, with stories so authentic and sometimes heartbreaking, that stay with you for days. And maybe, just maybe, Big Ups! is the start of a real reading revolution for teens in our country too.                8/13/2013 12:02:26 PM\r                            8/13/2013 12:03:24 PM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews Saving the Rhino in the Land of Kachoo\xa9 2016

Any story about the African Rhino is bound to be emotional, yet together <strong>Tina Scotford</strong> and Frans Groenewald (illustrator) create a story that is sweet and gentle, while still driving home the message that poaching is unacceptable.A poacher sneaks into the land of Kachoo after hearing of the birth of twin rhinos.  One has been endowed with a large horn and the poacher wishes to hunt it and become rich.  He lives in a cave, shoots with a bow and arrow (rather than a gun) and chews gum that he spits into the bush.  He is disrespectful and really, not a nice character.When faced by the Big Five and the Little Five together, the poacher appears rather feeble and his evil will to kill is nipped in the bud, to say the least.One of the great delights of the Kachoo stories is the inclusion of African animals that children seldom get to hear about.  The Big Five are commonly known  - Elephant, Lion, Buffalo, Leopard and of course, the Rhinoceros.But, in this book, the Little Five are cunningly added to the story with the additions of the Elephant Shrew, Ant Lion, Buffalo Weaver, Leopard Tortoise and Rhinoceros Beetle. The Secretary Bird gathers the troops.  The Big Five are rather predictable in their plans to scare the poacher away, while the Little Five are far more subtle and carefully woven into the fabric of this tale.  In Kachoo, all the animals work together, each vitally important in their own way and the \u2018Big versus Little\u2019 theme of Kachoo is right at the heart of this story.The Poacher is played off brilliantly against the residents of the bushveld, his stupidity making the reader ask who it is that really does have the brains in this situation?Frans Groenewald\u2019s drawings delight young readers and adults alike.  A favourite page in this book, was for us, the cave where the Poacher \u2018camps \u2013 out\u2019.  Wonderfully South African, a Cadac gas bottle stands with an aluminium pot upon it and a \u201cDefending the Caveman\u201d poster is stuck onto the wall next to an ancient San painting.Amusing, and a great deal of fun, the story ends (as the books of Kachoo do) with a page of Groenewald stickers, and with emotions running high on this topic, I think I know exactly where my son is going to stick his extra arrows!                8/26/2013 10:27:32 AM\r                            8/26/2013 10:27:32 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews The Leopard and Bushbaby in the land of Kachoo\xa9 2016

<img alt="leopard bushbaby, buck" src="https://fbcdn-sphotos-h-a.akamaihd.net/hphotos-ak-prn1/558679_241482395991822_1504966833_n.jpg"/>Many Africans live with the incredible Bushbaby, or Nagaap, and yet few have seen one in the wild.  One of the cutest residents by far, <em>Tina Scotford</em> and <em>Frans Groenewald</em> introduce nocturnal animals in this Kachoo tale.Night has fallen and Bushbaby can\u2019t sleep.  As he clambers through the trees, a branch accidently falls and spikes a Bushpig.  Luckily, Bushpig is far too thick-skinned to let it worry him and he\u2019d much rather play with his new night-friend.  Bushbaby then stubs his toe on a branch that hits Bushbuck on the head and gets stuck in his horns. Instead of getting thorny, the three become fast friends and disappear into the night to play in the bush.Leopard, a pirate of a carnivore, appears in the darkness as the three friends accidentally stumble into his path.  Bushbaby has to do some fast thinking to get them out of trouble, so, using the string of accidents and mistakes that got them there in the first place, he finds the tools to save them all from trouble.Now familiar with the land of Kachoo\u2019s changing canvases, the question was in seeing how the night theme would be coloured.  A mix of tertiary colours in khaki\u2019s, purples and blues, create a subdued feel of darkness, without taking away from the vibrant colours of Africa and the fun of Kachoo.As a picture book aimed at younger children, I was impressed to note that this Kachoo story remains a challenge for older readers who read out loud.The font helps children to visualise the language in a different format, while the rhyming verse keeps little tongues limber.  Challenging words had primary school readers tripping over the \u2018a la carte\u2019 menu and the \u2018bush buffet\u2019, as well as learning larger words like \u2018unbeknown\u2019 and \u2018sauntered\u2019.I personally missed the addition of South Africanisms in <em>Frans Groenewald\u2019s</em> drawings, but found this to be a far more accessible story for children worldwide.Not only was this tale delightfully amusing, but research continued online, long after the pages were closed.  I would suggest this book for children of all ages.                9/20/2013 6:21:19 AM\r                            9/20/2013 7:49:01 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU's Mary Sadler-Altena reviews Permanente Ink\xa9 2016

Hierdie is die resep vir 'n spannende krimi met al die regte bestanddele.  \u2018n Reeksmoordenaar wat hom toel\xea op verliefde tieners is doenig in Kaapstad se omgewing, en dis duidelik uit die manier waarop die jong slagoffers l\xea as hulle gevind word, dat dit 'n kranksinnige se werk is. Drie paartjies is al vermoor en volgens die aangeduide patroon bereken die polisie dat die vierde binne die eersvolgende week gaan volg.In hierdie gespanne atmosfeer word vier graad-elfers, die enfants terribles van die Ho\xebrskool Duiwelspiek, deur die hoof  aanges\xea om as straf vir hul slegte gedrag \u2018n ou vervalle gebou wat afgesonder en leeg op \u2018n uithoek van die skoolgronde staan, skoon te maak. Die gebou waarin jare terug \u2018n gesinsmoord gepleeg is en nou die sinistere agtergrondtoneel raak vir die storie se klimaks en ontknoping.Die vier is nie maats nie, inteendeel, hulle beskou mekaar as weirdos en het niks in gemeen nie behalwe \u2018n weersin in die skoolstelsel en disfunksionele ouers. Tog, met \u2018n bietjie hulp van die moordenaar, kry twee van hulle in die loop van die verhaal die hots vir mekaar om sodoende die intrige te regverdig. Hoewel die boek lekker en gemaklik lees, wonder ek op watter ouderdomsgroep dit gemik is. Die karakters is in graad elf, dus sestien, sewentien jaar oud - maar in die regte lewe lees daardie jongmense reeds Meyer, Mackenzie, Patterson en Reichs, om maar \u2018n paar te noem. Dus is dit bedoel vir jongeres, s\xea maar kinders van 12 of 13? Die re\xebls van kinderlektuur bepaal egter dat sulke lesers daarop moet kan staatmaak dat, in hierdie spesifieke geval, die tiener-karakters self die moordenaar aan die man bring, en nie slegs as katalisator dien vir polisie-optrede nie. Terselfdertyd is die slordige taalgebruik nie \u2018n goeie voorbeeld vir jong kinders wat nog \u2018n woordeskat moet opbou nie. Vir my is dit \u2018n baie oppervlakkige boek. Nie een van die karakters kom tot sy reg nie, wat jammer is, want daar is pragtige ontwikkelingspotensiaal in veral die meisie, Zelda. Ek aanvaar dat formaatbeperkings vir jeugromans grotendeels skuld hieraan het, maar voel terselfdertyd dat \u2018n gesoute skrywer soos Diedericks-Hugo die nodige aanpassings moet kan maak.Ek het meer verwag van hierdie boek, veral omdat dit aangegee word as die naaswenner van die uitgewers se jeugroman-kompetisie.Mary Sadler-Altena                9/16/2013 9:55:43 AM\r                            9/16/2013 9:55:43 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews Arabella, the Moon and the Magic Mongongo Nut for young readers.\xa9 2016

<strong>Hamilton Wende\u2019s</strong> fantasy is centered around a young girl who rediscovers her life through insects, garden creatures and magical suburban happenings.Arabella has just turned eleven years old and to celebrate, her Grandparents take her to buy a watch at the local clock shop.  Once there, Arabella notices a dusty Grandfather clock and learns that the timepiece runs on \u2018Moon Time\u2019 and is handed a \u2018moon key\u2019 as a special gift.  Sadly, the outing and the key are soon forgotten as  Arabella\u2019s father dies not long after.Strange things happen in the days that follow - an eagle crashes through Arabella\u2019s bedroom window late at night and she meets a \u2018mielie lady\u2019 who seems to know her.  A baby monkey passes her a Kalahari Mongongo nut without explaining why and the garden begins to look different overnight. Before she knows it, Arabella\u2019s life has changed.Creatures around her are given voices and the magical Mongongo Tree grows only in the moonlight.  Arabella is transformed into a butterfly and sent on an adventure to save the Earth.The chapter on parktown prawns is brilliant, not only incredibly amusing, but delightfully awful at the same time.  The thought of these creatures ruling our world is enough to make most shudder, but Arabella\u2019s sensitivity is charming.The battle with Ozymandias builds up to some superb tension on top of the Hillbrow tower and brings with it a wonderful twist to the story.  Hadeda birds - the bad guys - will never be looked at in the same way again.This story starts slowly, for just as the reader is getting to know Arabella and her world of magic, the intrigue is halted as the girl faces her father's death.  When the magic reappears, the excitement is somewhat anti-climactic and takes a while to build up again, making the story a little disjointed for young readers.  However, once the magic begins flowing, the story does too.Parents should be warned that this story is for tweens and deals with death and grief.  It should be appropriately assessed for sensitive readers who may feel unsettled by the chapters relating to a parent dying.References to Arabella being an only child and dealing with grief \u2018alone\u2019 were a tad worrying. The implication that single children can only be happy if they have siblings.  As many single children are quite comfortable in their own company, the concern is that these children will question their status when they\u2019ve never had need to before.With many characters to empathise with, and still more to discover, Arabella is sure to lead our youth on a tale of discovery and courage as they search their own lives, and gardens, for magical signs.                9/18/2013 7:33:53 AM\r                            9/18/2013 7:33:53 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU's Madelein du Toit reviews The Guinness World Records 2014\xa9 2016

My first reaction to the launch of <em>Guinness World Records 2014</em> was an excited \u201cOh yeah!\u201d Is there any child or adult out there who has never (NEVER) wondered about the highest, tallest, fastest, strangest or weirdest aspect of the world and humankind? We are a wondrous species and there is nothing as amusing and awe inspiring as ourselves.<em>The Guinness Book of World Records</em> (as it was first known) has provided us with substantiated facts of both human achievements and the extremes of the natural world for more than 60 years. It has certainly earned its status of \u201cworld renowned brand\u201d and has sold over 120 million copies to date. And kudos to them for keeping up with technology: a website which boasts 1.25 million viewers annually, regular posts on YouTube and presently cell phone apps which enable augmented reality and 3D images. Impressive. It means you can view the book on a smartphone or a tablet \u2013 devices which have become everyday tools for even the youngest child.\u201c<em>See amazing record holders at 100% size, from the smallest snakes and the tiniest technology to the biggest body parts and the most massive mango</em>.\u201d I tested their blurb and was intrigued and stunned at images popping up or popping out, it all just made the whole experience \u201coh wow!\u201d and made me lose track of time completely! And remember, it is not all that simple to boast with a record in this book. The GBWR employ official adjudicators authorized to verify the setting and breaking of records before accepted for publication.Although there are formidable records achieved by humans in all spheres of life, I marvelled at the so called useless information. For example, that Mickey Mouse was the first fictional character on the Hollywood Walk of Fame? Did YOU know that? Or who in the world owns the largest collection of Star Wars memorabilia? The kind of knowledge that will intrigue all ages and most probably make you the hero of any general knowledge quiz!If your children are the scholarly type and enjoy more serious stuff such as the shortest river, the most poisonous plant, the heaviest tumour found in the human body \u2026 they will find all the facts here. Even poor readers will devour the pages of this book as the many facts and figures are sure to hold their attention.This book is suited to children and adults of all ages and with the added technological enhancements should once again, be a best seller!                9/20/2013 8:59:28 AM\r                            9/20/2013 8:59:28 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews 'Back to Villa Park' by Jenny Robson.\xa9 2016

<img alt="street in Joburg" src="http://images.kalahari.net/img/2013/04/22/47301082_0_Img2.jpg"/>Jenny Robson\u2019s <em>\u201cBack to Villa Park\u201d</em> touches the very depths of the Johannesburg soul.  Digging deep to where South Africans are most vulnerable, Robson sources the incredible courage that sparks this nation.Dirk Karel Strydom is eighteen and today is his birthday.  He is a white boy who works as a gardener for a black family and on this auspicious occasion, will attempt to break the mold by applying for a job at Kagiso Holdings.  However, Dirk ends up cheating and is thrown out of the interview.  He has no family around him and no-one special to tell.The story takes the reader on a trip through Johannesburg as Dirk seeks out friends to spend the day with.  Along the way, his memories keep him company and most of the plot is carried out in the past.Dirk\u2019s friends consist of a homeless couple, Aggies and Rosie, and a girl called Bethany who seems not to be a friend at all, while Mrs Mogwera, the lady whose property he lives on, is a friend Dirk has yet to discover.The paths of these characters intertwine in ways that leave the reader breathless, the depths of each unique personality utterly compelling.  Some are so awful that the reader feels sick to the stomach, while others show extreme kindness through pain so tangible, the reader can\u2019t help but feel it too.The paradox is uniquely South African, different cultures, separated by zoning and playing off varying price brackets and lifestyles. At first, reading <em>\u2018Back to Villa Park\u2019</em> is uncomfortable, the blatant racial slurs horribly confrontational and Dirk\u2019s life story, in all its difficulty, is compacted into the space of one day, twisting and turning from the past to the present.However, this story is sheer brilliance and must be read to the very end to be fully appreciated.With our children desperately hungry for South African stories, <em>\u2018Back to Villa Park\u2019</em> is not only a good read, but a journey of inspiration.  This book will change you.                9/25/2013 5:09:48 AM\r                            9/25/2013 5:16:58 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Madelein du Toit resenseer Karoo-Kantate\xa9 2016

Die titel van die boek het my gefassineer. Ek het nie geweet wat beteken \u2018kantate\u2019 nie, maar het besluit om nie die naaste woordeboek te gryp nie want ek was seker die betekenis sou weldra duidelik word. Ek was nie verkeerd nie. Jeanne Labuschagne is \u2018n 13-jarige bruin meisie met \u2018n passie vir musiek.  Haar ma herken haar musiektalent en ten midde van groot finansi\xeble uitdagings as alleen-ouer slaag sy daarin om aan haar dogter \u2018n musiek opleiding te besorg. \u2018n \u2018Hoenderpaai\u2019 elke Maandag en \u2018n melktert op die Vrydag is genoeg betaling vir se\u0148ora Pizetti wat die sonderlinge talent van die jong meisie raaksien en koester. Na haar ma se ontydige dood beland Jeanne in \u2018n weeshuis waar haar lewe \u2018n totaal ander rigting sou inslaan.Toe Jeanne (of Jannie Lappies \u2013 haar weeshuis bynaam) nie meer haar musieklesse kon byhou nie, het sy aangehou oefen, elke dag, \u201c\u2026 want ek het geblo ek sal, en ek sal nie ophou nie.\u201d<strong>Mari\xe9 Heese</strong> skryf warm en menslik. Die karakters en verwikkelinge om Jeanne se lewe het baie gou vir my lewe gekry. Hulle is mense mense, sonder tierlantyntjies en foefies. Ek kon so lekker identifiseer met die verhaal. \u201cBeter as tiewie\u201d \u2026 Jannie Lappies se denkbeeldige gesprekke met \u2018n pa wat sy nooit geken het nie, was vir my baie spesiaal. Soms het ek gelag oor die eenvoud daarvan en soms was ek net hartseer. Die lewe is hard, maar die lewe gee ook baie, die lewe is die lewe.Ek het baie gehou van die manier waarop die skrywer die hede en die verlede gebruik om die storielyn te bou. Net as jy begin wonder oor \u2018n spesifieke aspek in die verhaal dan word  dit opgeklaar, net om die pad oop te maak vir \u2018n volgende scenario. My belangstelling en konsentrasie was die heeltyd geprikkel. Die storie was miskien voorspelbaar, maar dit is die uitbeelding van die karakters wat die verhaal net so vervlaks innemend maak.Dit is veral tieners wat musiekliefhebbers is wat groter aanklank by <em>Karoo-Kantate</em> sal vind. Alhoewel terme soos koloratuur, leitmotiv en partituur vir my vreemd was, het dit nie gepla nie. Ek het dit bloot aanvaar as die taal van die musiekw\xeareld waarin die storie afspeel, ek kon nog steeds die storielyn volg. Maar, nuuskierige agie soos ek is, moes ek net eenvoudig die paar woorde opsoek \u2026<em>Karoo-Kantate</em> is \u2018n kaleidoskoop van die lewe en in hierdie tye waar die donker knaend neig om ons te oorskadu, was dit heerlik om deel te wees van die warm menswees van hierdie verhaal. <img alt="enter image description here" src="http://www.nb.co.za/Authors/HomePage/Marie%20Heese%20klein.JPG"/>(Mari\xe9 Heese skryf na twee dekades weer \u2018n Afrikaanse boek vir die jeug. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Madelein du Toit resenseer Die vierletterwoord \xa9 2016

Clarissa Mentz is in graad 11 in Palm Lane High, \u2018n eksklusiewe dubbelmedium skool. Anders as haar maats met ryk ouers, het \u2018n prestasie beurs en polisgeld haar toegang en onderrig by die skool verseker.Haar pa se verdwyning twee jaar gelede het \u2018n groot impak gemaak op die lewens van Clarissa en haar ma. Die feit dat sy \u2018n kranige atleet is wat dikwels die pad vat met tekkies en drafklere om haar vorm te behou, help baie. En as dinge te erg raak druk sy die iPod in haar ore sodat die harde musiek haar kop skoonkry.  As redakteur van die skoolkoerant word daar baie van haar tyd in beslag geneem en sy verkies dit om besig te wees. Dit alles help om die spoke van haar pa se unfinished business weg te dryf.Wanneer sy \u2018n sms vanaf haar vermiste pa se selfoon ontvang krap dit Clarissa se lewe van voor af om. Boonop is daar \u2018n nuwe Afrikaans-onderwyseres betrokke by die skoolkoerant wat besluit om \u2018n adjunk-redakteur aan te stel. Skielik voel haar posisie as redakteur wankelrig. En boonop sukkel sy nog om haar en Penny se Projek Hoofseun aan die gang te kry.  Dis met sulke tye dat haar pak sigarette en die koel bankie in die secret garden by hulle huis, haar derms \u2018n kans gee om te ontknoop. Vriende Penny en Duane het gesorg vir die humor in die verhaal. Soms het Penny se knaendheid en nuus aandra gepla,  maar dit is seker die regte eienskappe vir \u2018n ywerige joernalis. Ek het gehou van Clarissa se besef van karmic accounting, dat balans miskien die grootste rol speel in ons lewens. En as dinge skeefloop, sal dit weer regkom, this too, shall pass.<em>Die vierletterwoord</em> geskryf deur <strong>Nelia Engelbrecht</strong> is \u2018n moderne verhaal waarmee jongmense tussen 13 en 16 sal kan identifiseer.(Die boek is aanbeveel vir graad 10 tot 12 Addisionele Taal)                10/11/2013 7:48:21 AM\r                            10/11/2013 7:48:21 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews "Cheeky"\xa9 2016

<img alt="crocodile" src="http://images.kalahari.net/img/2011/11/04/41240162_0_Img1.jpg"/><strong>Leon de Villiers\u2019</strong> story about Cheeky the baby crocodile, is simple but so effective.Cheeky leaves his Mum to explore the forest, discovering a range of bush residents as he goes.  At first, the animals are gently curious, wanting to cuddle and hug the little crocodile.  Animal instincts kick in each time as Cheeky firmly informs them that it\u2019s his body and they cannot touch him.  Some of the creatures want to do more than just touch, as Cheeky soon finds out when he meets the sly leopard and the hungry jackal.The repetition of this story drives home the message that this is \u201c<em>my body and you need my permission to touch it</em>\u201d.Bodies are sacred and I loved that the simplicity of Cheeky\u2019s journey never took away from the forcefulness of his words.  Nor does the little crocodile waver in his constant repetition \u2013 not one animal is allowed to touch him, no matter how nice they are.  And, after one reading I found children already repeating the mantra and using it.While this tiny tale hits home hard, the book itself is charming and so beautifully illustrated by <strong>Alzette Prins</strong>.  Immediately, we recognized the different art used for the background as the techniques are those taught to children at school.  Wax resist, stencils, collage and crayon-colouring combine with watercolour washes and running paint effects to create pages filled with colour and pattern.The characters themselves are seriously cute and I\u2019m certain that while this story is a great tool for discussion, these pages will be flipped through again and again purely for their appeal.Cheeky is a book with simple words, incredible pictures and a powerful story.                10/21/2013 6:01:10 AM\r                            10/21/2013 6:01:10 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Sunday Times Storytime and Nal'ibali\xa9 2016

<img alt="kids reading" src="http://www.jetonline.co.za/FileAssets/Competitions/85/nalibali-comp-image.jpg"/><h2>Nikki McDiarmid reviews'Storytime'</h2>Beginning with <strong>\u201c<em>Ma Josie\u2019s Pig</em>\u201d</strong> by <strong>Wendy Hartmann</strong>, children meet an amusing creature who is able to eat an entire household. Young readers will discover how cruel he is to a neighbour\u2019s dog and the local donkey.  Soon, however, the animals lead Leje to an understanding that will transform him forever.<strong><em>\u201cLesedi solves a mystery\u201d</em></strong> by <strong>Kagiso Lesego Molope</strong> follows a young female detective in solving the case of the missing apples, while <strong><em>\u201cThe girl who went to find the Stars\u201d</em></strong> by <strong>Sarah Wild</strong> is about a young girl aspiring to be an astronaut.  Of course, once she\u2019s seen the stars there\u2019s nowhere Ndonsa would rather be than at home.A personal favourite was <strong><em>\u201cMr Hare meets Mr Mandela\u201d</em></strong> by <strong>Chris van Wyk</strong>, a story that highlights the importance of numbers and reading in education.<img alt="rabbit" src="http://nalibali.org/wp-content/themes/ninja/timthumb.php?src=http://nalibali.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/Mr-Hare2.jpeg&amp;w=674&amp;h=328"/>Not only are the stories magical, but the illustrations are superb.  This quality of art is what South Africans <em>should</em> be seeing in publications.  Vibrant, filled with colour and each so different to the next, these images are an essential part of our South African heritage.Illustrators such as <strong>Joan Rankin</strong> (<em>HAUM Daan Retief prize 1986 and Katrina Harris Award 1991</em>), <strong>Maja Sereda</strong> (<em>ATKV Awards and Crystal Kite member\u2019s choice  Award</em>) and <strong>Paddy Bouma</strong> are recognised immediately.  <strong>Val Myburgh</strong>, <strong>Shayle Bester</strong>, <strong>Theresa Acker</strong>, <strong>Frances Ringwood</strong>, <strong>Angie Bowring</strong> and <strong>Stephne Wood</strong> complete the list of incredible illustrators.  Children will adore these images and return again and again to see them.Hungry for stories that speak of home, this book will have South African children clapping their hands in delight.  From short rhyming verse, to longer and more involved tales, \u201cStorytime\u201d is guaranteed to catch the attention of children aged two years and up.                10/24/2013 7:11:51 AM\r                            10/24/2013 7:30:20 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews "Lost Worlds" by Andrew Lane\xa9 2016

<img alt="skull image" src="http://www.panmacmillan.com/devpanmacmillan/media/panmacmillan/Books/width220px/callum-challenger-1-lost-worlds-978144722799101.jpg"/>Best known for his series \u201c<strong><em>Young Sherlock Holmes</em></strong>\u201d, <strong>Andrew Lane</strong> now searches for lost worlds and the missing link in human evolution.Every child imagines the \u201cWhat if?\u201d question. In an apartment from which he cannot move, the sixteen year old must find out if this creature is real, for if it exists, the genetic DNA that has ensured its survival may be his last hope for a normal life. It seems these youngsters have nothing in common and yet their lives are drawn towards Calum Challenger. Never, in their wildest dreams, do these youngsters expect to stumble upon one of the world\u2019s greatest secrets, in a buildup of suspense and intrigue that is hard to put down.  This story has the reader thinking about the impossible and wishing it was possible.Some red herrings and a few hiccups with grammatical issues make the reader stumble, but they aren\u2019t enough to quell a really exciting tale.  There are pages that begin to get rather sinister, but the story is quickly resolved, making for great teen fiction. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU's Madelein du Toit reviews Monday evening, Thursday afternoon\xa9 2016

Louise van Rensburg is writing to her very best friend, Faheema Majait. The girls met on the first day of school in grade one and despite their different backgrounds, have come to know, accept and respect each other.Two international incidents have far reaching consequences for the two girls, now in grade eight. Bombings on the London Underground and an insensitive cartoon portrayal of the prophet Mohammed, cause their families to react in different ways.  The friendship of Louise and Faheema comes to an abrupt halt as their families cannot show tolerance or understanding of their different views of life. The girls may not see one another anymore.What follows is a heart wrenching tale of two soul mates trying to bridge the divide between their families. \u201cThat is why I have decided to write it all down, everything I remember of us being best friends.\u201d The calm voice of Louise as she tells her side of the story to her friend Faheema, works very well.  It is an innocent voice untainted by the ugliness of worldly intolerance. <em>Monday evening, Thursday afternoon</em> is a disturbing tale of man\u2019s unkindness to his fellow man. Louise and Faheema didn\u2019t really find it necessary to discuss the fundamental differences between them as \u201cThere were so many other things we needed to talk about, weren\u2019t there?\u201d  As time goes by Louise comes to see the differences of the worlds they grew up in. When Faheema tries on a new prayer scarf, her distraction with the binding of the material around her head astonishes Louise. It is a side of Faheema that she has never seen before and she does not know what to make of it.And Faheema? She doesn\u2019t know what to make of the world Louise lives in either. And herein lies the big challenge: to be tolerant of those worlds we do not know what to make of. To find common ground and acceptance of our differences.I thoroughly enjoyed <strong>Jenny Robson\u2019s</strong> novel. It is a thought provoking book that should be read by every teenager. And their parents.This novel was shortlisted for the MacMillan African Writers\u2019 Prize. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Madelein du Toit resenseer Die Land verby Donker\xa9 2016

<strong>Fran\xe7ois Bloemhoef</strong> is weer op sy stukke met <em>\u2018Die Land verby Donker\u2019</em>. Die groot oog gillende figuur op die voorblad is die eerste leidraad dat hierdie boekie vir dapper lesers bedoel is.Die begin is mak genoeg met \u2018n inleiding van die alfabet maar, die waarskuwing is daar, hierdie A en die B en die snaakse C gaan jou \u201cplesierig bang\u201d maak! Ek het gevoel seuns eerder as dogters sal die donker figure waardeer: Igor wat deur die begraafplase sluip om parte bymekaar te maar sodat Hans Strydom gebou kan word, die rooi drakie, geeste en jakkalse wat wonder \u201choe sal \u2018n ou stukkie MENSvleis proe \u2026\u201d en Anna Piranha met haar skerp tande, beslis lekker bangmaak kos vir seuns.<strong>Dale Blankenaar</strong> se illustrasies is nommerpas en ek moet erken, die kombinasie van Francois se rymelary en Dale se skets van Mollie Monster (byvoorbeeld) was vir my lekker grillerig. Die tempo van \u201cRikus Riller is \u2018n griller\u201d het ek baie  geniet en ek kan net dink dis \u2018n rympie wat in jong lesers se koppe sal bly maal. Dis mos lekker om te \u201crrrrr\u201d. Ek moes hard aan myself werk om te besluit vir watter ouderdom ek die boek sou aanbeveel. Ek het ook nie gedink dis \u2018n boek wat geskik is om te lees as \u2018n slaaptyd storie nie. <em>Die Land verby Donker</em> is \u2018n ordentlike grillerige rympie  boek en in my verbeelding kan ek net sien hoe lesers ril en gril en lag oor die rympies.                 11/1/2013 5:55:18 AM\r                            11/1/2013 5:55:18 AM\r

Natuurlik gaan Argon, die blaffende konyn en Edison, die robot ook saam. Professor Igtus is die hoof van die akwarium en dit word gou duidelik dat hy bekommerd is oor iets belangrik. Sy gebruik van woorde wat met tye groter, skuins of donker gedruk is werk baie goed, ek kon sommer sien hoe waai die konyn se stertjie, hoe byt Bennie op sy tande wanneer sy sussie  hom irriteer, en as Professor Fungus se eksperiment soos gewoonlik \u201cskouspelagtig ontplof\u201d kan ek amper \u2018hoor\u2019 en \u2018sien\u2019 hoe die hele gedoente plaasvind.En <strong>Johann Strauss</strong> se illustrasies stel nie teleur nie. Wanneer Professor Igtus sy toespraak maak, lyk die klompie dood verveeld in die gehoor, Professor Fungus se groen haarpunte wat die toeskouer agter hom se neus kielie, Bennie wat wydmond gaap, Jenny met haar MP-3 speler se oorfone in haar ore \u2026 die toppunt van verveling! En op bladsy 29 steek Jenny haar tong uit vir haar boetie wat \u2018n tipiese terggees is. Daar is \u2018n goeie aanvoeling tussen outeur en kunstenaar. Dit is duidelik beide het \u2018n aanklank met hedendaagse kinders.En by Einstein se Snor! Daar is weer \u2018n wonderlike, eenvoudige en veilige eksperiment aan die einde van die verhaal wat lesers van 9 jaar en ouer sal fassineer.<em>Professor Fungus en die mensvreter-piranhas</em> is vol inligting, pret en humor, \u2018n goeie byvoeging vir enige biblioteek.                11/1/2013 6:07:21 AM\r                            11/1/2013 6:07:21 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews "The Day of the Dreader"\xa9 2016

<img alt="dragon underwater" src="http://www.renlearn.co.uk/wp-content/uploads/2012/05/The_Day_of_the_Dreader.jpg"/><strong>Hiccup Horrendous Haddock the Third</strong> is one of the finest heroes to come out of the twenty-first century, even though he doesn\u2019t <em>look</em> like a hero.Rather scrawny and useless, Hiccup is the polar opposite to his Viking family who are fierce and strong, but lacking in grey matter and simple in their decisions.  Hiccup uses his brain more than the villagers do and is the only boy on the island who can speak to the dragons in '<em>Dragonese</em>'.This story takes place when Toothless, Hiccup's pet, is still little and in the process of learning how to behave around humans.  A Dreader (huge sea dragon) has trapped the village on the island of Berk and food is running out fast.  Toothless is playing up because he\u2019s hungry, but boredom sees him chewing on the chief\u2019s belt and burning the furniture.Stoick the Vast (Hiccup\u2019s Dad and also the chief) suggests that the villagers take a ship out to confront the sea dragon, seeking to destroy it, but at the very least, hoping to scare the creature away forever.Hiccup suggests that perhaps <em>communication</em> would be the best way to ask the Dreader to leave, but this idea is far too civilised and not taken to well by the community.Toothless, meanwhile, remembers that he has three eggs stored away, yet, as he unearths them, the dragon is surprised to find that they DON\u2019T BEHAVE like eggs at all!Hiccup must be the unlikely hero, saving the village from starvation and a dangerous dragon.  He must also save his house from being destroyed, before his father sees it and banishes his dragon, while safely removing the three eggs from Toothless.Close attention is paid to the characteristics of the Vikings, their reactions to the situation amusing as they make their choices.  Hiccup is a wonderful role model for children and Toothless is intriguing to watch as he falls into the juxtaposition of good and bad in an attempt to behave.As usual this tale by <strong>Cressida Cowell</strong> is hilariously funny.Cleverly written and accompanied by the author\u2019s quirky drawings, this book is another brilliant addition to the <strong>\u201cHow to Train Your Dragon\u201d</strong> series, a quick read that is perfect for the whole family.To Buy the book: http://www.amazon.co.uk/The-Dreader-Train-Your-Dragon/dp/1444907735To visit the website: http://www.howtotrainyourdragonbooks.com/                11/4/2013 6:59:22 AM\r                            11/4/2013 6:59:22 AM\r

<em>Om Helena te hoor</em> sal byval vind by lesers tussen 12 \u2013 15 wat nog hard moet werk om hul plek in die lewe te vind. Dit is \u2018n menslike verhaal van \u2018n familie met alledaagse uitdagings en van ouers wat wil help om hul kinders se drome te bewaarheid. En dit is juis die probleem wat skrywer <strong>Carolyn Morton</strong> aanpak. In die elke dag se geroesemoes van huis toe werk toe deur ouers om \u2018n bestaan te maak, verloor \u2018n familie tred van mekaar. Pa en ma kom saans doodmoeg en afgestomp tuis, krag en energie heeltemal opgebruik. Aandete voorberei en opvang met die kinders se skoolgebeure word amper meganies uitgevoer. Opvang met mekaar bestaan amper nie meer nie. Helena sukkel om haarself te vind tussen al die harwar tuis en haar eie ontlokte potensiaal. Talentvolle boetie Henk aan die ander kant, het sy visier gerig op \u2018n totaal ander beroep in teenstelling met die keuse wat sy ouers as vanselfsprekend vir hom aanvaar. Met tye het die roman vir my bietjie stadig beweeg, maar die feit dat die materiaal so relevant is met vandag se vinnige lewe en die uitdagings wat aan families gestel word, het dit nie te erg gepla nie. Die tragiese ongesproke wense van die ouers (huis kort \u2018n laag verf, \u2018n bedding met blommetjies by die agterdeur, \u2018n ordentlike haarsny) was kennelik van die opofferings wat ouers maak om aan hul kinders \u2018n wegspringplek in die lewe te besorg. Daarenteen is die begeerte van die kinders om in die toekoms aan hul ouers te kan teruggee, ewe relatief.Veral musiekliefhebbers sal aanklank vind met <em>Om Helena te hoor</em>. Madam Pandora (waarom altyd die uitheemse name vir musiek onderwysers?) se aanmoediging en leiding om Helena en haar boetie voor te berei vir die komende musiek kompetisie is uiteindelik van groot hulp vir beide jongmense om lewensbesluite te maak.Die roman getuig van uithouvermo\xeb, vriendskap en waagmoed. Dit is <strong>Carolyn Morton</strong> se eerste publikasie. I didn\u2019t like it when the children were teasing her and hurting her feelings.I would recommend this book to girls of 8 or 9 years old. I am 8 years old and loved reading this book.  These stories are written for girls rather than boys.I wish this book would become a reader in our classroom so others can learn not to be mean and be strong. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Jay Heale Reviews Adventure Trails in Kirstenbosch\xa9 2016

Congratulations to one of the few authors who can write verse that has rhyme, rhythm and is not \u2018forced\u2019. This picture book is about an African Grey parrot (with a scarlet tail) who is friends with a bee busy pollinating flowers. We see brightly coloured birds in an aerial dynamics display, and a bit of info about bird camouflage. But there isn\u2019t really any story \u2013 just enjoyable verse and cheerful pictures. The map shows that the African Grey comes from West Africa including the Congo river basin. Are the flowers depicted genuine to that region? The bee is certainly more cartoon than reality. It seems to me like an opportunity missed for both author and illustrator to tell us more about birdlife in a real equatorial Africa. But it is fun. And there are some super stickers. No parents.  No rules.  Until the inevitable happens... Demi is dead.  The golden girl, the birthday girl, the girlfriend and the best friend, Demi is the one person that had the most to live for.  A party animal who plays a little too hard with her life, Demi pushes the freedom she is given to its limits.  But does she deserve to die?Travelling backwards in time, the role of each youngster is unfurled, like fingers within a clenched fist.Ashley, the awkward school friend, and 'V', Demi's oldest and best-friend, have grown up together, co-existing in the same community.  Damian, Demi\u2019s boyfriend, is slightly older and not so interested - these are Demi\u2019s friends, not his.  James is the bad guy and Siya, his friend, is the hook-up that everyone is trying to get Ashley together with, the \u2018balancer\u2019 to holds the group in an even number.These six profiles create the puzzle-pieces that complete the image of intrigue, each character a story within themselves. Led on a voyeuristic journey into their psyches, the reader discovers the issues and fantasies that drives them.Almost painfully, <strong>'Sharp Edges'</strong> is a reminder of when our own parents could do nothing right and is a cutting warning to today's youth.<strong>S.A. Partridge</strong> seems to scoff at the self-absorbed thinking of teens who make themselves the victims of their own circumstances, her words caustic and often regretful.  Or perhaps that is our own opinion as we walk again through this right of passage?In intense detail, the group's mistakes are glaring in their need for acceptance and it is a story that should be shared and spoken about, although I have to wonder how many boys will lift a book with the cover of a dancing girl upon it.<strong>Sharp Edges</strong> is a quick and seamless read that profoundly touches the inner layers of the readers soul and lingers on the edge of ones consciousness for weeks after.http://www.sapartridge.co.za/                11/25/2013 7:54:57 AM\r                            11/25/2013 7:54:57 AM\r

For the final chapters make sure that <em>nothing</em> and <em>no-one</em> can disturb you, for this ending deserves all the respect you can give it. <strong>'How to seize a Dragon's Jewel'</strong> is the ultimate buildup of anticipation and is thrilling to the last page.                12/2/2013 7:58:06 AM\r                            12/2/2013 7:58:06 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Amy Baxter Reviews 'Tales From The Marula Tree'  \xa9 2016

<img alt="Marula tree" src="http://images.kalahari.net/img/2011/11/04/32674239_0_Img2.jpg"/>\u201cTales From The Marula Tree\u201d in hardcover, comes with fifteen stories of how the bushveld animals came to be as they are.The baboons are settling in for the night at the top of a Marula Tree.  The younger members of the troop are listening to stories of their environment by the wise Elders, who speak about \u2018How the Hippos Dance\u2019, \u2018The Trees are Listening\u2019 and \u2018The Wild Dogs and the Python\u2019 just to name a few.\u201cThe Hippo Dance\u201d is about a family of hippos who want to learn to dance.  Not the lightest on their feet, the family leaves their first class feeling despondent, but determined to try again.  After a second lesson failure, they see a log dancing in the river, and realising that they will be lighter in the water, they dive in to dance.  I will always laugh at the memory of dancing hippos beneath the surface.The next story we enjoyed was \u201cThe Wild dogs and the Python\u201d about how the greedy Python tricks the Wild Dog into letting him guard their meal, while the Wild dog fetches his family to eat.    When they return, the Wild Dog sees that the Python has eaten his meal and has made him look silly in front of the pack.The Wild Dog grabs hold of the snake in anger and the Python wraps himself onto a tree.  After a while, the skin comes off the snake and the dogs leave the python with a long tongue that sticks out.  That is why the snake has such a long tongue!Each story is humorous, aimed specifically at children and making it delightful to read.My eight year old daughter struggled to see the magic and at first, didn\u2019t want to believe it was folklore, although she eventually read it on her own.  My godson, who is five, was totally mesmerised and I look forward to our next trip to the game reserve together.  There we can find the hippos and laugh together that they are dancing underwater.The artwork is charming and completes so much of the story.   The pictures are clever and expressive.  A beautiful touch to African stories.This book is a wonderful book to read together and at just the right length for a bedtime story \u2013 you can even do two stories as a treat \u2013 it is easy and enjoyable reading.I would definitely recommend this book to young children living overseas or buying it as a bookshelf staple. There are 176 beautifully illustrated pages covered in vibrant colours and exciting graphics.The humour of Angry Birds is carried over in the guide with a Q and A type interview of all the Birds with questions like: "What is the best thing about living on Piggy island?" And my favourite "What makes you angry?" I have always wondered why they are so Angry with the poor Piggies. So if you are an adult and don't understand the hype and why your children want everything from cereal to socks covered in those colourful Angry Bird pictures, it might be a good thing to read through the guide with them. You might even appreciate the humour.Let\u2019s talk about who this book will actually be bought for, the kids. Children of all ages can enjoy various activities as the book takes you through the worlds of 3 of the games, Angry Birds, Angry Birds Seasons and Angry Birds Space. The different activities range from fun like Which Bird are you?, Amaze-in and an Angry Bird Quiz (with answers in the back.)Then almost every page has a mini quiz called Hoggy Hat Spotter where you have to look for Pigs on the page wearing an odd hat and tick them off on a checklist on the page. Both Heroes (The Birds) and Villains (The Pigs) are 'interviewed' and detailed information is revealed on all the characters. Although this is not a step by step definitive guide of the game, a lot of hints are given that could help on certain of the game's levels.I can definitely recommend <em>The World of Angry Birds, Official Guide</em> to young and old and it would make a great gift for a kid who is a fan of the franchise.Happy Piggy hunting!                12/9/2013 7:03:31 AM\r                            12/9/2013 7:05:24 AM\r

En daar in sy slaapkamer skop sy verbeelding in en neem hom op \u2018n avontuurlustige reis na die land van die wildekanisse waar hy as koning gekroon word.Na \u2018n tydjie waar hy lekker saam met die wildekanisse speel, word hy verveeld en seker ook \u2018n bietjie honger, en besluit om terug huis toe te vaar waar hy sy aandete in sy kamer vind.Hiedie boek is \u2018n 50-jarige herdenkingsuitgawe van die oorpronklike Engelse boek deur <strong>Maurice Sendak</strong> en is vertaal in Afrikaans deur <strong>Leo van der Westhuijzen</strong>. Die illustrasies is kunstig en groot genoeg om bespreking met kindertjies uit te lok. Daar is ook die geleentheid om figuurlike uitdrukkings soos \u201cOns het jou lief genoeg om jou heel op te vreet\u201d te bespreek. Na my mening kan van die tekeninge van die wildekanisse \u2018n bietjie \u2018scary\u2019 vir sensitiewe kleintjies wees.Die sukses van hierdie storieboek sal sterk afhang van die interaksie en betrokkenheid van die voorleser van die storie met die kind.(Hierdie ikoniese werk was die wenner van die 1964 Caldecott-medalje vir die mees vooraanstaande prenteboek van die jaar en gryp al dekades lank kinders en grootmense se verbeelding aan. Dit is steeds een van die mees geliefde prenteboeke van alle tye ter w\xeareld.) [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU's Madelein du Toit reviews Bear Adventure\xa9 2016

TRACKS is an organisation with a passion for protecting the world\u2019s rarest animals and keeping them in their own environment. This fact alone spells adventure and action! Young Amazon and her 14-year old cousin Fraser are members of the group and have by now, picked up good experience of survival in the wild.This time around, the mission is personal. Amazon\u2019s parents have been lost in a tragic plane crash presumably in the thickly forested mountains of West Canada. A small party (including her uncle Hal Hunt who is in charge of TRACKS) is set up in the region to search for her missing parents.The brutal wilderness does not take kindly to human intruders and what follows is an amazing tale of the urgent need to find the survivors of the plane crash versus the passion of the group to protect the wild. When a bear notices a human smell, he sets out to revenge the killing of his mother when he was just a little cub. And so follows an intriguing tale of the hunter becoming the hunted, a mother bear and her cub searching for food and a search party desperately looking for a crashed plane and hopefully, survivors.<em>Bear Adventure</em> is a good read - it really picks up speed early on in the story and I found it hard to put down. The extensive travelling and wild-life research of writer <strong>Anthony McGowan</strong> is well-known and throughout the story his lifelong passion with the wild is obvious.  There is much to learn in this book and I thoroughly enjoyed the confrontation between the bear and the wolves. The strategy and cunning of the pack kept me glued to each page and I sensed it was not going to end well, but for who? The wolves or the bear? Riveting stuff.Parents and young adults alike will enjoy <em>Bear adventure</em>. (<strong>Anthony McGowan</strong> is a multi-award-winning author of books for adults, teenagers and younger children. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Puku reviews the ELRU Seed Series book, 'Ezintabeni/ In The Mountains/ In Die Berge'\xa9 2016

<img alt="Book Cover: Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge" src="https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/-U8PMvAbXFrs/V5B7BI-rOlI/AAAAAAAABLI/1iNWY-OvVbsq22GVtjTzhL_bgGPxhAoigCL0B/w346-h195/20160720_123414.jpg"/><strong>Written in three different languages, Zulu, English and Afrikaans, <em>Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge</em> is a glorious picture book aimed especially at South African children.</strong>In celebration of the South African landscape, this is the story of a local family who travel up into the <strong>Cederberg Mountains</strong> in the Western Cape to go camping. At the beginning of their journey, the photographs show wet roads and misty mountains and the first page reads:"<em>Ngemini usapho lwam olwalusiya ngayo ezintabeni luza kudlula <strong>kwiPakhuis Pass</strong> kwakukho isichotho nenkungu</em>.""<em>There was heavy rain and mist the day our family drove up the <strong>Pakhuis Pass</strong> into the mountains</em>.""<em>Daar was swaar re\xebn en mis die dag toe ons gesin oor die <strong>Pakhuispas</strong> die berge in gery het</em>."Exploring natural rock formations when they arrive at their destination, the family find caves, animal skeletons and wonderful creatures living in this diverse mountain ecosystem (all a part of the school curriculum.)<img alt="Photo illustration: Children amongst the reeds, Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge" src="https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/-CkGN0ITsOP8/V49JPFzzrwI/AAAAAAAABI4/xDTskBeRV_geoHeP31n4R-0rMGwyCkBvw/w346-h195/20160610_145346.jpg"/> A photograph of the children standing amongst giant <strong>reeds</strong> is an opportunity for discussion on the flora and fauna of the area, leading to an educational information supplement at the back of the book which is most useful for teachers and parents.  Details regarding the name of the plants and a description of different species, allows children, not only to read the book and recognise what reeds are, but also to begin identifying those that may grow in their own environments.  The choice of home-language names and words aids this process tenfold.Readers follow the family as they erect their tent and prepare for nightfall; the photographs of bush fires and kids with torches, recreating the images that South Africans are so deeply familiar with and so fiercely passionate about.The next day, together with the family, the trip continues, taking readers for a walk on the <strong>Sevilla Rock Art Trail</strong>, following painted signs and beacons of piled stones to see the cave paintings.  Art, geology and history meld into an unforgettable experience, all presented in written form in a way that allows every learner the chance to be a part of it. <img alt="Photo: Ewan reads Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge" src="https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/-HiI6BQsRc_E/V49KF_ndS4I/AAAAAAAABI8/2P_i3mhqAPICoNWA6xGZ5qgRHIfA2Y3vA/w346-h195/20160610_145252.jpg"/>As twelve-year-old Ewan says, "<em>The pictures are nice because you can actually feel like you are in that moment where they were</em>."When presented with a pile of books, twelve year old Ewan was immediately drawn to <em>Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge</em>. He says:\u201c<em>This is a cool book, it\u2019s really quite nice.  I liked the part where the children told each other what they thought the rocks looked like, and they said that they could see a pig, a human face and maybe a dassie. And then, when they went up the mountain, they saw the paintings and other stuff... and that was cool</em>."As the family in the story discover the famous South African <strong>Protea</strong> and stumble upon a truly African waterfall, the journey comes to an end. The reader is left strangely bereft and reluctant to close the book, for they've now been there, hearing the sounds of three languages as they went.This is a picture book that speaks to the eyes, ears, soul and heart of every South African. <em>Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge</em> is like the story of coming home.<img alt="Photo: Ewan is transported by the story in the picture book Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge" src="https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/-4qBJJdpd0ZI/V49MFeAW3UI/AAAAAAAABKg/UgYoPR4fDu4hIjq8TrrzIGVUpQeoNGvfA/w346-h615/20160610_145618.jpg"/><img alt="Photo: Ewan enjoys local picture book Ezintabeni-In The Mountains-In Die Berge " src="https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/-4ItRL3zfEaE/V49LLMF_nvI/AAAAAAAABJ0/ityBq_Xo8IgumHCxJvyro5C2Gwqc2GtYg/w346-h615/20160610_145600.jpg"/><img alt="Logo: ELRU - Early Learning Resource Unit" src="http://www.best.za.com/img/elru.png"/><strong>To find out more, please contact ELRU:</strong><ul><li><strong>Email</strong>: <em>info@elru.co.za</em></li><li><strong>Telephone</strong>: <em>021 762 7500</em></li><li><strong>Website:</strong> www.elru.co.za</li></ul>                7/21/2016 9:38:41 AM\r                            7/21/2016 11:19:38 AM\r

\u2018n Towerkissie met die wonderlikste inhoud: \u2018n spesiale towerkaart van die Geheime Koninkryk, \u2018n silwer horinkie wat jou in staat stel om met diere te praat, \u2018n glinsterende kristal wat die weer kan beheer, \u2018n p\xearel wat jou onsigbaar maak en \u2018n ys-uurglas wat tyd kan laat stilstaan. Dit is die inleiding vir \u2018n reuse avontuur wat enige 7 jarige leser vasgenael behoort te hou. Skrywer <strong>Rosie Banks</strong> se <em>Geheime Koninkryk</em> reeks is sekerlik \u2018n gunsteling by veral dogters wat hulle kan inleef in die betowerende w\xeareld van koning Kieliebaard, feetjies en Sneeubouters. <img alt="Geheime Koninkryk Towerberg" src="http://www.lapa.co.za/zpimages/thumb/173/276/products_orig/products_2012/geheime_koninkryk_5_towerberg.jpg"/>Die aaklige koningin Gorina kom met allerhande slinkse planne vorendag om haar broer se koninkryk oor te neem. Wanneer arme koning Kieliebaard nie meer weet watter kant toe nie, gebruik hy die towerkissie om vir Janie, Bianka en Tamsin in te roep vir hulp. Die maats help baie graag en met die hulp van hul feetjiemaat, Trixi, beleef hulle allerhande avonture in hulle stryd teen koningin Gorina.Skynbaar het koningin Gorina geen end aan haar pogings om die lewe vir die inwoners van die Geheime Koninkryk te versuur nie. Kan die maats help om die sprankelstof te red sodat die koninkryk se towerkrag vir nog \u2018n jaar herlaai kan word? En as die goor Gorina begin om die arme Sneeubouters in ysstandbeelde te verander moet Trixi inspring en help \u201com die Stormkabouters \u2018n les te leer wat hulle nie gou sal vergeet nie.\u201d<em>Skitterstrand</em> en <em>Towerberg</em> is die nuutste publikasies in hierdie reeks. Sjarmante stories vir beginner lesers met die allerfynste illustrasies van fee, tiaras en kabouters in \u2018n towerw\xeareld met sprankelstof en skittersand. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Madelein du Toit resenseer Ons kan!\xa9 2016

Net een dag in die jaar is die blinkbekbessies ryp. Die bos is sommer stil, want al die diertjies smul alreeds aan die bessies. Wrrrumpie, die Fripperwakkies, Knortand en Potifant pak \u2018n fesie uit. Meermoskat het vrede met <em>Babalela</em> wat so laat daar aankom, hy roep hom mos nou al lank al! Die lekker-eet sessie word onderbreek met die bekende geluide van \u2018n stootskraper wat bome omruk en plat stoot. Potifant vererg hom opnuut vir di\xe9 gevaar wat hul geliefde bos alweer bedreig. Die Fripperwakkies se rympraat is so lekker vir kleuters: \u201cPotifant gaan nog self die bos verwoesAlmal moet altyd net hardloop en koes.\u201dEn skrywer <strong>Martie Preller</strong> leer skelmpies wat gebeur as mens nie ore het nie en halstarrig jou  eie kop volg. Potifant wil met alle geweld die gevaar plat trap en almal moet net keer en koes as hy blindelings die bos invaar.Daar is so baie lessies rondom <em>Babalela</em>: die vreugde van vriende h\xea, saamwerk in moeilike tye, helderkop dink oor optrede, maar die grootste les van alles: ons kan enigiets doen as ons hard genoeg glo en wil. Die humor deurgaans maak dit ewe lekker vir die leser om voor te lees en uit te speel! Ek het gehou van die lettertipe wat met tye ekstra groot gedruk is vir beklemtoning. As die gevaar uitroep <em>\u201cLos my  uit!\u201d</em> kan mens die benoudheid en angs sommer hoor in die groot, swaar gedrukte pers letters. <strong>Andries en Erica Maritz</strong> se illustrasies gee lewe aan die diertjies wat saam met Babalela in die bos bly. Ek het veral die Fripperwakkies geniet met hul groot oop bekkies, ek kon my die gekwetter en gefripper voorstel. En as <em>Babalela</em> gaan ondersoek instel na die gevaar, het hy \u2018n moenie-met-my-sukkel-nie gesig. Hy meen besigheid! Die illustrasies was ook nommerpas met die aanmoediging van die storie om ons natuur te bewaar. Ek kan my nie 'n wereld indink sonder 'n bos met <em>Babalela</em> en al sy maatjies nie ...<strong>Martie Preller</strong> kan net voortbou op die sukses van <em>Babalela</em> met haar nuutste uitgawe van <em>\u201cOns kan!\u201d</em> <img alt="Martie Preller" src="http://kakkerlak.co.za/wp-content/uploads/2013/11/Preller-Martie-150x150.jpg"/>(Oor <strong>Martie Preller</strong>: sekerlik een van die mees bekroonde kinderboekskrywers in Afrikaans met 38 publikasies. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Nikki McDiarmid reviews Dogtective William and the Pirates\xa9 2016

<img alt="skull and cross bones" src="http://www.tafelberg.com/Books/Big/tafelberg_covers/childrens/2013/9780624062660.jpg"/><h2>Book 2 - Dogtective William and the Pirates</h2>Mum has won two tickets on a cruise ship to Mauritius.  As Dad can\u2019t get off work Alex will accompany her, yet William is determined to go too and is displaying a great deal of interest in books on pirates.Smuggled on board in Alex\u2019s backpack and stowed away in a linen cupboard that mysteriously has a new lock on the <em>inside</em> of the door, William leaves Cape Town on the cruise liner.  As Table Mountain disappears into the distance, the fun begins\u2026 for Alex anyway.  William is seasick and grumpier than ever.When Alex notices one evening that the galley has been left in darkness, William\u2019s keen sight picks up a shadow on the horizon.  A motor boat pulls up alongside the vessel and men with machine guns begin to climb on board.  Somali Pirates are taking over the ship!  Suddenly afraid, Alex can no longer worry about his dog as William dashes off to investigate. He turns in the opposite direction and goes in search of his Mum and the Captain.As William is no ordinary dog, he must save the passengers on board the cruise liner and find a way to arrest the pirates.  The question is, how is leaving the ship in the pirate's motor boat going to help them do that?  And where is this mysterious Tromelin Island that William is taking them to?Immediately amusing, the second book in the <strong>Dogtective Series</strong> wastes no time in getting the reader back into the action.  Quickly pulled into the story readers discover that William is his familiar grouchy self and still doing things a dog shouldn\u2019t be.Guaranteed to get boys reading and impossible to put down, Mums must know that when they nag about chores, they are interrupting the 'good parts'.Concerned that this tale might seem a little scary for young readers, with the reality of pirates present on the news and a part of adult discussions today, again, the opposite occurred.  Instead, Alex is on a great adventure and in the very capable paws of Dogtective William.  This story is relevant to the dangers of today\u2019s world and opens the doorway for discussion with young enquiring minds, perfect for Grade 4 readers and up.<strong>Christopher, 9 yrs</strong>: <em>\u201cKids should definitely read this book. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Lang Hennning en die Poskoetsrowers\xa9 2016

Ek wonder hoeveel jongmense besef dat hier, op hul voorstoep, in hul eie land, daar ook cowboys en kroeks gelewe het? Manne  wat vir dae aaneen op die rug van \u2018n perd moes sit om van punt A na punt B te kom met pistole in die holsters en haelgewere oor die skouers, knaend op die uitkyk vir swendelaars. Dit is 1850 (of daar rond) en Barney Barnato beheer die diamantvelde in Kimberley. Al wat leef en beef gaan soek \u2018n stukkie rykdom hier. Poskoetse word gebruik om pos, geld, passasiers en wel, amper enigiets van dorp tot dorp te vervoer en is dus \u2018n groot teiken vir struikrowers. Lang Henning en sy vriend, Boet, is op pad Gariep toe om \u2018n gesteelde geweer op te spoor. \u2018n Kreupel perd krap hulle planne deurmekaar en Boet moet die poskoets gebruik om by Kimberley uit te kom. Wat hy en Lang Henning nie weet nie, is dat daar glo \u2018n reuse klomp geld vervoer word na \u2018Mister\u2019 Barnato toe \u2013 die perfekte lokaas vir struikrowers. Wat volg is \u2018n heerlike storie vol intrige en spanning. Elke storie moet \u2018n held h\xea en die rooikop Lang Henning stel nie teleur nie. Hy skiet, skop en dinges, maar het ook \u2018n sagte, redelike kant nes dit superhero\u2019s van sy tyd betaam.Skrywer <strong>Mary Sadler-Altena</strong> gee vir die tienerleser \u2018n kykie in hierdie tyd van sesspan-perdekoetse, struikrowers, padkos wat bestaan het uit biltong en beskuit, uitspanposte waar die perde koud gelei en gevoer moes word vir die volgende dag se reis. Ek het aanvanklik gesukkel om gewoond te raak aan die stadige tempo van die storie. Die mees basiese aktiwiteit het in daardie dae net soveel meer tyd geneem! \u2018n Rit van 10 \u2013 12 myl (jy het reg gelees, MYL) het ongeveer 2 ure geneem op \u2018n stywe draf van jou perd. Sou jou perd boonop kreupel word as hy in iets skerp trap, moes jy STAP terwyl jy die perd lei na jou bestemming waar hy hopelik versorg kon word. Ondenkbaar in ons tyd van selfone, iPads en GPS-stelsels.Die gebruik van \u2018ou Afrikaans\u2019 het met tye gepla aangesien dit nie meer in die volksmond is nie en die humor van  die term \u2018stamboek-gemors\u2019 (byvoorbeeld) gaan dus verlore. Maar as jy lief is vir plaaslike geskiedenis is Die Karoo avonture-reeks met Lang Henning beslis \u2018n opsie. <em>Lang Henning en die Poskoetsrowers</em> is \u2018n lekkerlees verhaal wat mens maklik terugvoer na die manier van leef tydens \u2018n besondere era in Suid-Afrikaanse geskiedenis.                4/13/2015 11:54:39 AM\r                            4/13/2015 11:54:39 AM\r

[<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Madelein du Toit resenseer Duinebesies\xa9 2016

Dit was \u2018n onvergeetlike naweek. Elle vertel opgewonde aan haar ma van haar optrede as rock-violis saam met die kleuters van Kumba Kaya, die oorverdowende waardering van die gehoor op die Musikanto rockterrein en Alex wat  haar voor die skare omdop en hard op die mond soen!En nou die skok stilte oor die krakende satellietfoon wanneer haar ma verduidelik dat Elle se droomvakansie van \u2018n wit Kersfees in Parys saam met Refilwe nie gaan gebeur nie.  Sy moet haar oom Eddie vergesel Namibi\xeb  toe, hy en sy groepie eerstejaarstudente gaan navorsing doen oor spookkrappe. En so verander \u201c\u2026 Elle die Jetsetter na Elle die Woestynghwar in een vinnige oproep.\u201dDit was vir my heerlik om weer deur Elle se lysies te lees. Sy is nou besig met haar graadtieneksamen en Alex met sy finale matriekeksamen. Hy gaan daarna vir drie weke op \u2018n manne-avontuur, maar sy wat Elle is moet nou woestyn toe karring  agter haar oom en sy goggas aan. Hierdie lysie van haar lyk maar vaal.Skrywer <strong>Christien Neser</strong> se nuutste boek <em>Duinebesies</em> vertel verder van die lewens van Elle Kroon en haar maats Refi en Laya. Weereens staan die vriendinne bymekaar deur dik en dun wanneer die aanvanklik goor en vervelige Desembervakansie ontaard in \u2018n opwindende ervaring met allerhande onverwagte kronkels. Hierdie keer is daar is vir my \u2018n groter diepte rondom die verhouding tussen Elle en Alex. Beide jongmense besef hul lewens gaan merkbaar verander wanneer Alex universiteit toe gaan die volgende jaar. En die groot vraag is daar: sal hulle verhouding dit kan deurstaan? Elle sien hoe Alex sy skoolseunskoene ontgroei. As sy hom onverwags sien, skrik sy aanvanklik vir sy rowwe baard en lang hare na sy 4x4 manne-avontuur. Maar gou vind sy hierdie \u2018nuwe\u2019 Alex onweerstaanbaar. Die skrywer slaag daarin om Alex se karakter vas te vang in hierdie oorgangsfase van sy lewe. Hy is nog steeds dol op Elle. Met oorgawe dol op haar. Maar nou op \u2018n meer volwasse manier.Weereens \u2018n lekkerlees van Christien Neser. As jy in ho\xebrskool is sal jy beslis met Elle en haar maats kan identifiseer. Ek persoonlik kan nie wag vir die volgende boek in die reeks nie. <img alt="Christien Neser" src="http://www.nb.co.za/Authors/HomePage/christien-neser-%282%29--2013.jpg"/><strong>Christien Neser</strong> is \u2018n spraakterapeut woonagtig in Bryanston, Johannesburg. Sy s\xea sy hou van tale, skryf en lees. [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">PUKU se Madelein du Toit resenseer Thomas@vrees.net\xa9 2016

Wanneer Thomas per ongeluk \u2018n selfoongesprek tussen sy advokaat-pa en \u2018n privaatspeurder hoor, besef hy hierdie saak wat sy pa tans hanteer is anders.  Daar is \u2018n dringendheid en miskien, wel, \u2018n bietjie vrees in sy pa se stem. Thomas gee nie t\xe9 veel aandag aan die situasie nie, want is hy pas opgerof deur die tweeling boelies van die skool t.s.v. sy pogings om uit hul pad te bly.  Buitendien is die tweeling by die skool nou sy prioriteit, want hulle boelie om die beurt vir Thomas en sy maat, Hannes, en dis nogal uitputtend. En pynlik! Hy wil nie die situasie met enigiemand bespreek nie uit vrees vir weerwraak van die oorgrote misbaksels af. Hy sal moet dink hoe om dit self uit te sorteer.Thomas se meisie, Alex, blom van entoesiasme wanneer die graadneges se Mandela-dag projek rondom die kinders van \u2018n weeshuis uitgevoer moet word. Aanvanklik dink Thomas ook dis \u2018n goeie idee om die kinders te vergesel na die Duitse skool se kermisdag, maar as hy besef dat daar op die dag \u2018n spul hansworse tussen die mense gaan ronddwaal as vermaak, kramp sy maag van vrees. Thomas is doodbang vir hansworse.Wanneer Thomas se pa hul familie se sekuriteit opskerp is hy aanvaklik halsstarrig oor die wegneem van sy selfoon, iPad en rekenaar, maar besef gou dat die misdadigers hul familie teiken. Boonop het die tweeling by die skool aan \u2018n wonderlike plan gedink om Thomas en Hannes weer te treiter en dit gaan al hul pogings tot dusver oortref! Waarom gebeur alles altyd met hom? Maar dan nou weer, hy is gewoond aan \u2018n lewe wat nie as \u2018normaal\u2019 beskryf kan word nie, somtyds dink hy hy\u2019s vliegpapier vir freaks!Skoolboelies is \u2018n probleem wat al hoe meer prominent word en is \u2018n onderwerp waarmee jong lesers van 11+ beslis al sal kan identifiseer. Vir my persoonlik is dit \u2018n gruwelike tendens wat, nes Thomas, sommer my maag laat kramp van pure woede.<em>Thomas@vrees.net</em> is \u2018n goeie veronderstelling van die lewe van hedendaagse tieners in Suid-Afrika. Dit is \u2018n storie van maats wat bymekaar staan deur dik en dun omdat hulle groot waarde heg aan hul vriendskap. Ons almal het vrese in ons lewens wat ons self moet oorkom en Thomas se konfrontasie met die groteske tweeling is \u2018n uitdaging waarvoor hy \u2018n oplossing moet kry om die boelies finaal uit sy en Hannes se lewens te kry.Die lewenslesse in <strong>Carina Diedericks-Hugo</strong> se verhaal is die uitdagings wat tieners <em>vandag</em> beleef. Die pas van die storie is vinnig en kom mooi bymekaar aan die einde. \u2018n Lekker lees!                2/26/2014 8:55:17 AM\r                            2/26/2014 8:55:17 AM\r

<strong>Feit!</strong> Lugvervoer het so gewild geword dat daar tans op enige oomblik van die dag of nag \u2018n halfmiljoen mense deur die lug vlieg!<em>Die Aarde \u2018n Ensiklopedie vir kinders</em> (Human&amp;Rousseau uitgewers) is propvol met sulke feite en kitsfeite wat jou vasgenael hou. Elke afdeling het sy eie kleur sodat mens aan die buitekant van die boek blitsvinnig bruin (vir planeet Aarde) of pers (vir Klimaat en Weer) sal kan identifiseer. Die boek is geoogmerk vir lesers van 8 jaar en ouer wat aangemoedig word om te lees en die basiese feite te soek van die opdragte wat aan hulle gegee word. Dit is verseker vinniger om navorsing op die internet te doen en ek onderskat nie die webvaardighede van lesers van hierdie ouderdom nie, maar ek hou nogal van die feit dat die leser rustig deur die boek sal kan blaai en feite op di\xe9 manier bymekaarmaak.En ek moet dit weer  noem: die fotografie is ongelooflik en indrukwekkend - 'n wenkombinasie saam met feite, kitsfeite en bladsye vol inligting.Hierdie ensiklopedie is veral geskik vir naslaan en tuisstudie doeleindes. <a href="http://www.nb.co.za/Books/16371">Geniet 'n voorskou hier                2/28/2014 7:10:04 AM\r                            2/28/2014 7:10:04 AM\r

Hoe sal \u2018n leser van 4 jaar oud werklik kan verstaan presies hoe groot, hoe hoog of hoe swaar \u2018n dinosourus was? En s\xea nou maar \u2018n Diplodokus het maagpyn gehad, wat dan? [<div class="span8"><p class="lead">Madelein du Toit resenseer Galop: perdestories\xa9 2016

Sug, perdestories \u2026 so het ek aanvanklik gevoel oor hierdie klompie kortverhale wat deur <strong>Fanie Viljoen</strong> saamgestel is. Nadat ek die eerste verhaal <em>Powerhouse Nelson kry \u2018n nuwe baas</em> (<strong>Christien Neser</strong>) gelees het, het ek besef dat hierdie klompie kortverhale anders gaan wees.<em>Galop: perdestories</em> is dertien uitgesoekte stories geskryf deur van Suid-Afrika se beste tienerboekskrywers, en elkeen het sy eie kinkel en kabel wat dit nie sommer net nog 'n klomp stories oor perde maak nie!Eienaarskap van enige dier dra groot verantwoordelikheid. In <em>Tristesse</em> (<strong>Rosa Vermeulen</strong>) sien Alida die potensiaal raak van \u2018n perd wat deur sy eienaar as \u2018n slegte belegging afgeskryf is. Alida is heeltemal bewus van die vosmerrie se prominente heupbene en rugstring en die aaklige saalseer op haar rug. Maar sy sien ook Trish se lang, skoon bene raak wat rats en seker trap soos di\xe9 van \u2018n duikertjie en haar groot, sagte o\xeb wat haar goeie temperament weerspie\xebel. Slegte belegging se voet! Trish het potensiaal wat mens nie sal raaksien as jy net in rand en sent redeneer nie. Zanethemba Lodge moet aanvanklik \u2018n nuwe begin wees vir Vicki en haar loslit ma, die rondtrekkery is nie vir Vicki vreemd nie, eerder net \u2018n irritasie. Want dis hoe haar ma rol, na elke liefdesteleurstelling pak hulle op en begin elders oor. Hierdie tipe lewenswyse maak van Vicki \u2018n eensame, onaangename, stuurse mens, maar wie weet, dalk net kom <em>\u2018n Hand vol wense</em> (<strong>Jaco Jacobs</strong>) hierdie keer vir haar waar.Natuurlik moet daar ook \u2018n spookstorie wees soos <strong>Solet Scheeres</strong> se <em>Die uithourit</em>. Mistig, grillerig en fassinerend. Tagtig kilometer op die rug van \u2018n perd is \u2018n lang pad en baie kan gebeur \u2026<em>Die Seun</em>, wat deur <strong>Annelie Ferreira</strong> vertel word, het my knaend uitgeboul. Die lewensverhaal van \u2018n perd vertel soos vanuit sy eie w\xeareld is swaar gelaai met lewenslesse wat vir \u2018n 11-jarige leser van onskatbare waarde sal wees.As jy met deernis dink aan hawer, perdemis en stalle, gaan jy uiteraard vir <em>Galop</em> baie geniet. En al is perde nie regtig jou ding nie, (soos in my geval), sal jy nog steeds van hierdie boek hou. Ek weet ek het.                3/5/2014 7:20:13 AM\r                            3/5/2014 7:30:02 AM\r
